- [x] 53. Package security hardening (T-041) — **MUST happen (the user 2026-05-29: "we need to do a security task… it needs to happen")** _shipped 2026-05-29, PR #64; gates the v0.1.1 provenance publish_
  - Estimate: M · Depends: 43 (published to npm) · **v0.1.x — timing my call; slot after Task 49 ships + the Task 44 live test**
  - **Why**: the kit is now a published npm package that (a) executes hooks on the user's machine, (b) spawns subprocesses (`claude --print`, `cmk-*` bins), and (c) **auto-extracts conversation content into _committed_ files** — so a leaked secret or poisoned write lands in git. The runtime poison-guard (PG-001..013, NFR-9) screens auto-extract writes, but there's no repo/supply-chain-level security gate. The npm-token-leak incident (2026-05-29, publish) is concrete evidence the surface is real.
  - **Scope decision (2026-05-29)**: do NOT adopt the third-party `mukul975/Anthropic-Cybersecurity-Skills` repo (verified: 754 reference *playbooks* for an agent to *perform* security work — not executable package-security tooling; no dep-scan/SAST/secret-scan implementations; adopting 754 third-party skills is the tool-bloat the project guards against). Build our own focused CI gates instead.

Supersedes local publish (decision-trail preserved). **Replaces** the laptop-`~/.npmrc` token storage that leaked. Requires user to add `NPM_TOKEN` secret + revoke local token (see plan/SECURITY.md).

- [x] 53.5 **Threat-model doc** — `SECURITY.md` at repo root: threat surfaces (hook exec, subprocess spawn, auto-extract→committed-files, memory poisoning), mitigations (poison-guard PG-001..013, `<private>`/`<retain>`, no-silent-network NFR-5, spawn/lock discipline), responsible-disclosure (GitHub private reporting + email), accepted dev-only moderates, publish-integrity + verify-what-you-install. `bugs` URL added to both package.json.

"Gate bites" is proven by the scan jobs running on the PR itself.
  - _Requirements: NFR-5, NFR-6, NFR-9; design §16 (new security-hardening entry); ADR (new — "package security posture")_

- [x] 54. Code-quality + coverage CI (T-042) _shipped 2026-05-30, PRs #75 (coverage) + #78 (SonarCloud)_
  - Estimate: S/M · Depends: 53 · **v0.1.x — the SonarQube-equivalent dimension CodeQL doesn't cover**
  - **Why**: Task 53 covers security (SCA/SAST/secrets) but not code-quality / maintainability / **test coverage** / quality gates — the things the user's team gets from SonarQube. Distinct concern from security; kept out of Task 53 to stay focused.
  - **Decision (2026-05-30): the user chose "Both" — coverage now + SonarCloud.** Shipped: (B) Vitest v8 coverage gate (`@vitest/coverage-v8`, 70% ratchet thresholds, lcov reporter, `coverage` job in `ci.yml`) — PR #75; AND (A) **SonarCloud** CI-based analysis with coverage (`org lh8ppl`, `sonar-project.properties` + `sonarcloud.yml`, `SONAR_TOKEN` secret) — PR #78. SonarCloud **Automatic Analysis disabled 2026-05-30** so the CI-based scan is the sole analyzer (the two are mutually exclusive). Decision-trail: option (C) CodeClimate not pursued.
  - _Requirements: NFR-8 (docs/quality)_

- [ ] 55. Behavioral pattern detection + promotion — "learn how I work," not just facts (T-043)
  - Estimate: M · Depends: 45 (auto-persona) · **v0.2 — The user endorsed 2026-05-29 ("I want this feature… a clean refinement of what we have, so we just do it")**
  - **Why**: the kit captures facts (decisions/preferences/environment) and records *some* working-style as facts (`USER.md`/`HABITS.md`/`SOUL.md`, "from now on…" memories, auto-persona Task 45). This adds the refinement: auto-extract actively **detects recurring behavioral patterns** ("always wants X format", "runs tests before commit", "prefers terse replies") and **promotes** them into `HABITS.md` / the persona, instead of leaving them as scattered one-off facts. A ranking/promotion step on the existing extract→trust→scratchpad pipeline — no new storage model.
  - **Scope boundary**: this is ONLY the clean refinement (detect + promote behavioral patterns as memory). The bigger ECC-style **procedural memory** (turn patterns into actionable reusable *skills/procedures*) is a separate, larger direction — explicitly OUT of scope, evidence-gated to a later call. Don't conflate.
  - **Sketch** (design §16.52): (1) recurrence signal in auto-extract (same canonicalized observation seen N times, or an "always/usually/prefer" cue); (2) promote to `HABITS.md` / user-tier persona with a `pattern_count`/confidence field (numeric refinement of the categorical trust level — the one idea worth borrowing from ECC); (3) surface in the frozen snapshot like other high-trust memory. Composes with Task 45 (shared promotion target), trust hierarchy (§4), review queue (medium-confidence → confirm).
  - **Design input — U-Mem contrastive failure-memory + the self-diagnosis constraint (2026-07-01, [U-Mem note](../docs/research/2026-07-01-umem-autonomous-memory.md), D-251) — THIRD independent source for the error→fix type.** U-Mem (arXiv:2602.22406, NUS) types failure-memory as **Global Procedural** ("the correct workflow/recipe for this class") vs **Local Corrective** ("in context X, don't assume Y, do Z") — adopt that split for the error→fix shape (Global ≈ the `Prevention`/lesson field, Local ≈ the `Root Cause`+`Solution` pair). **The load-bearing constraint (out-of-the-box, applies to ALL of Task 55's capture):** *"you cannot self-diagnose a failure without a correct reference."* U-Mem's evidence shows naïve self-reflection on a wrong trajectory HALLUCINATES the cause — the agent lacks the knowledge to identify its own error (their MemRL baseline extracted "trivial but correct" details that missed the real flaw). **Implication for our auto-extract:** reflecting on a session ALONE (which is what we do) is structurally weak for failure-lessons; the *correct reference* in a single-user kit is usually **the user's correction** ("no, do it this way"). So the highest-value capture signal for a behavioral/error pattern is the user-correction turn — a good-vs-bad contrast, not a solo reflection. Design 55's recurrence/cue detection to WEIGHT user-correction turns as the reference trajectory, not just count restatements. _Composes with the escalate-to-user-capture idea below._
  - **Design input — error→fix as a first-class memory category (2026-06-15, [AWS AgentCore + build-slides note](../docs/research/2026-06-15-aws-agentcore-memory-and-build-slides.md)):** AWS's build-event slides ("What Do We Store: Facts / **Errors** / Research" + a `memories/errors-and-fixes/` folder) and AgentCore's custom-strategy both treat **"we hit error X → the fix was Y" as its own memory category.** The kit captures this today only as a generic `project`/`reference` fact — no error→fix TYPE with a "what was the fix when we last hit this?" retrieval affordance. Same instinct as the ruflo/memclaw dossier below (trajectory + outcome memory), but more concrete. When designing 55, evaluate an `error`/`fix` (or error-shaped `lesson`) type + the auto-extract rule that recognizes error→fix turns. **Caveat:** a new fact TYPE ripples through the enum + trust + routing + persona logic + the taxonomy in 4 files (`write-fact.mjs`, `auto-extract.mjs`, `mcp-server.mjs`, `import-claude-md.mjs`) — design deliberately, don't bolt on. Overlaps Task 66 (a fix is true until the dep changes — temporal). _Provenance: the user's AWS build-event photos + the AgentCore docs._ **SECOND (stronger) source 2026-06-15 ([project-memory predecessor note](../docs/research/2026-06-15-project-memory-skill-predecessor.md)):** the Claude skill the user USED BEFORE building this kit had `bugs.md` as a first-class file with a clean ready-made schema — **Issue / Root Cause / Solution / Prevention** (dated, chronological). Adopt that quadruple as the error→fix shape; the **Prevention** field is the durable cross-project lesson (→ HABITS/LESSONS), the rest is project-scoped. Error→fix is now confirmed by an actually-used tool, not just a slide._
  - [ ] 55.1 Recurrence/cue detection in auto-extract
  - [ ] 55.2 Promotion to HABITS.md / persona with pattern_count + confidence field
  - [ ] 55.3 Snapshot surfacing + review-queue routing for medium-confidence patterns
  - [ ]* 55.4 Tests — recurrence detection; promotion lands in the right tier; medium-confidence routes to review; over-mutation guard
  - _Requirements: US-1/US-5 (the kit's thesis, behavioral slice); design §16.52, §6 (auto-extract), §4 (trust); Task 45_

- [x] 56. Upgrade vitest 2.x → 4.x (+ `@vitest/coverage-v8` in lockstep) — **maintenance; Dependabot PR #71** _verified done 2026-06-03 (D-47/D-33): vitest 4.1.8 shipped; tests run on v4.1.8._
  - Estimate: S/M · **v0.2-era chore; do when convenient (no feature depends on it).** Not a feature — a dev-toolchain major bump.
  - **Context**: Dependabot opened PR #71 bumping `vitest` **2.1.9 → 4.1.7** (a TWO-major jump: 2→3→4). It bumps ONLY `vitest`, leaving `@vitest/coverage-v8` at `^2.1.9` → **version mismatch that breaks the `Coverage` CI job**. Do NOT merge #71 as-is.
  - **What this entails**: (1) bump BOTH `vitest` + `@vitest/coverage-v8` to the matching 4.x in `package.json`; (2) read the vitest 3.0 + 4.0 migration notes for breaking changes (config shape, coverage provider, snapshot format, `environment` API); (3) run the full suite (1262 tests) + `npm run test:coverage` + the 8 validators; fix breakages; (4) confirm the 70% coverage ratchet still computes; (5) close/supersede Dependabot #71. TDD-not-applicable (toolchain); the gate is the existing suite passing on the new major.
  - _Why it's tracked, not auto-merged_: a test-framework two-major bump can silently change test/coverage behavior; it earns a deliberate pass, not a rubber-stamp (the design §16 / Task 53 "let Dependabot PR the dev-only bumps, don't force the major inside a feature task" note).

> Folded into the spine 2026-05-31 from the former `docs/journey/PHASE-3-PLAN.md` per the documentation-governance restructure: a working plan is "what's next," which lives in `tasks.md`, not a separate journey file. **Status: PROPOSED — awaiting explicit go to begin.** Target scenario: a new session where _"2 days ago you said X was a mistake; now you're saying the opposite"_ — Claude knows it, owns it, reconciles. Adds **US-16** (AI-side position consistency) + **FR-31** (capture / recall / reconcile) — see [`requirements.md`](requirements.md). (Numbering note: the pre-fold plan said "US-14/FR-31"; US-14/15 were already taken, so the new story is **US-16**.) Design calls (recommended; revisit at go): positions live as `type: decision` fact files in the project tier; capture by extending the existing auto-extract pass (no new spawn); adopt the minimal §16.18 temporal slice (`shape` + `started_at`/`ended_at`), not the full retrieval classifier.

- [ ] 57. Capture Claude's stated positions as `type: decision` facts (Phase 3 / P3.1) — PROPOSED
  - Estimate: M · Depends: 23 (auto-extract), 25 (conflict-detect) · **Phase 3 go required**
  - Extend the auto-extract subagent prompt with a `POSITION:` candidate pattern (same shape as Task 45's `PERSONA CANDIDATE`): capture durable positions ("I recommend X", "X is a mistake", "don't Y") as `type: decision` fact files, project tier, `write_source: auto-extract` (→ trust medium), with the source-transcript citation + timestamp. `<private>` stripped at capture. Reuses the bi-turn temp file + `writeFact` + trust hierarchy. Name carefully — distinct from MEMORY.md `## Pending Decisions` (open questions for the user), which these are not.
  - [ ]* 57.4 Tests — position capture lands a decision-fact with citation + trust=medium; over-mutation guard
  - **🔬 PRIMARY-SOURCE GEM (deep-read 2026-06-28; D-218).** The decision JOURNAL (`decisions-journal.mjs`, Task 147/156/159, v0.3.3) is shipped, but it's the VIEW — it journals `type:project` facts from the 6 auto-extract triggers + `cmk remember`, NOT a capture of Claude's OWN positions. `auto-extract.mjs:305` auto-DEMOTES assistant-origin lines + has no `POSITION:` pattern → the capture half is genuinely absent. Two transferable findings: (a) **letta** ([`prompts/system_prompts/sleeptime_v2.py`](https://github.com/letta-ai/letta)) — its memory-edit prompt insists "do not write 'today'/'recently', write specific dates, because memory is persisted indefinitely" → a captured POSITION must carry an ABSOLUTE date so the 66/58 reconciliation+digest have a real anchor; (b) **mem0** is a NEGATIVE source ([`configs/prompts.py`](https://github.com/mem0ai/mem0) `USER_MEMORY_EXTRACTION_PROMPT`: "GENERATE FACTS SOLELY BASED ON THE USER'S MESSAGES… YOU WILL BE PENALIZED IF YOU INCLUDE… ASSISTANT MESSAGES") — the industry default REFUSES assistant capture entirely, which VALIDATES our auto-demote hedge AND confirms position-capture-as-decision-type is a genuine differentiator no surveyed product ships. _STATUS: backlog-no-version-yet — gated on an explicit "Phase 3 go" (the trio's product-theme greenlight, never given). Entry-point of the 57→58 trio (59 folded into 66); inert alone._
  - _Requirements: US-16, FR-31; design §6 (auto-extract), §4 (trust); Task 45 precedent_

- [ ] 58. Inject a "recent decisions" digest at SessionStart (Phase 3 / P3.3) — PROPOSED
  - Estimate: S/M · Depends: 57 · **Phase 3 go required**

This is what makes reconciliation possible — the prior position is in front of Claude. Indexing transcripts for search is the **transcript half of Task 51** (the session-rollup half stays deferred per Task 51's own caveat).
  - [ ]* 58.4 Tests — digest surfaces recent decision-facts within budget; composes with the §7.1 caps
  - **🔬 PRIMARY-SOURCE GEM (deep-read 2026-06-28; D-218).** DECISIONS.md is reachable PULL-only today (`search.mjs` `SEARCH_SCOPES.DECISIONS` / `mk_search scope:'decisions'`); it is NOT pushed into the frozen snapshot — `tier-paths.mjs SCRATCHPADS_BY_TIER` excludes it, so a decision that aged out of MEMORY.md's bounded window is invisible at session start until the model thinks to search (the cross-session-blind failure the kit exists to kill). **claude-mem** ([`src/services/context/ObservationCompiler.ts`](https://github.com/thedotmack/claude-mem) `queryObservations`) shows the cheap shape: `ORDER BY created_at_epoch DESC LIMIT`, with `decision` a FIRST-CLASS observation type folded into ONE token-budgeted recency timeline (no dedicated section needed) — interleave-by-recency, not a separate carve-out. So 58's "recent decisions section" might just be a recent-slice of decision-facts in the existing snapshot, with its own byte budget composing with the §7.1 12,275-byte sum. **basic-memory** confirms the negative: its `recent_activity` is PULL-via-MCP-prompt, never auto-injected (the read-past-the-README gap D-217 flagged). _STATUS: backlog-no-version-yet — Phase 3 (hard-depends on Task 57's capture) AND the byte budget is most cheaply co-designed with Task 151's injection rework (v0.4.3). If Phase 3 goes, decide separate-section vs interleave-by-recency (claude-mem's answer) at design time._

- [x] 60. Native-auto-memory coexistence — `cmk disable-native-memory` opt-in (ADR-0011) _shipped 2026-05-31, PR #93_
  - Estimate: S · Depends: 3 (install), 37 (doctor) · **v0.2.0 — user-facing; ADR-0011 accepted 2026-05-31 (Option C default + one-command opt-in to A)**
  - **Why**: Claude Code ships its own native Auto Memory (v2.1.59+, ON by default), which writes machine-local `~/.claude/projects/<slug>/memory/` in the SAME `MEMORY.md + <type>_<slug>.md` shape the kit uses in-repo. With the kit installed, BOTH inject at session start (~25 KB native + ~13 KB kit snapshot) → context bloat. Per ADR-0011 the kit is **additive, not enforcing**: it does NOT touch the user's native setting by default — it informs + offers a one-command opt-out.
  - [x] 60.1 `cmk disable-native-memory` / `cmk enable-native-memory` — `setNativeAutoMemory({projectRoot, enabled})` in [`native-memory.mjs`](../packages/cli/src/native-memory.mjs) writes `autoMemoryEnabled: false|true` into the project's `.claude/settings.json` (committable → travels with `git clone`); idempotent (no-op write reports `unchanged`, file byte-identical); preserves every sibling key; errors WITHOUT clobbering an unparseable file. CLI via `runSetNativeMemory` (injection seams).
  - [x] 60.2 `cmk install` heads-up line — `nativeMemoryInstallNote(projectRoot)` returns the coexistence note + `cmk disable-native-memory` pointer, or `null` once the user has opted out (no nag). Outcome-over-inventory tone.
  - [x] 60.3 `cmk doctor` HC-8 enhanced — reads the project's `autoMemoryEnabled` state (`getNativeAutoMemoryState`): `disabled` → "kit is sole layer"; native ACTIVE + not disabled → surfaces `cmk disable-native-memory` (the both-layers bloat heads-up); records `setting_state` in the NDJSON snapshot. (No new HC — stays HC-1..HC-9.)
  - [x]* 60.4 Tests — `tests/cli-native-memory.test.js` (11): disable/enable write the right key + preserve siblings (over-mutation guard) + idempotent + no-clobber-on-broken-json + state reporting + CLI glue + install-note fires-only-when-relevant. `cli-doctor.test.js` +1: HC-8 reports DISABLED + records `setting_state` (Door 4). Doors 1 (return) + 2 (settings.json state) + 4 (doctor NDJSON).
  - **Docs-in-PR**: README + `docs/CLI.md` + CHANGELOG (new user-facing command).
  - _Requirements: ADR-0011; design §11 (Anthropic coexistence); Task 3 (install), Task 37 (doctor)_

- [x] 61. Inline cross-project promotion — auto-persona fires *now*, not weekly (the "TikTok-age" responsiveness fix) _shipped 2026-05-31, PR #90_
  - Estimate: M · Depends: 23 (auto-extract), 45 (auto-persona) · **v0.2.0 — makes the cross-project differentiator visible in a short trial; the user 2026-05-31: "nobody is going to wait a week, not even a day."**
  - **The gap**: auto-extract captures facts to the **project tier every turn**, but cross-project doctrine is only promoted to the **user tier weekly** (`autoPersona` runs only in `weekly-curate`). So "it knows my preferences in every project" lags up to 7 days — invisible in a short trial, which re-opens the `#2` self-test gap (user tier stays empty) in practice. Decision (2026-05-31): **two layers, not four** —
    - **Layer 1 (new, immediate):** detect cross-project doctrine **at capture time** and promote it **this turn**. Free — rides the auto-extract Haiku call that already fires every turn; no second LLM call, no extra cooldown.
    - **Layer 2 (kept, demoted to janitor):** the existing `autoPersona` consolidation pass stays **weekly** (or lazy-on-read when no cron) for dedup/merge/catch-miss. Nobody waits on it.
  - **Design (reuse, don't reinvent):** auto-extract's Haiku ALSO emits a `PERSONA CANDIDATE | target=<HABITS|LESSONS|USER>.md | section=<…> | confidence=<…> | <text>` line (the exact format `auto-persona.mjs` already parses) for any fact that is cross-project doctrine (working style / tooling habits / architecture preferences — NOT this-project specifics). Route those through `auto-persona`'s existing promote-to-user-tier path (memoryWrite → user scratchpad, auto-supersede on conflict, never overwrite trust:high — D-13 + the 45.4 invariant). Normal `TRUST_X` lines keep routing to the project tier unchanged.
  - [x] 61.1 Extract a shared `promoteCandidatesToUserTier()` helper from `auto-persona.mjs` (the promotion block) so both `autoPersona` (janitor) and `auto-extract` (inline) call ONE promotion path. Export `buildClassifierInstructions` + the `PERSONA_CANDIDATE_RE` parser for reuse.
  - [x] 61.2 `auto-extract` prompt: append the cross-project `PERSONA CANDIDATE` directive (reuse `buildClassifierInstructions`'s body). Parse the persona lines alongside `parseCandidates`.
  - [x] 61.3 Thread `userDir` into `runAutoExtract` + the `cmk-auto-extract` bin (resolve via `tier-paths` / `MEMORY_KIT_USER_DIR`); route persona candidates to the user tier when `userDir` is available (skip gracefully on a fresh machine with no user tier, like `autoPersona` does). _Both bins wired: `packages/cli/bin/cmk-auto-extract.mjs` + the plugin twin `plugin/bin/cmk-auto-extract.mjs`._
  - [x]* 61.4 Tests — a turn with a cross-project preference → the fact lands in the **user tier** (HABITS/LESSONS/USER) **this run**, while project-specific facts still land in project `MEMORY.md`; over-mutation guard (project facts untouched). Persona-only turn still promotes (action=extracted, observation_count 0). No-userDir back-compat. Doors 1 (return: `persona` struct) + 2 (user-tier scratchpad state) + 3 (single Haiku call — `backend.calls === 1`) + 4 (extract.log `persona_promoted`). **Stress 5× (spawn/detached surface).** Plus: inline-promotion failure is isolated from project extraction (try/catch — secondary job never breaks the primary).
  - **Docs-in-PR**: README + CHANGELOG (the cross-project memory now fills in real time, not weekly).
  - _Requirements: US-2 (cross-project continuity); design §16.16 (auto-persona cadence — closes the open cadence question), §6 (auto-extract), §4 (trust); Task 45; ADR-0003 (3-tier)_

- [x] 62. Node-only hook execution — retire the bash dependency (cross-OS parity with Claude Code) _shipped 2026-05-31, PR #91_
  - Estimate: M · Depends: 23, 49 · **v0.2.0 candidate.** Surfaced 2026-05-31 when the user asked *"i need the kit to run on windows/mac/linux like claude code itself"* + the dev box's default `bash.exe` (Docker Desktop's distro) has no `/bin/bash`, spuriously failing ~35 hook-bin tests. The shipping **npm route is already node-only and cross-OS (CI `windows-2022 — install + doctor` passes)**; the remaining bash surfaces are (a) the plugin route's `hooks.json` (`bash "${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/bin/<name>"`) + its extensionless bash wrappers, and (b) the **test harness** (`spawnSync('bash', [stub])`). Goal: zero bash dependency anywhere, so the kit + its tests run on node alone like the `claude` CLI.
  - [x] 62.1 **PRIMARY-SOURCE CHECK (done 2026-05-31).** Anthropic's plugins-reference (<https://code.claude.com/docs/en/plugins-reference>): *"Claude Code provides three variables for referencing paths. All are **substituted inline** anywhere they appear in … **hook commands** …"* → Claude Code expands `${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}` **itself, before the command runs** (NOT shell-dependent). Confirmed by the docs' own MCP example `"command": "node", "args": ["${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/server.js"]`. **Verdict: NOT a rabbit hole.** The plugin `hooks.json` command can become `node "${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/bin/<name>.mjs"` — the substituted `node "C:\…\x.mjs"` runs under any shell (cmd/PowerShell/bash) on any OS, no POSIX shell needed. 62.3 is a one-line-per-hook swap; no node-launcher workaround required. (Record in SOURCES.md.)
  - [x] 62.2 Converted the hook-bin tests (`cli-hooks-scaffold`, `cli-capture-prompt`, `cli-capture-turn`, `cli-inject-context`, `cli-observe-edit`) from `spawnSync('bash', [stub])` to `spawnSync(process.execPath, [mjsBin])` + repointed `BIN_PATH`/`BIN_DIR` at the `.mjs` files. **Proof: full suite green with NO Git Bash on PATH** (was ~35 failing on the broken-bash machine). Also fixed `release-verification.test.js` (asserted the deleted wrappers existed → now asserts the `.mjs` handlers).
  - [x] 62.3 `plugin/hooks/hooks.json` → node form (`node "${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/bin/<name>.mjs"`); retired the 6 extensionless bash wrappers + legacy `auto-extract-memory.sh`; ported `cmk-version-check` to a node `.mjs` stub; `cmk-observe-edit.mjs` absorbed its wrapper's hook-envelope contract (emit `{"continue": true}` first, then the fire-and-forget append — the bash detach was unnecessary under `async: true`). Decision-trail preserved in design §5.1 + settings-hooks.mjs.
  - [x] 62.4 Shebang test now asserts the node shebang on the `.mjs` bins; CHANGELOG `[Unreleased]` ### Changed entry (node-only, no bash, cross-OS). README/INSTALL needed no change — the bash dependency was never a documented Windows prerequisite (only the optional Docker/memsearch Layer 5b mentions bash, where it's available).
  - _Requirements: NFR (cross-OS portability); design §5.1 (hook envelope), §18 (legacy cleanup); ADR-0008-class (cross-platform command discipline)_

## v0.2.0 BLOCKERS — surfaced by the 2026-05-31 live test (must land before the v0.2.0 tag)

Full diagnosis + detailed specs: [`docs/journey/v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md`](../docs/journey/v0.2.0-live-test-findings.md) (history). These task entries are the SPINE record (per DOCUMENTATION-MAP D-19 — a fix isn't real until it's a task here).

- [x] 63. **Rich-capture fix (F1 — the headline).** v0.1.2 routed all captures through `cmk remember` (sanitized but TERSE one-line MEMORY.md bullets) + told scaffolded CLAUDE.md to never hand-write fact files → v0.2.0 captures one-liners where v0.1.1 captured rich doctrine fact files. Restore richness THROUGH the safe path. _shipped 2026-06-01, PR #95_
  - [x] 63.1 `cmk remember` rich mode: `--why`/`--how`/`--title`/`--type`/`--links` → write a **granular fact file** via `writeFact()` ([write-fact.mjs](../packages/cli/src/write-fact.mjs)) THROUGH home-path sanitizer + Poison_Guard + correct schema. - [x] 65. _shipped 2026-06-10, PR #150 (v0.3 lane PR 4; ADR-0015/D-109). **WINNER: sqlite-vec (in the existing index) + Xenova/bge-base-en-v1.5 via optional @huggingface/transformers — R@5 0.941 / paraphrase 1.000** (vs the 0.529/0.300 rung-0b bar; bge-small 0.824/0.900; bge-m3 0.765/0.800 — the giant LOST, ladder ceiling found). Built: [semantic-backend.mjs](../packages/cli/src/semantic-backend.mjs) (content-addressed embedding cache, model-derived dims, sync seam preserved via prepareSemanticBackend); CLI `--mode=semantic|hybrid` + `mk_search` auto-prepare; CMK_DISABLE_SEMANTIC=1 control; embedder optional (~258MB) → Task 46 ships the install opt-in. Deterministic rerank (kw 0.30/temporal 0.40) built + benchmarked: no gain over raw on this corpus → not default (honesty norm). Tests cli-semantic-backend.test.js; live-tested all 3 modes on the dogfooded repo._ **Layer 5b semantic recall — deep research → backend bake-off → build** (the video's "most important" piece; deferred). = **wow #2 (recall with reasoning); reaching it = video parity (D-25).** Post-F1/F2, post-friend-validation (0.3.0). **MemPalace data point (D-70, 2026-06-05, [research note](../docs/research/2026-06-05-mempalace-review.md)):** a third independent vote for **embedded vector, not a server** (it uses pure-Python embedded **ChromaDB**; keep `sqlite-vec` default + Chroma as a possible opt-in `--backend`, never required). **Concrete hybrid-pipeline blueprint to copy:** raw semantic → keyword boost → **temporal-proximity weighting** → optional **LLM rerank**, with **raw-vs-reranked reported separately** (their LongMemEval: 96.6% raw → 98.4% hybrid → ≥99% rerank). Compose the temporal-proximity weighting with Task 66. **Recall is a TIERED LADDER, not flat search** (the video's primary plan, re-verified 2026-06-06 — [source](../docs/sources/simon-scrapes-master-claude-memory.md#primary-source-local--re-verification-2026-06-06); MemPalace agrees via "Drawers"): **Tier 0** in-context (MEMORY.md + today's log, zero cost) → **L1** semantic search (`--top-k 5`) → **L2** expand-to-full-section around the hit → **L3** raw transcript drill, escalate-only-if-needed. Build the ladder, not just the embedder. **CONCRETE RECIPE (D-72, source dive of memsearch + MemPalace — [research note](../docs/research/2026-06-06-recall-deep-dive-memsearch-mempalace.md)):** fuse **sqlite-vec (dense) + FTS5 `bm25()` (sparse) via RRF k=60** (both native to us; replaces §9.3's 0.5/0.5 weighted sum), over-fetch ~3×/top-50, then **keyword-overlap rerank (weight 0.30) + temporal-date boost (weight 0.40)** — pure Python, **~98% R@5 with ZERO API calls** (the LLM cross-encoder rerank adds only the last ~1pp → opt-in flag, off by default). ONNX **bge-m3** = the local/no-API/cross-platform embedder. Reject Milvus (memsearch) + Chroma-server (MemPalace) — same algorithm, our sqlite-vec+FTS5+markdown stack.

- [ ] 95. **Dream-style re-curation — consolidate from RAW transcripts into a REVIEWABLE output, not in-place.** _v0.3; D-62, from the 2026-06-04 Anthropic Dreams primary source ([research note](../docs/research/2026-06-04-anthropic-managed-agents-memory-and-dreams.md))._ Our `weekly-curate`/`daily-distill` mutate in place over *derivatives*. Anthropic's "dream" model is strictly better and unifies four kit tasks: re-curate from the **raw transcripts** (D-44: classify over raw, not degraded), **merge duplicates + resolve contradictions with latest-value** (F-D semantic dedup + Task 66 temporal validity), **surface new cross-session insights** (Task 55 behavioral patterns), producing a **new reviewable output** the user adopts-or-discards (never destroys the input — the D-61 no-loss invariant applied to curation). Supersedes/absorbs the in-place curate. **Concrete operation set (D-73 dive of mem0):** mem0's batched "memory manager" decides **ADD / UPDATE / DELETE / NONE** per fact given *(existing memory + new facts)* via one LLM pass — exactly the framing this re-curation pass wants (UPDATE handles "moved Postgres→SQLite" as a supersede, not a contradicting ADD; DELETE retracts; NONE skips dups). mem0's `DEFAULT_UPDATE_MEMORY_PROMPT` is a ready template. Keep it as a **batched reviewable pass** (not per-write — per-write stays our deterministic canonical-ID dedup, zero-API). **➕ SECOND ready template (Memora Fig. 6, 2026-07-03; [research note](../docs/research/2026-07-03-memora-harmonic-memory-review.md)):** their update-or-add prompt does judge + candidate-pick + **merged-value generation in ONE call** (code: `builder/memory_builder.py::upsert_memory_entry`, similarity candidates at θ=0.80); their App. F sensitivity table (0.6 → 3.4× merges, NO quality gain — over-consolidation measured) is the empirical warning for 95's merge aggressiveness knob. _Relates F-D, Task 55/66/84, D-44, mem0 (D-73), Memora (D-266), weekly-curate.mjs._
  - **🔬 PRIMARY-SOURCE GEM + STATUS (deep-read 2026-06-28; D-218).** Confirmed: 95 is the ENGINE for the whole 66/95/97 + deferred-tails(143/144/147/68) cluster — too big to fold, others fold into IT. The gem is exactly the mem0 `DEFAULT_UPDATE_MEMORY_PROMPT` ADD/UPDATE/DELETE/NONE pass above, paired with **letta**'s detached every-N-turns background job (sleeptime). **The key differentiator the survey confirms: neither mem0 nor letta emits a REVIEWABLE output — they mutate in place. Our no-loss diff (re-curate → reviewable new output, adopt-or-discard) is OURS, no surveyed product ships it.** **Two unresolved forks (why needs-design):** (1) review-gate vs auto-apply-revertible — the D-169 no-ritual tension (a review queue the user must drain is the anti-pattern; "auto-apply + `cmk forget` to revert" is the field-standard posture we already adopted for persona); (2) raw-transcript input is a PRIVACY surface (`context/transcripts/` is gitignored — the re-curation must emit a SANITIZED output only, never leak raw transcript content into a committed file). **Hard-blocked on Task 66** (D-166: 66 before 95 — 95 consumes 66's validity-window engine). _VERDICT: needs-deeper-design; backlog-no-version-yet, sequenced AFTER 66 (v0.4.4) — likely v0.4.5+ once the two forks are grilled._
  - **🔬 SECOND READY-TEMPLATE — U-Mem's Eliminate/Consolidate/Refine/Retain maintenance prompt (2026-07-01, [U-Mem note](../docs/research/2026-07-01-umem-autonomous-memory.md), D-251).** U-Mem's appendix Fig 12 (the "Memory Refinement Expert" prompt) is a second, independently-published template for this exact batched pass — a verified primary-source alternative to mem0's ADD/UPDATE/DELETE/NONE. Its four objectives map onto our re-curation: **Eliminate** (redundancy — highly-similar memories), **Consolidate** (merge a specific into its general form into one robust unit), **Refine** (generalize imprecise phrasing to raise transferability), **Retain** (keep valuable non-redundant items untouched). Two specifics worth stealing at build time: (a) every extracted memory must **state WHEN it applies (a trigger condition)** — U-Mem enforces this in ALL its extraction prompts; adopting it in OUR auto-extract (not just re-curation) would raise fact transferability today; (b) the explicit note *"a retrieved historical memory that was irrelevant this time is not necessarily useless — evaluate by generalizability"* — a guard against over-eager DELETE. Compare mem0's vs U-Mem's prompt at build time and take the better framing (or merge). _Relates the mem0 gem above (the first template), U-Mem note, the deferred F-D semantic-dedup (gap G5 — reworded-restatement dedup), D-251._
  - **🔬 REVISIT-WHEN-BUILDING — memclaw's fingerprint-dedup-of-rejected (deep-read 2026-06-29; D-223).** A clean pattern for the re-curation pass: memclaw's Forge computes a `fp:v1:sha256(goal+domain+top-entities+step-skeleton)` per candidate and keeps a **`forge_rejected_fingerprints` cooloff table** — when the user rejects a proposed merge/insight, its fingerprint is recorded with a 30-day TTL so the SAME proposal isn't re-surfaced next run. For us (single-user, markdown): a local `rejected-fingerprints.json` (or a tombstone-class marker) keyed on the re-curation candidate's content hash, with a TTL — so a reviewable re-curation pass doesn't re-propose a dedup/merge the user already declined. Closes the "the curation keeps suggesting the same thing I said no to" annoyance. _Relates Task 180 (same fingerprint primitive), the tombstone discipline (rejected ≈ a soft-tombstone), D-223._
- [ ] 96. **Compliance scrub + recovery — `redact` a leaked secret/PII from ALL history, + `cmk purge --hard` (ABSORBS Task 130; reframed 2026-06-28, D-218).** _v0.5 (compliance feature, not a core-loop wow — re-laned off the shipped-past v0.3.x); D-62, from the 2026-06-04 Anthropic Memory-Stores primary source._ **⚠️ REFRAMED after the primary-source deep-read (2026-06-28):** the original framing led with "point-in-time recovery" — but that half is **~80% ALREADY SHIPPED via git**: the whole `context/` tier is committed, so `git show <sha>:context/...` recovers any past value of any fact, and `archive/superseded/` + `archive/tombstones/` give prior-value at the app layer (`merge-facts.mjs::moveToSuperseded`, `forget.mjs::moveFactToTombstone`). The primary sources CONFIRM git is the standard answer — **letta** (`memory_repo/git_operations.py` uses real git for point-in-time at any ref) and **basic-memory** (deletes the file, relies on git sync for history) both lean on git. So the recovery half shrinks to at most a thin `cmk recover <id> --as-of <date>` wrapper over `git show` (sugar, low marginal value). **The genuinely-new, genuinely-HARD deliverable is the COMPLIANCE SCRUB** — truly remove a leaked secret/PII from live file + every tombstone/superseded copy + git history, while preserving an audit entry "redacted on DATE for reason." **Why hard:** git ACTIVELY RESISTS history deletion (immutable; a scrub needs `filter-repo`/force-push, which breaks teammates' clones — fighting the kit's "survives `git clone` / team-shareable" niche, D-27). The primary sources show NOBODY solves this cleanly: **mem0**'s only hard-scrub is `reset()` → `DROP TABLE history` (all-or-nothing nuke, no targeted redact); **letta**'s `BlockHistory` CASCADE-deletes whole blocks (coarse, not "redact one secret keep the fact"); basic-memory + letta-git keep everything in git forever. So the scrub-over-a-git-committed-store is a NOVEL, design-hard deliverable — `cmk purge --hard` is its verb. **Done when (design-first):** ☐ the recovery half = at most a `git show` wrapper (don't rebuild what git gives free); ☐ `redact <id> --pattern <secret>` scrubs the span from live + archive copies + replaces it with `[redacted: reason]`, keeps the audit entry; ☐ the git-history-rewrite-vs-portable-clone tension (D-27) is resolved in an ADR BEFORE code (force-push breaks clones — is redact local-only? a documented one-time team operation? a new-orphan-branch?); ☐ `cmk purge --hard` = irreversible, explicit-human-only, NEVER an MCP tool (the §6.5 separate-destructive-path contract). _Relates §6.5, audit-log.mjs, Poison_Guard, Task 70 (the sibling inject-defense), Task 130 (now absorbed), D-218._
  - **➡️ ABSORBS TASK 130 (`cmk purge --hard`).** 130 was the true-deletion verb, explicitly chained to 96 ("ships WITH Task 96") but stale-laned at the shipped-past v0.3.x. It IS the compliance-scrub verb over the versioned store — merged into 96 as a sub-deliverable so the destructive path + its recovery/redact semantics design as one unit. _(Task 130's standalone entry retired into this fold 2026-06-28; D-218.)_
  - Estimate: L (ADR-first on the git-rewrite tension, then build) · Depends: none · _v0.5 — a compliance/governance feature, NOT a core-loop differentiator; re-laned off v0.3.x (shipped-past) to a real future slot. D-218._
- [~] 97. **Dynamic trust — trust scores accumulate over time. FOLDED INTO TASK 151 as sub-task 151.T (2026-06-29, D-228).** **Why folded:** the 7-system code-read (D-228) settled that the evolving-trust field IS the protection mechanism Task 151's demote-not-evict (Move 2) depends on — they're the same machinery (recurrence gates PROMOTION, trust gates PROTECTION-at-cap; the maintainer's two-fields call 2026-06-29). So 97 ships AS 151.T (the `trust_score` field: event-driven `+0.1/−0.15`, floor 0.05, from passive contradiction/supersession/restatement signals — memclaw `_adjust_weights`, index-not-frontmatter placement per D-218). The fuller dynamic-trust scope (ranking integration, decay tuning) rides 151.T or a follow-up. _Original 97 scope (memory-os source-based init + access-aware staleness) preserved below + folded into 151.T's design; D-228._ _v0.3+; D-64, from memory-os ([research note](../docs/research/2026-06-04-memory-os-review.md)); the user 2026-06-05 ("we should also take the trust scores accumulate over time")._ Today trust (high/medium/low) is set ONCE at capture and frozen. memory-os has a **feedback loop**: a fact re-confirmed (restated, acted-on, not contradicted) gains confidence; a fact contradicted or superseded loses it. Make trust a living score: bump on re-confirmation, decay/lower on contradiction (compose with F-D contradiction detection + Task 66 temporal validity + the §19 graduation/inject ranking — higher-trust stays injected longer, lower-trust graduates/ages out first). Concretely: a trust delta on re-capture of an existing fact (dedup hit → confidence++), and a downgrade path on supersede. **memory-os's ACTUAL mechanism (D-73 source dive — [note](../docs/research/2026-06-06-recall-deep-dive-graphiti-mem0-memoryos.md), corrects the README read):** it's NOT a re-confirmation bump — it's **(a) source-based confidence init** (curated/wiki → 0.85, session → 0.70, default → 0.75; i.e. `user-explicit` starts higher than `auto-extract`) **+ (b) `last_accessed_at` tracking → a decay-scanner archives the never-accessed.** So the cheap high-value version for us: bump a `last_accessed` field when `cmk search`/recall surfaces a fact, and make the consolidate/graduate sweep prefer dropping **low-trust AND long-unaccessed** rather than pure 14-day age — **access-aware staleness beats pure-age staleness.** _Relates F-D (contradiction), Task 66 (temporal), §19.3 (importance-aware inject ranks by trust), trust.mjs._
  - **🔬 PRIMARY-SOURCE GEM + STATUS (deep-read 2026-06-28; D-218).** A THIRD mechanism surfaced: **caura-memclaw** (`evolve_service.report_outcome`) does **outcome-scored** trust — a float weight updated by task success/failure with an ASYMMETRIC delta (+0.1 on success / **−0.15 on failure** — "failures propagate faster"), feeding recall ranking directly. So across the survey, trust-over-time has THREE incompatible designs: **re-confirmation-bump** (this task's original read), **source-init + access-decay** (memory-os's actual code), **outcome-scoring** (caura) — different signals, different data types (enum vs float). **That divergence IS why this is needs-design, not build:** pick ONE. **The defensible safe slice (don't churn committed markdown):** track a derived `last_accessed` in the **rebuildable SQLite index, NOT committed frontmatter** (a float that changes every recall = git-diff noise on every session — violates markdown-as-truth's "files are clean, diffs are meaningful"), and feed access-aware-staleness into the curation DROP-order only. caura's outcome-scoring needs an explicit success/failure SIGNAL the kit doesn't have (violates D-169 no-ritual) → reject the full loop, keep only the derived slice. _VERDICT: needs-deeper-design; backlog-no-version-yet. Caveat (honest): this round read caura + memory-os but NOT letta's 4th variant — read it before committing the mechanism._
  - **🔬 REVISIT-WHEN-BUILDING — captain-claw is a working dynamic-trust reference (deep-read 2026-06-28; D-221).** `kstevica/captain-claw`'s `nervous_system.py` (MIT) implements exactly this task's evolving-trust in working code — STRONGER than the caura/memory-os summaries above: each intuition carries `confidence` (0–1) + `importance` (1–10) + `access_count` + `last_accessed` + `validated`, and they MOVE over time — `validate()` bumps confidence +0.2 / importance +1 when the agent confirms an intuition; `record_access()` tracks usage; a `run_decay()` sweep lowers confidence 0.05/day after 7 days un-accessed and DELETES very-low-confidence unvalidated items (capped at 500); **validated items NEVER decay.** This is access-aware + outcome-aware trust as a feedback loop — the exact "trust accumulates over time" Task 97 wants. **The HONEST gap they ALSO have (so we don't think they solved it):** their confidence only moves on MANUAL `validate()` or decay — there's no automatic "agent acted on it and FAILED → drop confidence" wire (the outcome-feedback loop caura attempts). So captain-claw confirms the SHAPE (confidence float + decay + validated-protected) but leaves the same hard part open we flagged: where does the success/failure SIGNAL come from without a user ritual (D-169)? **Revisit at build time** — their `validate()`/`run_decay()`/access-count logic is the cleanest reference for the derived-`last_accessed`-in-the-index slice; the float-in-SQLite-not-markdown placement matches our "don't churn committed frontmatter" call exactly. _Relates Task 179 (their dream loop), D-221._
  - **🔑 KEY UNBLOCK — the "where's the outcome SIGNAL without a user ritual?" gap (flagged above as why this is needs-design) has a working answer: memclaw's 6 PASSIVE signals (deep-read 2026-06-29; D-223).** This task's open hard part is: a confidence score that moves on success/failure needs that signal, but prompting the user for it violates D-169. captain-claw (the note above) confirmed the SHAPE but left this gap open; **caura-memclaw's Forge SOLVES it — infer outcome passively** from contradiction-detected / fact-superseded / repeat-recall / terminal-memory-classification / cross-session-reuse / git-CI (`session_trace.py`). **We already produce signals 1/2/5** (contradiction-queue, `superseded_by`, index access tracking) → a passive confidence delta is reachable with NO prompt. See Task 177's fuller note (the SAME primitive serves both 97's trust-delta and 177's validation gate). _Relates Task 177 (the shared passive-signal unblock), Task 180 (Forge), D-223._

The skip-set is the per-command fix; this task is the structural one: run the whole scaffold smoke with `MEMORY_KIT_USER_DIR` + `CMK_PROJECT_DIR` pointed at a per-test temp dir so even a real mutating command can't touch the host. v0.2.x test-hardening. _Relates D-69, the five-doors "external calls" discipline (a smoke that mutates the host isn't isolated)._

- [x] 100. **`cmk-compress-session` hangs when run manually (no stdin EOF) — the SessionEnd bin blocks on `readFileSync(0)` (v0.2.0 blocker; surfaced by the cut-gate B7 probe; DECISION-LOG 2026-06-06 FIX).** _shipped 2026-06-06, PR #123._ Both twin bins (npm `packages/cli/bin/` + plugin `plugin/bin/`) drain the hook payload via `readFileSync(0, 'utf8')` then discard it (`void`) — the read only closes Claude Code's hook pipe. Run as a real hook, Claude Code pipes the JSON + closes the pipe → instant EOF → returns at once. Run **manually** without redirecting stdin (exactly the B7 probe: `cmk-compress-session | Out-Null` pipes stdout, leaves stdin on the interactive console) → the console never EOFs → the read blocks **before any of the body runs** → the 60s SessionEnd hook ceiling kills it (**exit 124, MEMORY unchanged, 0 graduated events, ZERO stderr**). This masqueraded for days as a graduation/Haiku/lock/memsearch hang — all four theories were wrong because the body never executed (the `void rawInput` made the read look inert). Falsified by reproducing the full SessionEnd pipeline against repo source with per-stage timing = **47ms total, no hang**, and by the installed bin returning instantly with stdin=`/dev/null` vs hanging with a never-EOF pipe. **Fix:** extracted the drain into a testable [`read-hook-stdin.mjs`](../packages/cli/src/read-hook-stdin.mjs) — `readHookStdin({ isTTY })` returns `''` when stdin is an interactive TTY (skips the blocking read) instead of hanging; both twin bins call it with `process.stdin.isTTY`. Cut-gate B7 probe also now feeds stdin (`'{}' | cmk-compress-session`). Unit-tested ([`cli-read-hook-stdin.test.js`](../tests/cli-read-hook-stdin.test.js), 3 cases, Door 1); full suite 1439 green; stress 5/5. **LESSON:** four theories chased the code being READ; the reproduce-with-instrumentation step falsified all of them in one shot and pointed at the wrapper. _Requirements: NFR-5 spirit (a hook bin shouldn't hang the user); design §8.5 (SessionEnd hook ceiling); surfaced by the v0.2.0 cut-gate (B7); relates Task 94.3 (the feature whose probe surfaced it)._
- [x] 101. **Extend the manual-run-stdin-hang fix to ALL hook bins (the rest of the class Task 100 surfaced).** _shipped 2026-06-07, PR #125._ Self-review of Task 100 found that EVERY hook bin shares the identical blocking `readFileSync(0)` — `cmk-capture-prompt` (UserPromptSubmit), `cmk-capture-turn` (Stop), `cmk-inject-context` (SessionStart), `cmk-observe-edit` (PostToolUse), and the plugin-only `cmk-version-check` — so each hangs the same way when run manually without a piped stdin. Only `cmk-compress-session` was fixed in Task 100 (the reported v0.2.0 blocker). **Not bundled into Task 100 because:** the payload-CONSUMING bins (capture-prompt/turn/observe-edit) read+`JSON.parse` stdin BEFORE their dynamic `import` of the src module, so routing them through the dynamically-imported `readHookStdin` helper requires REORDERING 6 production hook bins that fire on every interaction — materially higher blast radius than the blocker, deserving its own focused PR. **Verified safe to extend** (each payload consumer already guards `raw.trim() === '' ? {} : JSON.parse(raw)`, so a TTY → `''` → graceful no-op, not a crash; existing bin tests feed stdin via `input:` so isTTY is false → unchanged production behavior). **Approach:** either (a) STATIC-import the zero-dep `read-hook-stdin.mjs` at each bin top (it's a sibling source file; a corrupt install fails the main import anyway), or (b) reorder to dynamic-import the helper before the stdin read. Apply to both twins per bin; keep the `process.stdin.isTTY` injection. v0.2.x hardening (NOT a v0.2.0 tag blocker — only the SessionEnd bin was). _Relates Task 100, NFR-5 spirit; the twin-bin drift hazard (keep both copies in lockstep)._
- [x] 102. **`cmk lessons promote` / `cmk forget` give an actionable error when fed a scratchpad-bullet id (the `cmk search` id mix-up; cut-gate F-3/F-7 finding 2026-06-06).** _shipped 2026-06-06, PR #124._ `cmk search` surfaces ids for BOTH graduated facts (`context/memory/<type>_<slug>.md`) AND scratchpad bullets (a `- (ID) …` line in `MEMORY.md`/`SOUL.md`/the user-tier persona), but `lessons promote` and `forget` operate on FACTS only — so pasting a bullet id returned a flat, unhelpful `no matching fact for ID` / `no fact with id ID` even though the id is a live bullet right there in the scratchpad. - [x] 103. **Enrich `cmk-auto-extract` so RICH fact files ride the immune Stop-hook path, not the native-vulnerable explicit path (D-74; from the 2026-06-06 native-memory coexistence investigation — [research note](../docs/research/2026-06-06-native-auto-memory-coexistence-investigation.md)).** _shipped 2026-06-07, PR #126._ _v0.2.x._ **The finding:** the entire competitor field (memsearch, claude-mem, claude-remember, Hermes) captures **only via the Stop hook** that auto-summarizes the conversation — **none** expose an agent-invoked "remember this" command, so Claude Code's native Auto Memory has nothing to compete with. The kit ADDED an explicit `cmk remember`/`mk_remember` path on top (our differentiator: rich Why/How fact files) — and that explicit path is the **only** surface native can win. In `cut-gate3` (v2.1.167) the agent saved to native and never called `cmk remember`; the kit's `context/memory/` ended up empty. **BUT** the kit's Stop-hook `cmk-auto-extract` still captured the cross-project persona + terse `MEMORY.md` bullets independently (the wedge is immune by construction). The ONLY thing lost when native wins a turn is the **rich project fact files** — because today auto-extract writes TERSE (`memoryWrite` → bullets) while only the explicit path writes RICH (`writeFact` → Why/How). **The fix:** have `cmk-auto-extract` write rich Why/How fact files (via `writeFact`) for durable project facts — so rich capture rides the **immune** Stop-hook path. Then explicit `cmk remember` becomes a *bonus* and native winning a turn costs nothing. **THE BAR = native-parity-then-better (the user 2026-06-06):** native Auto Memory has CAUGHT UP on rich Why/How fact files — our old F1 "we capture richer" moat is GONE. Side-by-side evidence (2026-06-06): for the same backend-philosophy turn, **native's `user_backend_philosophy.md` synthesized a STRUCTURED breakdown** (Routes / Services / Repositories / Pydantic each explained) **+ a fuller Why/How**, while our one-shot `cmk remember` wrote a single prose paragraph. So the synthesized fact `cmk-auto-extract` produces MUST be **at least as structured/useful as native's**, then beat it. **It's BOTH/AND, not either/or (the user 2026-06-06):** git-portability + provenance + 3-tier **STAY real differentiators** — native is machine-local + ephemeral (~30-day expiry), so it structurally *can't* do them; they are NOT dropped. The correction is narrower: don't pitch the win **solely** on those 3 while the memory itself lags — *"leaning on this 3 are idiotic [as the whole pitch]… this project is supposed to deliver memory, not gimmicks."* So: **keep the differentiators AND make the memory itself native-parity-then-better.** Portability is the delivery truck (the wedge — real value); the cargo (capture + recall quality) ALSO has to be better. **Compose with:** the §6.4 bi-turn temp-file shape, the trust-routing (auto-extract facts at `trust:medium` vs explicit `trust:high`), the poison-guard/home-path sanitization writeFact already enforces, and the load-cap/graduation (§19) so the richer project capture doesn't write-lock. **Not the fix (documented why):** a CLAUDE.md line steering off native is cheap but Anthropic says it "won't reliably hold" (context, not enforced config); a PreToolUse hard-block is the only *forced* redirect but is **REJECTED (the user, 2026-06-06)** — intercepting Claude Code's own tool calls is too invasive/fragile for an intermittent loss of the least-critical tier. _Requirements: F1 rich-capture differentiator (don't lose it when native wins); relates Task 21/23 (auto-extract), Task 63 (rich capture), ADR-0011, Task 60 (`disable-native-memory`), the competitor parity finding._

Sub-structured (D-117): ships as 2 PRs per the Task-108 precedent — **capture is time-sensitive (every uncaptured turn is unbackfillable), search is not**, so 104.1 lands first. Sub-decisions settled: (a) detail = +tool calls/results (compact, capped), NOT thinking (bulky, rarely recall-worthy, privacy-heavier); (b) index = a SEPARATE transcript scope on the existing FTS5+sqlite-vec machinery, reached explicitly (`--scope transcripts`) — never mixed into L1 results (the MemPalace last-resort contract); (c) retention = full history (the differentiator vs native's ~30-day expiry; growth bounded by per-turn caps; a retention knob deferred with a "transcripts dominate repo size" trigger)._
  - [x] 104.1 **Enriched capture**: _shipped 2026-06-10, PR #157 (D-117)._ capture-turn reads the current turn's tool activity from the Stop payload's `transcript_path` (Anthropic's live JSONL — verified a common hook field; reading the CURRENT turn at Stop time is NOT the JSONL-copy crutch the user rejected) via a new pure `turn-tools.mjs` (tail-read, defensive parse — entry types verified against a real 7.8MB session: user/assistant carry message.content blocks of text/thinking/tool_use/tool_result; harness types like queue-operation/attachment are skipped). Appends a compact capped `**Tools:**` block under the assistant transcript entry. Best-effort: missing/unreadable/format-shifted JSONL → no block, never a capture failure.

  - [x] 104.3 Retention documented — _design §19.4.1 (D-118)._ Full history (the differentiator vs native's expiry); growth bounded at the source (the 104.1 caps); the retention knob deferred with the repo-size trigger.

  _Original task statement (pre-sub-structure, preserved):_ **Transcript fidelity for the recall waterfall (the L3 raw tier) — expand the kit's OWN transcript, do NOT copy Anthropic's JSONL (the user 2026-06-06).** _v0.3 recall lane (lands with Task 65)._ **The question it answers:** Anthropic's session JSONL (`~/.claude/projects/<slug>/<id>.jsonl`) IS a complete, line-by-line, verbatim record of the whole session — every user/assistant message, **thinking block, tool call + result** (mem-test3: 281 entries / 1.05 MB) — BUT it is **machine-local, Anthropic-managed, and EXPIRES (~30 days)**, so it is neither portable nor durable. The kit's `context/transcripts/{date}.md` is committed + permanent + our-format, but today stores only the **conversational text** (user prompts + assistant text replies), dropping tool calls / thinking. **The user's directive (2026-06-06):** do **NOT** copy/snapshot Claude's JSONL into our dir — *"that is a crutch i dont think i want or need; we could just expand our transcript mechanism to do the same."* So: **enrich the kit's own transcript** (our format, committed, under our retention control) to be complete-enough to be worth falling back to. **How it's USED (the waterfall — like MemPalace):** the transcript is the **L3 raw tier, read LAST and ONLY as a last resort**, reached via **semantic search**, not loaded at session start — exactly the §19 / Task 65 recall ladder floor (Tier 0 distilled → L1 semantic → L2 expand → **L3 raw transcript**). *"if we go the transcript path we will only read it as last resort and only search there with semantic search, like mempalace did with their waterfall style."* **Open sub-decisions (for the design):** (a) how much detail to keep (text-only vs +tool-calls vs +thinking) vs git-bloat — driven by what RECALL needs at L3, not "back up everything"; (b) the semantic index over the transcript (sqlite-vec/FTS5 per Task 65); (c) whether to keep a bounded window or full history (compose with the rolling-window compression §6). _Relates Task 65 (recall ladder / semantic backend), §19 (the L3 floor), the MemPalace waterfall (D-70/D-72), the verbatim-transcript differentiator native lacks (machine-local + 30-day expiry); driven by Q1 of the 2026-06-06 native-memory investigation._
- [x] 105. **Lazy-roll `now.md` → `today-*.md` on SessionStart, so rolling compression doesn't depend on a clean SessionEnd (cut-gate finding 2026-06-06).** _shipped 2026-06-07, PR #127._ _v0.2.x robustness._ **The finding (mem-test3 / cut-gate2 / cut-gate3):** the `now.md` → `today-{date}.md` roll (Haiku `compressSession`) fires **only at SessionEnd** — and Claude Code only fires SessionEnd on a **clean window-close**, NOT when you start a new chat in the same window. So across cut-gate2 + cut-gate3 (never cleanly closed) `now.md` accumulated ~10 KB / 22 turns spanning multiple sessions and **never rolled**; `today-*.md` + `recent.md` never built; the **Task-86c SessionEnd persona pass + the §6 rolling summary never ran**. Confirmed it **DOES** fire correctly on a clean close (mem-test3: `now.md` 10 KB→0, accurate Haiku `today-*.md`, graduation sweep, `context/sessions/{date}.compress.log` all written at close). **Consequences if a user never cleanly exits:** (a) `now.md` grows **unbounded**; (b) `recent.md` (the SessionStart-injected rolling summary) never builds → recall leans entirely on `MEMORY.md` (works, but the §6 summary is missing); (c) low/medium persona candidates the inline path queued never get the 86c second-grade. **The fix:** in `cmk-inject-context` (SessionStart), **lazy-roll a stale `now.md`** — if `now.md` carries turns from a prior session/day, roll+compress it to `today-*.md` THEN inject — exactly mirroring the daily-distill lazy-on-SessionStart pattern (today→recent) that already works. Keep the SessionEnd path too (both fire; idempotent). **Compose with:** the cooldown (don't double-compress within 120 s), the §19 graduation (the roll's graduation sweep), and the compress.log (one entry per roll). **NB (observability):** `compress.log` lives at `context/sessions/{date}.compress.log` (NOT `.locks/`) — keep it there; it's the per-date compress trail. _Requirements: §6 rolling-window compression must not depend on clean exit; relates Task 86c (SessionEnd persona pass), the daily-distill lazy-on-SessionStart precedent, `cmk-inject-context`, `compress-session.mjs`, `roll.mjs`; surfaced by the v0.2.0 cut-gate (Session 1→2 boundary)._
  - [x] 105.1 `detectStaleness` ([`lazy-compress.mjs`](../packages/cli/src/lazy-compress.mjs)): new `stale-now` verdict — `nowMdHasContent` (now.md `trim() !== ''`, matching `compressSession`'s own emptiness check). Precedence: cron > no-context-dir > **now** > weekly > daily > fresh (now→today is the first pipeline level; the rest cascade on later SessionStarts once now.md drains).
  - [x] 105.2 `runLazyCompress`: dispatch `stale-now` → `compressSession({cooldownMs:0})` (the up-front 120s gate already fired). Logs `delegated_to: compress-session` to `lazy-compress.log`; `compressSession` writes its own per-date `sessions/{date}.compress.log`.
  - [x] 105.3 `cmk-inject-context` ([`inject-context.mjs`](../packages/cli/src/inject-context.mjs)): added `stale-now` to the detached-spawn condition — SessionStart detaches the lazy worker (Haiku roll can't run inline in the 500ms budget). THIS session injects pre-roll state; next session gets the rolled state (the standard lazy tradeoff).

- [x] 106. **Close the `now.md` compress race with the file-rename pattern (§16.27 candidate #1) — surfaced by Task 105 self-review (2026-06-07).** _shipped 2026-06-07, PR #128._ _v0.2.x._ `compressSession` reads `now.md` → ~5–10s Haiku → `truncateSync(now.md, 0)`. A turn appended in that window is dropped from `today-*.md`. **Task 105 promoted this from "benign §16.27 edge case" to the concrete ship-trigger:** its detached SessionStart roll fires while a NEW session is actively appending (vs SessionEnd, where the session is ending), so the race is more likely + opens a minor new loss path (transcript-recoverable, not durable-memory loss; timing usually avoids it). **Fix:** read = atomically `rename(now.md → now.md.compressing-{ts})` → compress the renamed file → unlink it. Atomic on POSIX (rename(2)) + NTFS (MoveFileEx); the new session keeps appending to a freshly-created `now.md` with zero contention. Closes the race for BOTH callers (SessionEnd + SessionStart-lazy). Earns its own PR — touches the shared `compressSession` read/truncate steps + needs a concurrent-append race test. The existing benign-outcome honesty tests ([`cli-task27-checkpoint-fixes.test.js`](../tests/cli-task27-checkpoint-fixes.test.js)) pin the contract, not the impl, so they survive the change. _Relates §16.27, D-78, Task 105, Task 27 (I4), `compress-session.mjs`._
- [x] 107. **Finish the Task 82 scaffold-cruft scrub (the CLAUDE.md block it missed) + make the `.gitignore` version-marker consistent — surfaced by the v0.2.2 live test (2026-06-07; the user: "fix everything").** _shipped 2026-06-07, PR #129._ Task 82 [x] scrubbed kit-internal cruft from `template/**`, but a v0.2.2 live-install of the scaffolded `CLAUDE.md` still showed: (a) *"v0.1.0 is under active development"* (a shipped install shouldn't say this), (b) *"Health checks (HC-1..HC-8)"* (there are **9**), (c) RELATIVE links `[docs/adr/](docs/adr/)` + `[specs/design.md](specs/design.md)` that resolve **inside the user's own repo** (404 — kit-repo paths leaking into the user scaffold), and (d) the `.gitignore` managed-block marker hardcoded `:start v0.1.0` while the (load-bearing, version-injected) CLAUDE.md marker correctly showed the install version — a confusing drift. **Fixes:** `template/CLAUDE.md.template` → version-agnostic framing + drop the HC count + external github URLs instead of relative kit-repo links; `install.mjs` → `gitignoreStartMarker(version)` so the gitignore marker tracks the kit version (the replace-regex already ignored it, so cosmetic-but-now-correct); `template/.gitignore.fragment` → drop the `Task 92` reference; `journey-log.md.template` → version-agnostic build-log link. **NB — finding "context.local not scaffolded" was a FALSE alarm** (my `Get-ChildItem` false-negative; `install.mjs` DOES scaffold `context.local/{machine-paths,overrides}.md`, proven by `cli-install.test.js:123` + the user's direct observation — retracted). Regression-guarded by `template-scaffolding.test.js` (no `v0.1.0`/under-active-dev/HC-count/relative-kit-links in CLAUDE.md; no Task-NN in the fragment) + `cli-install.test.js` (the gitignore marker carries `getKitVersion()`). _Requirements: "worth giving to a friend" polish (D-25/82); user-facing scaffold surface; surfaced by the v0.2.2 cut-gate live run. v0.2.x._

## v0.2.3 — patch lane: cut-gate5 sweep findings (the wedge polish that makes it honest)

> Surfaced by the 2026-06-07 cut-gate5 full live run + CLI sweep. v0.2.2's ★ headline (B9/D1/E1) passed; these are the fixes the sweep — and the user's "no code-word passes; a regular user expects everything automatic" push — surfaced. ALL slated **v0.2.3** (patch: fixes/polish to the wedge, no new differentiator). Lane assigned in [`RELEASE-PLAN.md`](../docs/RELEASE-PLAN.md). Decision trail: D-81 / D-83 / D-84.

- [x] 108. **Unify CLI + MCP over ONE shared memory-op core + RESILIENT structured input + a parity guard (the D-82 task — the v0.2.3 headline).** _✅ SHIPPED 2026-06-08: 108a (PR #130) + 108b (PR #131)._ Fixes **D-81** (explicit `cmk remember` silently corrupts backtick-bearing rich facts — bash command-substitution eats the content before cmk reads argv). Core: extract each memory op (`rememberRich`/`trust`/`forget`/`lessonsPromote`/`queueResolve`/`search`/`get`/`timeline`/`cite`/`recentActivity`) into a pure structured-object-in / result-out function; CLI + MCP become thin adapters. Resilient input: `cmk remember --from-file <fact.json>` + `--json -` (stdin) → `JSON.parse` → the SAME object the MCP tool passes (content never on a shell command line — claude-remember's stdin-from-file + claude-mem's JSON-params, unified). Parity: MCP gains the write/mutate tools, CLI gains `get`/`timeline`/`cite`/`recent-activity`; `validate-cli-mcp-parity.mjs` guard wired into `npm test`. Destructive MCP ops (`forget`/`purge`) require a confirm-token param. **RESEARCH-FIRST** (user directive): read the ACTUAL source of **basic-memory** + **mempalace** (both real dual CLI+MCP) before designing. Carries **ADR-0014** + a design §10/§12 revision (decision-trail-preserved: §10.3 framed MCP retrieval-first; APPEND the write extension). **The MCP path also enables the R2 / D-80 fix (tracked as Task 118):** a tool call isn't a shell command, so the `cd`-compound permission prompt can't arise, and an install-time `mcp__cmk__*` allowlist makes the Claude-mediated path prompt-free. _D-82; D-80/D-81; [ADR-0014](../docs/adr/0014-unify-cli-mcp-shared-core.md); design §10/§12._ (ADR-0014 reserved-future for this task; file written at task-start.)
  - **108 ships as 2 PRs (decided 2026-06-07 — driver is QUALITY, not speed: a tighter two-pass review per PR, and the parity guard can only pass once both surfaces match so it must land last):**
    - [x] **108a** (PR 1) — _✅ shipped 2026-06-07, PR #130._ **108.2** CLI `remember --from-file <json>` / `--json` (stdin) → the **D-81** backtick-corruption fix (rich content read from a file/stdin never touches the shell). - [x] 109. **Fix `cmk register-crons` on Windows (broken since v0.1 — never tested).** _D-83 / F-6._ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08._ Even `--dry-run` failed (exit 2): `command: must not contain double quotes` for both daily-distill + weekly-curate — the builder emitted a schtasks `/TR` value with inner double-quotes that the kit's OWN guard rejected → cron could NEVER register on Windows. **Fix:** the win32 path now execs `schtasks` with an **args array (no `shell:true`)**, so the `/TR` value's inner quotes are delivered verbatim (no cmd.exe re-parse) — the double-quote rejection (self-contradictory) was removed; `buildWindowsSchtasks` returns the argv array (exported + unit-tested). **macOS sibling fixed** in the same pass (the `launchd` plist split kept literal quotes → launchd exec'd a quoted path → ENOENT; now strips the wrapping quotes). **HC-6** needs no change — once the command works, its "Run `cmk register-crons`" advice is correct (it already points at the lazy fallback too). Windows test added via a `platform` test seam on `registerCron`. **Follow-up (D-89):** a node/project path that itself contains a SPACE is the remaining macOS edge (the `launchd` whitespace-split) — needs the registerCron `command:string` → `argv:string[]` refactor; filed as a v0.2.x backlog follow-up (D-89), not a blocker (node/project paths rarely contain spaces). _The user 2026-06-07: "we didn't check the crons since the first version."_
- [x] 110. **`cmk forget` (and every mutation) must auto-propagate — no manual `cmk reindex`.** _F-7._ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08 (D-90)._ `cmk forget <id>` tombstoned the file correctly (→ `archive/tombstones/`) but did NOT reindex, so the forgotten fact still appeared in `cmk search` until the next manual `cmk reindex`. **Fix:** (1) `reindexBoot` now PRUNES orphaned index rows (any `files` row whose source vanished) — since every index reader lazy-calls it, the whole deletion class (forget / queue-discard / supersede) self-heals on next read; (2) `forget()` reindexes IN-BAND after tombstone+scrub so it's immediate, and both `cmk forget` + `mk_forget` share `forget()`. **Audit done:** `trust` (in-place edit) + `lessons promote` (add) already self-heal via the existing lazy reindex (mtime/sha1 diff); only deletions needed the prune — locked by a real-`overrideTrust` audit test. **inject:** never broken for facts (`injectContext` reads scratchpads, which forget already scrubs). Tests: orphan-prune (+over-mutation +no-false-positive), forget in-band (+graceful no-projectRoot), trust audit-lock. design §6.5 + §9.2.1. **The user 2026-06-07: "users will not run commands; the regular user will want everything to happen automatic."** (NOT "minor / just a stale index" — that framing was itself the bug, D-84.)
- [x] 111. **`cmk persona generate` errors on a real run.** _F-2._ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08 (D-92)._ With its cooldown cleared it failed: `error (compress_failed): HaikuViaAnthropicApi: claude --print did not return within 50000ms`. **Root cause = prompt-overload, not a hang:** `assembleProjectCorpus` joined EVERY tier-P fact + scratchpad into one UNBOUNDED prompt (the SessionEnd path was already 40KB-capped; the `facts` path wasn't), and the 50s timeout was sized for the 60s SessionEnd ceiling even though the CLI command has NO outer ceiling. **Fix:** (1) cap the facts corpus at `PERSONA_CORPUS_BYTES` (60KB, whole-facts-only + a truncation marker); (2) parameterize `autoPersona({timeoutMs})` — SessionEnd keeps 50s (composes with the 60s ceiling per §8.5/D-42), the ceiling-free CLI + weekly callers pass 120s; (3) the CLI surfaces a clear timeout hint (re-run) instead of the raw internal error. **Tests** (the real cooldown-bypassable ones the task asked for already existed asserting actual promotion; added): corpus-cap (input ≤ cap + marker, Door 3 via `onCompress`), timeout default-vs-override, CLI 120s + hint. **Known limitation (documented):** facts past the cap drop in file-iteration order — a value-ordered (trust/recency) accumulation is the follow-up if a large corpus drops doctrine.
- [x] 112. **`cmk weekly-curate` — real verification.** _F-4._ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08 (D-94)._ The sweep only ever saw "skipped (cooldown)" + nothing 7 days old in a same-day project → the 7-day-archive path was never exercised on real input. **Found on investigation:** the UNIT archive path was already well-covered (`cli-weekly-curate.test.js` 34.4 — 14-day fixture, archivedDays:7, archive.md written, OLD deleted/CURRENT preserved, over-mutation guard) AND the cooldown is already overridable (`weeklyCurate({cooldownMs})`). The real F-4 gap was a **mock-only** verification: no test ran the archivist call through the REAL `claude --print`, and the cron-chain smoke only asserted the bin *logged* (hollow on non-aged data). **Fix:** added [`tests/spawn-smoke-weekly-curate.test.js`](../tests/spawn-smoke-weekly-curate.test.js) — a live-Haiku smoke that seeds aged `today-*.md` (>7d) + runs the real `HaikuViaAnthropicApi` (cooldownMs:0, skipRecentRebuild) + asserts the archive ACTUALLY fires (archive.md non-empty, aged rotated, current preserved). **Result: the feature WORKS on real input — no bug** (live round-trip ~48s, green). Closes the D-84 hollow-pass for F-4.
- [x] 113. **`cmk queue review` / `cmk queue conflicts` — real verification.** _F-9._ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08 (D-95)._ The sweep ran them against EMPTY queues (0 pending) — verified only that the walker doesn't crash on nothing, NOT that it promotes/discards/resolves. **Investigation finding (2026-06-08):** the unit RESOLVERS (`resolveReviewQueue` / `resolveConflictQueue`) are ALREADY fully covered on real seeded items + ALL actions + effects (review: promote/discard/skip + queue-drain + audit reasons; conflict: keep-old/keep-new/merge-both→`mergeFacts`/skip + over-mutation). The real F-9 gap is the **interactive CLI wiring** `runQueueReview` / `runQueueConflicts` (subcommands.mjs ~1492/1370): they build a readline prompter over `process.stdin` + use `process.cwd()`, so they're UNtestable → the sweep could only run them on empty queues. **Deliverable:** dep-inject `runQueueReview({projectRoot, prompter, log})` / `runQueueConflicts(...)` (defaults = readline + cwd + console, unchanged for prod) so a test can seed real queued items + drive a real resolution through the CLI path + assert the effects (promoted bullet in MEMORY.md, conflict winner applied, queue drained, output lines). Same shape as Task 112 (sound core, untested command layer). **Shipped:** dep-injected + exported `runQueueReview` / `runQueueConflicts` (defaults = readline + cwd + console, prod unchanged), + 4 CLI-path tests (review promote→MEMORY.md+drain, review discard; conflict keep-old, keep-new). **Verified working — no command-layer bug.** One contract clarified by the tests: conflict resolution MARKS entries resolved (rewrites the `resolution` field for audit; `listConflictQueue` filters `pending`), it does NOT delete them — so the Door-2 assertion is "a 2nd pass finds nothing pending," not "the id is gone."
- [x] 114. **`cmk import-anthropic-memory` — real verification.** _F-13._ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08 (D-97)._ The sweep only ran `--dry-run` with nothing to import (native off). **Found:** the CORE (`importAnthropicMemory`) was already tested on real input (non-dry-run apply with `write_source: imported` + `trust: medium` + dedup, via the `harnessRoot` seam) — so the literal ask existed; the gap was the CLI WRAPPER (`runImportAnthropicMemory`, only ever run `--dry-run`-with-nothing in the sweep). **Fix:** dep-injected + exported the wrapper (`{projectRoot, harnessRoot, log, logError}`; defaults unchanged for prod) + 4 wrapper tests (applied / no-source / dry-run / requires-confirmation). **LIVE-verified** (D-97): seeded a real native `MEMORY.md` at the actual `~/.claude/projects/<slug>/memory/` path + ran `cmk import-anthropic-memory --yes` → "applied 2 proposal(s)", bullets imported into `context/MEMORY.md` with `write_source: imported, trust: medium, source: anthropic-auto-memory`. **Works on real input — no bug.**
- [x] 115. **Transcript temp-file hygiene.** _(minor; cut-gate5 H1.)_ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08 (D-98)._ A `context/transcripts/.extract-*.tmp` got committed by `git add -A` in the portability test. **Fix:** added `context/transcripts/.extract-*.tmp` to [`template/.gitignore.fragment`](../template/.gitignore.fragment) (which `cmk install` applies as the managed `.gitignore` block) — so a crash-orphaned partial never travels with `git clone`. - [x] 116. **Coverage hardening — make "never tested since v0.1" impossible.** _(meta; D-84.)_ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08 (D-99)._ register-crons (109) + the hollow-pass commands (111–114) shipped untested because neither the cut-gate checklist nor the suite exercised them on REAL input. **Done:** (a) added the **★★ real-input rule** to [`cut-gate.md`](../docs/process/cut-gate.md) "How to read this" — a check passes ONLY on real input (cooldown-skip / empty-queue / dry-run-nothing / same-day = `unverified`, re-run for real); (b) the automated REAL-input tests landed in Tasks 112 (weekly-curate live-Haiku archive smoke), 113 (queue CLI on real items), 114 (import on real native MEMORY.md); (c) live-verified 109/110/111/114 (D-96/D-97). The anti-pattern (conflating "didn't crash" with "works") is now caught both by the checklist rule AND the suite tests.
  - [ ] 116.x **Test-isolation hardening (filed from Task 111's stress gate, D-93).** The 5× stress gate surfaced two PRE-EXISTING concurrency flakes — both pass in isolation, fail only under parallel load: (1) `cli-capture-turn` spawn-latency (FIXED in 111 as a detour — `pollFor` 3s→12s); (2) **`cli-persona-portability` Task-72 rollback flake** (`expected 'ORIGINAL B profile' … got 'NEW imported profile'`, with `r.action==='error'` — so the failure DID trigger + rollback ran, but USER.md wasn't restored). **Investigation (2026-06-08, Task 116 start) RULED OUT the cross-contamination hypothesis:** the fixture IS per-test `mkdtempSync` (not a shared path); `reindex` takes an explicit `userDir` (no `process.env`/homedir fallback); vitest's **default file isolation** prevents cross-file `process.env.MEMORY_KIT_USER_DIR` leakage (the file mutates it at lines 237/264 but that can't reach another isolated file); and `applyBundleAtomic`'s logic is deterministic (insertion-order keys → USER.md backed up before `aaa` fails → `rollbackImport` `renameSync`s the backup over the new USER.md). **Actual diagnosis: a RARE Windows-filesystem-under-load timing race in the `renameSync` backup/restore** — same CLASS as the capture-turn spawn-latency flake (only manifests when `npm run stress` runs 5 vitest processes saturating the machine; 5/5 clean on a quiet re-stress). **✅ FIXED:** `rollbackImport`'s restore did `renameSync(bkp, dest)` where `dest` already holds the half-applied NEW content — renaming ONTO an existing file intermittently throws EPERM/EBUSY on Windows under load, and the **fully-silent catch** then left the un-rolled-back NEW file (= the flake). Replaced with `restoreBackup()` using `copyFileSync` (reliable cross-platform overwrite) + a 5× retry for transient locks; backup removed only after a confirmed copy. 14/14 persona-portability green. Real FS-robustness fix, not test-isolation (isolation was already correct).
- [x] 117. **Free-speech intent → action coverage — make the kit INVISIBLE (the D-85 principle).** _D-85; depends on 108._ _✅ shipped 2026-06-08 (D-100)._ **Audit result — every user-expressible memory intent now has a free-speech path:** _capture_ ("remember"/"from now on"/"we decided") → memory-write skill + `mk_remember` (AND automatic via auto-extract); _correct_ ("update memory: X is now Y") → skill; _forget_ ("forget about X") → skill + `mk_forget` (already covered); _**trust ("trust this" / "that's important" / "that's not important / I'm not sure / low priority") → ADDED this task: memory-write skill + `mk_trust`**_ (was the one open gap — D-85 named it); all _automatic_ ops (SessionStart inject, compress, auto-extract, persona-promotion) need no user action. **Only remaining gap = reliable active recall** ("what did we decide about X") — partial today (`mk_search`/`mk_get`/`mk_timeline` exist), reliable always-fires recall is **Task 75 (v0.3)**, out of v0.2.3 scope. **Done:** extended `memory-write/SKILL.md` (description triggers + `allowed-tools: mk_trust`/`Bash(cmk trust *)` + an "Adjust trust" action) — synced to all 3 copies (template / packages/cli/template / plugin; `validate-skill-sources` green). **LIVE-verified:** `cmk trust <id> low` flips a fact high→low + search reflects it with no manual reindex. The interaction model is **universal** — even the maintainer drives the kit by telling Claude *"run it"*, never typing `cmk`; the regular user voices an intent and assumes it happens (or happened automatically). Audit EVERY memory operation for a free-speech path — **automatic** (hook) OR **Claude-mediated** (skill trigger / MCP tool + instruction) — and close the gaps: **"forget X"** (no path today — add a forget skill-trigger + MCP `mk_forget`, confirm-token-gated per 108), **"trust this / not important"** (no path), **reliable recall-on-a-question** (partial → Task 75 active-recall, v0.3). A CLI verb without a free-speech path is **invisible** to the regular user. The MCP tools + skills (108) ARE the action surface; this task is the coverage AUDIT on top — which intents a user can voice, and whether each is automatic or Claude-mediated. Composes with 108 (tools/parity), 110 (forget completes automatically), 75 (active recall), and the memory-write skill pattern.

- [x] 132. _shipped 2026-06-11, PR #162 (D-122)._ **Fix the auto-extract dedup self-poisoning (CUT BLOCKER, found by cut-gate8).** Since Task 87 wired now.md as the conversation buffer, capture-turn appended the CURRENT turn to now.md BEFORE spawning the extractor — which then read "the last now.md entry" as its dedup context. - [ ] 140. **[D-253a trigger: ride-along the next time canonicalize.mjs is touched for ANY reason (byte-identical constraint stands); OR a Sonar re-flag]** **canonicalize: loop-based trailing-strip (the one REAL finding of the 31-hotspot Sonar triage, D-128).** `RE_TRAILING_PUNCT_WS = /[\s.,:;]+$/` is the textbook super-linear pattern (the StackOverflow-outage class).
