- [ ] 141. **[D-253a — TIME-SENSITIVE, re-laned: phase (a) mitigation (doctor HC + README note) rides v0.4.4 (npm 12 ships ~NOW, July 2026); phase (b) node:sqlite migration trigger: npm 12 GA + the first native-binding failure report, or the v0.5.0 cut — whichever first]** **npm v12 readiness (ships ~July 2026): the install-scripts default flips OFF — our native deps break on fresh installs (D-129).** `better-sqlite3` installs its binding via an install script (`prebuild-install` — already deprecation-warned), and `--with-semantic`'s `onnxruntime-node` does the same: under npm 12 a fresh `npm install -g` silently skips them → search/index crashes at first use. Two phases: **(a) v0.3.x mitigation** — reproduce under npm 11.16 warnings, add a `cmk doctor` HC ("native binding missing — npm 12 blocked the script; run `npm approve-scripts ...`"), README install note, `--with-semantic` runner guidance. **(b) the structural fix** — replace `better-sqlite3` with **`node:sqlite`** (built into Node 22.5+/24: zero native deps, zero install scripts, immune to the class; also ends the reinstall EPERM locked-DLL annoyance). `node:sqlite` supports `loadExtension` for sqlite-vec. The user (2026-06-12): "we can upgrade our node version to latest at any time" — the engines floor is NOT a blocker; spike the sqlite-vec extension load + the better-sqlite3 API-surface migration (index-db/search/semantic-backend callers). No git/URL deps in the kit, so `--allow-git`/`--allow-remote` are no-impact.

- [ ] 146. **Kit x Claude Code WORKFLOWS composition: concurrent MCP access + swarm recall (D-131).** Dynamic workflows spawn up to 16 CONCURRENT subagents (1,000/run), each starting COLD in the project - the kit's amnesia problem times a hundred, and the kit already reaches them through two existing doors: the CLAUDE.md managed block (loads per agent) and the inherited tool allowlist (`mcp__cmk__*` since Task 108 - every swarm agent can `mk_search` settled decisions prompt-free). Investigate: (a) a live workflow whose agents query mk_search (does recall reach a swarm?); (b) a concurrent-writes stress (N parallel mcp serve processes writing); (c) document the kit-x-workflows story in README/docs if it holds ("your swarm shares one memory"); (d) design question from the squad review (2026-06-12): per-ROLE memory partitions for swarm agents (squad gives each agent a charter.md + history.md alongside shared decisions) - shared facts + per-role histories may beat one undifferentiated pool at swarm scale.
  - **🔬 PRIMARY-SOURCE GEM + STATUS (deep-read 2026-06-28; D-218).** Confirmed a REAL data-loss path, not just theoretical: `appendScratchpadBullet` uses lockless `readFileSync`/`writeFileSync` on the markdown, and the SQLite index has **zero `busy_timeout`** → immediate `SQLITE_BUSY` under N concurrent servers. **mem0** names our exact race (funnel concurrent read-modify-write into ONE batched pass). **letta** ([`orm`](https://github.com/letta-ai/letta)) uses an optimistic `version_id_col` → raises `StaleDataError` so a lost write is LOUD, never silent — the pattern to steal. **Fit nuance:** the DB half needs only a `busy_timeout` (cheap); the MARKDOWN half needs the lock (reuse auto-extract's existing `O_CREAT|O_EXCL` lock-discipline). Patch-shaped. _VERDICT: keep-as-own-task; backlog-no-version-yet, RIDES Task 50 — the cross-agent work multiplies the concurrent servers, so live-test the race THERE (today, with one agent, it's mostly latent). Sequence alongside whichever agent release stresses it._
  - **🔬 REVISIT-WHEN-BUILDING — `songth1ef/nestwork`'s PARTITION-BY-WRITER concurrency (deep-read 2026-06-29; D-227).** A git-native markdown multi-agent memory tool (11★, license-unspecified — patterns not code) solves the concurrent-write race CHEAPER than locks/CRDT/busy-timeout: **each agent OWNS its own directory** (`agents/<host>/<agent-id>/memory.md`) so write paths NEVER overlap → no conflict resolution needed; plus a PreToolUse `git pull --rebase` before write + PostToolUse commit+push after, collapsing the race window to a single op. **For us:** if Task 50 ever has multiple agents writing the SAME shared `context/` concurrently, the cheapest fix may be PARTITION-BY-WRITER (per-agent scratchpad files) rather than locking the shared file — sidesteps the lock entirely for the per-agent surface, keeping locks only for the genuinely-shared facts. A real alternative to the lock-the-shared-file approach (mem0/letta) noted above. _Relates Task 50 (cross-agent — where the partition would live), the lock-discipline; D-227._

- [~] 147. **`cmk digest` (regenerated render) + `context/DECISIONS.md` (APPEND-ONLY permanent journal) (D-132, architecture settled D-161).** _CODE merged 2026-06-15/16 (decisions-journal.mjs + digest.mjs + `cmk digest` verb; DJ2 lowercase-id idempotency bug found+fixed by the cut-gate, D-159-adjacent); but the FEATURE is **HELD for v0.3.3, NOT shipped in v0.3.2 (D-164)** — un-framed from the v0.3.2 CHANGELOG/README because it is **write-only for the AI** (the journal isn't in any recall directive / isn't indexed → the AI never recalls from it). The kit's thesis is "you ask the AI and it recalls," not "the human opens a file"; a journal a human must read themselves doesn't deliver its purpose. v0.3.3 ships it COMPLETE = this code + **Task 156** (the AI-recall directive + memory-search step + a new cut-gate recall stage DJ4 + the live recall gate).   - **(a) `cmk digest` — regenerated render.** Everything the kit currently knows as one readable markdown page (facts by type, persona, active threads). A current-knowledge snapshot → **regenerated on demand** (like INDEX.md — correctly reflects only what exists now). The README-demo artifact from the D-130 sweep.
  - **(b) `context/DECISIONS.md` — APPEND-ONLY permanent decision journal.** A chronological, readable page of every decision + its why — the VIEW the kit is missing today (facts are captured but scattered across N per-fact files with no chronological decision view; `cmk search` is pull-not-browse; MEMORY.md is bounded + rolls). This is the squad `decisions.md` / our own DECISION-LOG.md equivalent, made automatic. **Lifecycle = append-only, kit-maintained, NEVER regenerated-from-live, NEVER parked/rolled like MEMORY.md** (D-161): decision captured → entry appended; superseded → OLD entry annotated in place (struck, not deleted) + new appended; forgotten → marked retracted, not removed. Unbounded by design — old decisions are the MOST valuable part (they explain why the codebase is shaped as it is), so the MEMORY.md rolling-window must NOT apply. Steal `merge=union` (`.gitattributes`, Task-154 infra) so teams don't conflict on the append-only file. v0.3.2 scope = explicit signals only (capture/forget/explicit-supersede); AUTOMATIC contradiction-detection deferred to F-D/Task 95.
  - **Decision source (the open sub-question):** decision-class facts = `type: project` (the kit taxonomy's decision/state category — what project-memory's `decisions.md` and our D-log track). No new `decision` type (schema change too heavy for a patch; settled in design when 147 lands).
  - **Why standing beats render-on-demand (for b):** the journal entry appears IN THE PR DIFF that captured the decision (reviewable at code-review time), travels with git clone to every teammate/swarm agent, readable without running anything. Composes with 144 as a sibling derived surface.

  > **⚠️ Decision-trail (D-161, supersedes the original 147(b) plan):** the entry above ORIGINALLY (pre-2026-06-15) read "decision-type facts append a journal line at capture, **maintained by the writers like INDEX.md**" — i.e. regenerated. **Set aside 2026-06-15** because reasoning through fact supersession/forget showed regeneration would silently ERASE superseded decisions (rewriting history — the decision-trail-preservation failure). The journal must be append-only/permanent; only `cmk digest` (a) is regenerated. See D-161.

- [ ] 148. **[D-253a trigger: the next auto-extract classifier-prompt touch (its natural home — Task 192 the Stop-hook judge is a candidate ride); OR a privacy incident / user request. Re-verdict at the v0.5.0 cut]** **Auto-judged privacy — sensitivity is Claude's judgment, not the user's tag (D-150).** The kit auto-decides what to KEEP (auto-extract) and auto-catches credential SECRETS (Poison_Guard); the `<private>` tag was the one place we punted judgment back to the user — and it's the worst place for a prospective tag (you don't know a passage is sensitive until you've already typed it). Apply the auto-extract thesis to privacy: at extraction time, if a candidate fact contains personal/sensitive content beyond Poison_Guard's regexes (health detail, real name, home address, private grievance), Claude does NOT write it to the git-committed project tier. **Default = Option A (the user's pick): DROP from the committed tier**; genuinely-useful-but-sensitive content falls through to `context.local/` (gitignored, this-machine-only) rather than vanishing. The `<private>` tag SURVIVES as the explicit override (the rare "scrub THIS passage" escape hatch — parallel to `cmk remember` as the override on auto-extract), NOT the primary path. Open design (settle before code): WHERE the judgment lives — the auto-extract Haiku classifier's instruction set is the natural home (it already judges durability per turn; add a sensitivity axis returning a `local-only` / `drop` / `commit` routing), composes with the existing `private: true` frontmatter flag (design §6.6) and the Poison_Guard boundary (§6.7); how `cmk remember`/`mk_remember` (no Haiku in the loop) get the same screen (a lightweight heuristic pass or a confirm-prompt for the explicit path); and the false-positive recovery story (a `cmk` command to pull a mis-routed local-only fact up to committed). _Slotted 2026-06-14 (D-150).   - **🔬 PRIMARY-SOURCE GEM + STATUS (deep-read 2026-06-28; D-218).** **UNMATCHED across all 9 surveyed repos — the design is genuinely OURS, no template to steal.** mem0 is the INVERSE (`fact_extraction` prompt instructs the model that PII/health are "the MOST valuable" to store); letta has zero sensitivity gate; basic-memory/the rest don't screen. **Why this matters MORE for us than for any of them:** a committed-tier leak ships to every `git clone` — strictly worse than a DB-backed competitor where a sensitive row stays on one server. So we're solving a problem the field doesn't, BECAUSE our git-committed model creates it. **Fit is clean:** add a `sensitivity: commit|local-only|drop` axis to the EXISTING auto-extract Haiku (it already judges durability per turn), fall through to gitignored `context.local/`. It rides 66's not-yet-started v0.4.4 lane (not v0.4.3) because 150 is DESIGN-FIRST — the D-126 ADR gates the build and must not delay the in-flight persona release. **Interim already in place:** the CLAUDE.md "Per-task-boundary (dogfood-memory flush)" rule (Durable-state-first checkpoint #4) makes this-and-future-session-me commit accumulated `context/` at every task boundary, unprompted — the manual stop-gap that closes the gap NOW, until 150's structural prompt subsumes it. **Build order for 150:** (1) the D-126 reconciliation ADR (propose-and-approve vs full-auto — recommend propose-and-approve, basic-memory-validated, honors the user-owns-the-commit gate); (2) the conversational-surface prompt (Claude proposes in-chat: "captured N durable facts — commit them? [y]"); (3) compose with the frozen-snapshot + no-surprise-in-git-history constraint._ `context/memory/*.md` is committed BY DESIGN (the kit's thesis — memory travels with `git clone`), but nothing makes it durable for the user. A user who never runs `git add context/` accumulates uncommitted facts lost on `git clean` / machine switch — "memory survives" depends on the user committing, and the kit is silent. **Surfaced live:** the v0.3.1 cut-gate's OWN dogfood accumulated 25 uncommitted facts that nearly went un-captured (the assistant kept discarding them as churn). **The user's directive — the fix is NOT a `cmk doctor` nudge** (relying on the user to remember to run doctor, then act, is the same anti-pattern as relying on `<remember>`; it breaks the "you don't manage memory, it just works" premise). It should be **AI-JUDGED automation**, the same shape as auto-extract (Claude judges what to save) and D-150 auto-judged privacy (Claude judges what's sensitive): Claude notices durable memory has accumulated and acts in-flow. **THE OPEN DESIGN TENSION (settle in the design doc before any code):** this collides with **D-126 (SETTLED: "no auto-git-commits; the user retains the publish gate")**. The reconciliation the user leaned toward: **AI proposes / one-tap approve** — the AI judges WHO/WHEN/WHETHER-worth-committing and initiates ("captured N durable facts this session — commit them to keep your memory? [y]"), the user retains the WHETHER gate (honors D-126's user-owns-the-commit) but carries zero remembering burden. Design doc must: (a) decide propose-and-approve vs revisit-D-126-for-full-auto (needs the user's explicit new-evidence call to overturn a SETTLED line); (b) where the judgment/prompt lives (SessionEnd? a Stop-hook batch? the conversational MCP surface so Claude does it in chat?); (c) how it composes with the frozen-snapshot + the user's outward-publish gate; (d) the no-surprise-in-git-history constraint. _Slotted 2026-06-14, reframed from a doctor-nudge to design-first per the user's steer. - [x] 151. **Persona-promotion model — reconsider the human-gated review-queue (BROADER DESIGN; v0.4 curation lane; gated here so we don't rabbit-hole it now but it doesn't fall to the sidelines — the user's 2026-06-14 call).** _**COMPLETE on branch `task-151-recurrence-promotion` 2026-06-30 (all 13 sub-tasks 151.1–151.13 + the 151.5 sweep re-eval). Full suite green throughout._ SURFACED BY the v0.3.1 cold-open (E1): the wedge transferred TOOLING habits (uv/ruff/types — stated as universal rules → `confidence: high` → auto-promoted) but NOT the user's layered-ARCHITECTURE philosophy. Root cause (verified against backup persona folders — NOT a code regression): the user stated architecture as a *philosophy* ("how I build backends: FastAPI is the delivery layer…") not a *universal imperative* ("in EVERY project ALWAYS…"), so `PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE` (auto-persona.mjs:205) correctly graded it `medium` (inferred, not stated-as-rule) → routed to `queues/persona-review.md` → which is **invisible (surfaced in no `cmk doctor`/status-line) AND has no resolve command** → the candidate is STRANDED → the cold-open only injects the ACTIVE persona, so the architecture never transferred. Older tests (cut-gate3/7 backups) had it as `trust: high` in the active persona — it worked then because it was phrased/graded as a rule. **The user's binding directive:** the fix must NOT add a command the user has to remember to run (a `cmk queue persona` walker is "a shitty and wrong fix" — same anti-pattern as `<remember>` / the rejected `cmk doctor` nudge). EITHER fix the AUTOMATIC promotion process so durable cross-project traits reach the persona on their own, OR have the AI judge/handle it in-flow (auto-extract / D-150 / Task-150 shape). **The broader question this gates (the real design):** is the confidence-gated, human-reviewed persona-promotion model the right architecture at all, or should persona promotion be AI-JUDGED in-flow like the rest of the kit's automation? Coheres with Task 149 (recall-trigger: judgment-pulled vs always-search), Task 150 (AI-judged commit), Task 148 (AI-judged privacy) — they are ALL instances of the same meta-question: **where the kit still relies on a human-gated queue / manual command, should it be AI-judged automation instead?** This task is the persona-curation instance. **RESEARCH DONE (2026-06-14) → [persona-promotion research note](../docs/research/2026-06-14-persona-promotion-models-cross-system.md):** cloned + read 9 real systems (mem0, MemoryOS/MemOS, Letta/MemGPT, langmem, graphiti/Zep, memory-os, claude-mem, basic-memory) + ChatGPT memory + articles. **Decisive: EVERY real system AI-judges promotion automatically; NONE use a human-gated review queue (we're the sole outlier). And our confidence signal is BACKWARDS — every system that scores durability uses FREQUENCY + RECURRENCE, not imperative phrasing.** **DIRECTION DECIDED (D-154, the user's "adopt the direction + a v0.3.1 down-payment"):** drop the human-review-queue; AI-judge promotion by cross-project recurrence + LLM judgment (mem0's add/update/skip per-fact pattern applied to the persona tier, à la Letta's sleeptime self-edit); post-hoc reversibility (`cmk forget`) instead of pre-gating. **DOWN-PAYMENT ALREADY SHIPPED (v0.3.1, D-154):** `resolvePersonaReviewQueue` + `autoDrainQueues` wiring — medium-confidence candidates now auto-promote on the daily/weekly drain (stops the stranding; no manual command). **THIS TASK (v0.4) = the full redesign:** replace `PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE`'s form-based gate with a recurrence-scored, LLM-judged promotion pass; keep explicit-imperative as a fast-path-to-high but stop second-classing demonstrated-but-not-declared traits; make the persona trivially inspectable + revertible. **DESIGN INPUT — EverOS reflection model (2026-06-25, [research note](../docs/research/2026-06-25-everos-markdown-memory-runtime.md)):** EverOS's `ReflectionOrchestrator` does **Select → Merge → Re-extract → Deprecate** — clusters fragmented episodes, merges to one high-quality entry, re-extracts atomic facts, and **deprecates the originals in-place via a `deprecated_by` frontmatter backref** (NOT delete). This is a more principled consolidation than the kit's rolling-window, and the deprecate-not-delete-with-backref pattern fits the kit's tombstone/decision-trail discipline cleanly. When designing 151's consolidation half, evaluate adopting the Select→Merge→Re-extract→Deprecate shape + a `superseded_by`/`deprecated_by` frontmatter field for the persona/fact merge (vs the current hard-drop). _Slotted 2026-06-14, the user: "do full deep research, gate the broader question to the next version, write it down as a task in a definite lane so we don't rabbit-hole but it doesn't fall to the sidelines." Relates D-154 (the down-payment + direction), Task 149/150/148 (the AI-judged-vs-human-gated meta-question), Task 12/97 (consolidation + dynamic-trust siblings), the auto-persona PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE (Task 78), the D-6 review-queue auto-drain (the down-payment's precedent), the EverOS reflection blueprint, D-126._
  - **▶ SECOND MECHANISM surfaced by the v0.3.4 cut-gate (2026-06-19, cut-gate17) — the redesign must cover BOTH, not just the confidence-gate.** The original filing is about AUTO-persona grading a philosophy `medium` → review-queue (the *promotion-never-happens* path). The redesign must reconcile the rolling-window cap-relief graduation (which EMPTIES the injected scratchpad) with the cold-open's need to READ that scratchpad — candidate fixes: (a) inject high-trust graduated `fragments/` at cold-open (not just the live scratchpads); (b) EXEMPT `trust:high` `user-explicit` promotions from cap-relief graduation (they ARE the durable persona the cold-open needs — graduating them out is self-defeating); (c) the recurrence-scored redesign naturally re-injecting recurrent traits. _Data point added 2026-06-19 from cut-gate17; D-177._ **▶ ROUTING ASYMMETRY (the sharper version, 2026-06-20):** the SAME architecture fact landed in DIFFERENT user-tier files across runs because of WHICH promoter fired — and only one routing survives the cold-open. **Auto-persona** (the session-end LLM synthesizer, `source: persona-synthesis`) routes by TOPIC → the architecture went to **LESSONS.md** in the prior real tier (`U-S65JW2SG`) and SURVIVED (injected). **Explicit `mk_lessons_promote`** (when Claude calls it in-chat) **defaults ALL facts to `HABITS.md § Working Style`** (`DEFAULT_SECTION['HABITS.md']`, lessons-promote.mjs) → this run's 8 promotions ALL concentrated in that one section → it overflowed its 1800B cap → cap-relief graduation evicted the oldest 6 (incl. arch) to fragments → not injected. **The root is target-file CONTENTION, not cap SIZE** (HABITS + LESSONS share the same 1800B cap): auto-persona SPREADS facts across HABITS/LESSONS/USER by topic (survives), while explicit-promote PILES them into one section (overflows). **So the redesign must also fix the explicit-promote routing** — either (d) route explicit promotes by topic like auto-persona does (don't dump everything in HABITS § Working Style), or (e) make `mk_lessons_promote`'s default target topic-aware. This is WHY the cut-gate saw the arch "in fragments now but in LESSONS before" — same fact, two promotion paths, two destinations, one survives. _Routing detail added 2026-06-20; the user's "it's in fragments now but in lessons.md in prior cut-gates?" catch._ **▶ SEVERITY CORRECTED (2026-06-20, the live E1): the cold-open WORKS — the wedge transferred the architecture philosophy clean.** The session-end auto-persona RE-SYNTHESIZED the architecture back into HABITS (`U-RMPX3T6Z`, condensed, trust:high) after the graduation eviction, so the cold-open injected it and Claude built the layered structure with zero prompting. So this is a TRANSIENT-soft-spot for Task 151 to harden (heavy-promotion or no-re-synthesis sessions could still strand), NOT a wedge-breaking gap. The re-synthesis (D-154 down-payment) covers the common case. See D-177._
  - **▶ THIRD INPUT — the `awrshift/claude-memory-kit` propose-then-confirm UX (2026-06-28; D-215).** Surveying the same-named `awrshift` kit surfaced one promotion idea worth folding in: their `/close-day` audit **proposes** promotions in-conversation (*"noticed you rejected em-dashes in three short copies this week — make it a tone-of-voice rule?"*) and writes the patch on "yes." **The recurrence-scoring half is ALREADY this task** (the "confidence is BACKWARDS, use FREQUENCY + RECURRENCE" decision above — `awrshift` independently arrived at the same recurrence signal every surveyed system uses, which CONFIRMS the direction; it is NOT new). **What IS new is the SURFACE: propose-then-confirm vs our silent auto-drain.** We deliberately auto-promote silently (post-hoc-reversible via `cmk forget`) — the D-169 "no manual ritual" thesis; their model asks first. **DECISION (keep our default, add an optional mention — NOT a gate):** the redesign KEEPS silent auto-promotion as the default (asking-first would re-introduce the human-in-the-loop we removed, and `awrshift`'s whole capture hinges on a manual end-of-day `/close-day` which is exactly our D-169 anti-pattern). But it MAY add an OPTIONAL low-friction surface where, on a HIGH-recurrence promotion, Claude *mentions* it in-conversation ("I've noticed X across 3 projects — I've promoted it to your persona; say so if that's wrong") — a heads-up, not a gate, so the user can `cmk forget` it if wrong without ever being BLOCKED on a prompt.   - **📐 DESIGN LOCKED 2026-06-29 (D-228).** Canonical HOW → [design.md §20](design.md); decision → [ADR-0016](../docs/adr/0016-recurrence-promotion-passive-trust-demote-not-evict.md); evidence (7-system code-read) → [research note](../docs/research/2026-06-29-curation-cluster-code-study.md). Grounded in the 7-system curation-cluster CODE-read (MemoryOS/mem0/letta/langmem/memclaw/graphiti/MemOS). Four moves, two new fields. The form-based gate → capped-recurrence; the fragments-eviction bug → demote-not-evict (snapshot = VIEW over never-deleted store); + an evolving-trust field (folded Task 97); + topic-spread routing. Cross-system consensus: never-delete + status-flip; recurrence (CAPPED) earns promotion; trust moves on outcome events not a clock. The two value-blind sweepers (MemoryOS LFU / MemOS top-N) ARE our bug — don't replicate.
  - **MOVE 1 — recurrence-scored promotion (replaces the form-based `PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE`):**
    - [x] 151.1 **`recurrence_count` frontmatter field + re-surface detection.** Add `recurrence_count:int` to the fact-file frontmatter schema (`provenance.mjs` validation + `write-fact.mjs`); bump it when the SAME canonical fact re-surfaces (re-stated by auto-extract → same content-hash ID; OR surfaced by `cmk search`/`cmk cite`). The existing canonical-ID (content-hash) IS the re-surface detector — same hash = same fact. **Done when:** re-capturing an identical-shape fact increments its `recurrence_count` (not a 2nd file); a `cmk search` hit on a fact bumps it. Over-mutation guard: other facts' counts untouched.
    - [x] 151.2 **The heat function (`computeHeat`) — capped recurrence + lazy recency.** Pure function: `heat = min(recurrence_count, RECUR_CAP)·W_REC + exp(-Δhours/τ)` (τ=24h), recency computed AT READ (no cron). The CAP is load-bearing (MemOS `min(count·w,2)`) — recurrence is a tie-breaker, never the driver. Constants named + tunable. **Done when:** unit-tested formula; a noisy-trivial fact (high count, low base) does NOT outrank a once-stated durable decision (the cap proves out).
    - [x] 151.3 **Wire the heat gate INTO promotion; delete `PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE`'s form-gate.** _shipped (branch) 2026-06-30 — cite-and-sum gate live: `resolveRecurrenceSum` + `assembleProjectCorpus` returns `{corpus,factIndex}` + classifier cites `source_fact_ids` + gate = `confidence=high OR recurrenceSum≥3`. Hole-A test green (3×-demonstrated medium trait promotes, no "always/never"). Two-pass review done (2 Important + 4 Minor from skill-review, actioned #1/#2/#4/#2-minor). 2415/2415 + stress 5/5._ **WIRING CONFIRMED (cite-and-sum, D-230, 5/5 bridge study):** the classifier emits `PERSONA CANDIDATE | … | source_fact_ids=[…]` (cites the facts it synthesized the trait from — NOT a `recurrence=N` count; 5/5 systems reject LLM-counting). Code resolves the ids against the corpus (reject hallucinated), SUMS their `recurrence_count` (151.1), gates promotion on that sum ≥ `PROMOTE_THRESHOLD` (3, from heat.mjs) — replacing the `confidence==='high'` gate at `auto-persona.mjs:534`. The promote flow AFTER the gate (section-ensure → detectConflicts → memoryWrite) is untouched. TDD: extend `PERSONA_CANDIDATE_RE` + `parsePersonaCandidates` for `source_fact_ids`; add a `resolveRecurrenceSum` helper; swap the gate. Caveat: the sum is deterministic, trait MEMBERSHIP is the LLM's grouping (acceptable — grouping is synthesis). See design.md §20.1. `auto-persona.mjs` promotes a working-scratchpad bullet → user-tier persona when `recurrence_count ≥ 3` (memclaw threshold, diversity-gate dropped for single-user) instead of when phrasing-graded `high`. Keep explicit-imperative as a fast-path-to-promote (a stated rule still promotes immediately) but STOP second-classing demonstrated-but-not-declared traits. **Done when (the Hole-A test):** a 3×-demonstrated philosophy promotes with NO "always/never" wording — the v0.3.1 cold-open regression case goes green.

    - [x] 151.5 **Sweep ORDER = low-trust AND long-unaccessed first; high-trust persona never swept.** _shipped (branch) 2026-06-30 — research-grounded (the note + ADR-0016 say a two-axis CONJUNCTION; single-axis IS the MemoryOS-LFU/MemOS-top-N bug).   - **MOVE 3 — evolving-trust field (= folded Task 97; the PROTECTION signal Move 2's sweep order needs):**
    - [x] 151.6 **`trust_score` field in the REBUILDABLE INDEX (not committed frontmatter — D-218).** _shipped (branch) 2026-06-30 — `observations.trust_score REAL` column + a new pure `trust-score.mjs` (`initTrustScore` seeds from source: user-explicit/manual-edit > imported > auto-extract/compressor at the same trust enum; clamped [0.05, 0.95]). Computed at insert in `index-rebuild.mjs` (one place, both builders); reconstructed deterministically on every full reindex; committed `.md` files carry NO trust_score (D-218). Non-destructive migration in `openIndexDb` (`PRAGMA table_info` → `ALTER ADD COLUMN`, idempotent) so a pre-151.6 DB gains the column without a rebuild + keeps its rows. Caller-map: only index-db/index-rebuild write observations — contained. **⚠️ This TRIGGERED the 151.5 sweep re-eval (now a real signal exists) — deferred the consume to 151.7/151.8 (the update rule + passive signals must land first; the sweep then keys on the evolved score).** Two-pass review pending pre-merge. 2420+._ A float per fact in the index-db (a moving value = git-diff noise if in frontmatter; markdown-as-truth keeps committed files clean). Init from source (`user-explicit` higher than `auto-extract` — memory-os source-based init). Rebuildable from events on reindex. **Done when:** the index carries `trust_score`; `cmk reindex` reconstructs it; committed `.md` files unchanged by trust movement. **✅ 151.5 RE-EVAL RESOLVED (2026-06-30, D-238):** assessed after 151.8 landed the evolved `trust_score` — verdict: the sweep KEEPS the `trust` ENUM proxy; it does NOT consume the float. Grounded in research (memclaw/letta/graphiti use the evolved score as a FLOOR/never-delete protection, NOT a sweep-ranking driver; rank-and-sweep-by-score = the cautionary MemoryOS-LFU/MemOS-top-N bug) AND code (the FLOOR 0.05 protection is already wired in the arithmetic; the enum already protects high-trust structurally; the inject path doesn't open the index-db, so a trust_score lookup would add 500ms-budget DB I/O + rank on an overlay that resets on full reindex = non-deterministic). The enum sweep order (151.5) + the trust_score floor (151.7) + demote-not-evict (151.4) already deliver the research-faithful protection. The `// 151.6: re-evaluate` markers are resolved to decision-trail pointers. Full verdict: design §20.3.
    - [x] 151.7 **The trust update rule — asymmetric, clamped, floored, EVENT-driven.** _shipped (branch) 2026-06-30 — `updateTrustScore(current, event)` in trust-score.mjs: `REINFORCE_DELTA +0.1` / `DAMPEN_DELTA −0.15` (asymmetric — a fail outweighs a success), clamped to `[FLOOR 0.05, CEIL 0.95]`, NO time-decay (event-driven, not clock-driven; recency decay stays a read-time search-ranking concern). Pure + deterministic; an unknown event is a no-op (a not-yet-wired signal can't corrupt a score). 9 tests: deltas, asymmetry (reinforce-then-dampen nets negative), floor holds at 0.05 over 20 dampens (never zero → never auto-deleted), ceil holds, no-time-decay, defensive garbage-clamp, composes with initTrustScore. Adversarial probe confirmed float accumulation lands exactly on CEIL (no drift) + boundary-idempotence. Two-pass review 0 findings. Caller-map: new export, no callers yet (151.8 wires it). Grounded in memclaw `evolve_service._adjust_weights` (the research). 2443/2443._ `+0.1` reinforce / `−0.15` dampen / floor `0.05` (memclaw `_adjust_weights`), NO time-decay of the stored value (decay is search-ranking only). **Done when:** unit-tested deltas; floor holds at 0.05 (never zero / never auto-deleted); asymmetry (failures dampen faster) proven.
    - [x] 151.8 **Passive outcome signals → the trust deltas (zero ritual — D-169).** _shipped (branch) 2026-06-30 — 3 signals wired, NO `cmk` command (D-169). **Two mechanisms, research-corrected (D-237):** (a) the asymmetric DAMPEN overlay (`applyTrustSignal` in new `trust-signal.mjs`, best-effort, never throws) for **contradiction** (conflict-queue route → dampen the existing fact, `memory-write doAdd`) + **supersession** (`memory-write doReplace` → dampen the old fact; covers direct replace + persona-supersede) — these are the genuine memclaw `_adjust_weights` outcome events, runtime overlays on the rebuildable index (survive boot reindex, reseed on full — local-protection posture, D-237); (b) **restatement/recurrence is NOT an overlay** — the review caught that a re-surface overlay was reseeded away by the very reindex `bumpRecurrence`'s file-write triggers (proven: 0.45→0.55→reindex→0.45). The RESEARCH-FAITHFUL fix (MemoryOS/MemOS/honcho all make the recurrence COUNT a score TERM, not an event): fold a **capped recurrence term into `initTrustScore`** (reconstructed from the committed `recurrence_count`, 151.1) → a re-stated fact seeds higher DURABLY (survives every reindex) — cap is load-bearing (a high-recurrence low-trust fact never outranks a once-stated high-trust one). **Two-pass review** found this as a Blocking bug + fixed it; the merge-path supersession gap (mergeScratchpadBullets / merge-facts don't dampen) is honestly deferred to 151.12. Integration tests exercise the REAL writeFact/memoryWrite chains incl. a signal→reindex→assert durability regression. 2452+._ Wire the 3 single-user-portable signals: **contradiction** (contradiction-queue hit → dampen), **supersession** (`superseded_by` set → dampen the old), **restatement/recurrence** (the 151.1 re-surface → reinforce). NO `cmk` command, no `report_outcome` call. **Done when:** a fact contradicted in a session has its trust dropped with NO manual command; a re-stated fact's trust rises.

Research-grounded (FTS5 spec §3 primary source + basic-memory's `_prepare_search_term`). The 3 pre-existing FTS5-error tests inverted to assert success (justified test change). Live-verified on the real CLI (`v0.3`, the exact crash string, `user-explicit` all return clean). - [x] 157. **Bug 1 — `cmk reindex --full` UNIQUE-constraint crash (id-keyed vs file-scoped delete).** _fixed 2026-06-16, v0.3.3 branch `fix-reindex-id-collision` (D-165)._ `cmk remember` dual-writes a fact to BOTH the `MEMORY.md` scratchpad bullet AND its granular `context/memory/*.md` archive, both with the same content-addressed id; but `observations.id` is a global PRIMARY KEY and `replaceObservationsForFile` deleted by `source_file` only, so reindexing the second source collided (`UNIQUE constraint failed: observations.id`) and aborted the whole reindex (4 colliding ids on the live corpus). **Full cross-project root-cause pass** ([research note](../docs/research/2026-06-16-index-uniqueness-id-vs-file-scoped-delete.md)): 3 markdown-first analogs (TencentDB id-keyed upsert / basic-memory partial-unique-index + resolve_permalink / memweave content-hash) all key replacement on the id, never a composite `(id,file)` key. **Fix:** id-keyed replacement with archive-beats-scratchpad precedence — `fact` source DELETEs-by-id then INSERTs (wins); `scratchpad` source `ON CONFLICT(id) DO NOTHING` (yields). Order-independent. **Self-review caught a 2nd bug:** the first impl's `INSERT OR REPLACE` orphaned the old scratchpad body in the external-content FTS5 index (silent stale hits) — switched to explicit DELETE-by-id so the FTS `'delete'` sentinel fires; pinned by a Door-4 orphan-guard test. Live-verified on the real corpus (no crash, FTS consistent, dups→one archive row each).

- [x] 160. **CLAUDE.md diet — migrate heavy PROCEDURAL disciplines out of the always-loaded rules file into on-demand skills (D-170).** _**REVISED 2026-06-18 (D-170 revision — see DECISION-LOG):** the adoption path below was CORRECTED. The mattpocock skills are NOT gitignored project copies + NOT wired into the agency table — they live at the PERSONAL tier (`~/.claude/skills/`) via the author's installer (auto-discovered everywhere, untouched upstream), and CLAUDE.md was REVERTED to inline TDD/deep-modules rules. D-170's core insight stands (overflow→rules-followed-less); only the where/how of adoption changed. Fact P-FJZFLaP9._ _Conservative pass shipped 2026-06-18 (the user's call: "stop at conservative"). **Done (as originally executed — since revised):** (1) 6 mattpocock skills adopted verbatim into `.claude/skills/` (gitignored dev-tooling — diagnosing-bugs / codebase-design / domain-modeling / grilling / prototype / tdd); (2) CLAUDE.md's generic TDD/boundary-test how-to + the deep-modules block replaced with one-line skill pointers (commit efd23a3), kit-specific rules kept; (3) all 6 skills wired into the **Skill-agency table** with concrete triggers so they FIRE proactively (the whole point of adopting them) + a note that they own the procedural HOW so it doesn't bloat the always-loaded file. **Deferred (NOT this pass — the user gated it):** the bigger size win — moving the HEAVY kit-specific precedent-laden disciplines (live-test flow, two-pass review, caller-map, composition-verification, lazy-framing) into NEW kit-authored skills with one-line pointers. Those are precedent-dense + no mattpocock skill covers them, so migrating them needs careful per-rule authoring (no precedent lost) and changes how core disciplines load — re-evaluate after the kit's own overflow actually bites. Net: the conservative pass is additive (389→397 lines); the real reduction is the deferred heavy-flow migration. KEPT always-on judgment rules (name-privacy, source-of-truth table, working-style, anti-patterns, "did you check the primary source?")._ **The insight (the user, 2026-06-18):** *"we know that at some point when CLAUDE.md overflows the AI at some point doesn't really do what is written there — and if we are at that point, it makes all the times you didn't actually do what is written there make sense."* CLAUDE.md is always-loaded + very large; an overflowing always-on rules file is followed LESS reliably (attention dilutes), which retroactively explains misses against rules that ARE written down (e.g. the D-169 done-criteria gap, the times a verification rule was skipped). **A well-built SKILL ≠ a CLAUDE.md rule** (the user's load-bearing point, validated by reading mattpocock/skills — D-170): a skill is **loaded on-demand**, focused, with depth in linked files, invoked only when the task fits — the correct architecture for *procedural* discipline (a multi-step HOW), vs CLAUDE.md which should hold *always-true* judgment rules + the source-of-truth table. **Scope (DESIGN-FIRST — audit, don't rip):** identify CLAUDE.md rules that are PROCEDURAL (a repeatable multi-step flow the AI executes when a trigger fits) vs ALWAYS-ON (a judgment/anti-pattern/source-of-truth fact that must color every turn). Candidates to migrate to skills: the **live-test-every-task** flow, the **two-pass code-review** flow, the **cut-gate** run, the **caller-map-before-changing-a-shared-fn** procedure, the **adoption-verification** template, the **branch/PR/merge housekeeping** sequence. Candidates to KEEP in CLAUDE.md: name-privacy, the source-of-truth table, the working-style/tone, the anti-patterns, the verification-judgment rules ("did you check the primary source?"). Each migrated rule leaves a ONE-LINE pointer in CLAUDE.md ("Reviewing a PR → invoke the `code-review` skill") so the trigger→skill link survives. **Compose with the existing skill infra:** dev-tooling skills live in `.claude/skills/` (gitignored — local, per-machine) OR a tracked `dev-tools/` if we want them shared; the KIT's OWN skills (memory-search/memory-write) stay in `template/`+`plugin/` (shipped) — do NOT mix the two. _Relates D-170 (the pocock-skills adoption + the overflow insight), the D-169 done-criteria rule (a recent rule that nearly wasn't followed), the "Prose rules vs enforcement" section (this extends it: prose→validator for structural rules, prose→skill for procedural ones), the CLAUDE.md "Skill agency" section. v0.3.x dev-tooling lane — ships nothing to users._
  - Estimate: M (design-first audit + per-rule migrate) · Depends: none (but informed by the Task-160-adjacent pocock-skills adoption) · _v0.3.x dev-tooling; reduces the overflow→ignored risk._

- [x] 161. **Session-buffer compression times out as `now.md` grows (v0.3.4, D-171).** _shipped 2026-06-19, PR #206 (D-175). The fix is a BOUNDED TRANSIENT-ONLY RETRY, not an input cap — measurement (D-174) inverted the original size-spiral premise: the timeout is environmental, not size-driven (the kit's own log: largest success 470 KB > largest timeout 334 KB; a 9 KB input timed out). `compressWithRetry` + `isRetryableCompressError` (9-system retry survey); ceiling-free paths retry (maxAttempts:2), the SessionEnd-hook delegates to the lazy path (maxAttempts:1, D-42/D-79). Observability fix (HaikuFailedError exit_code/stderr → log) shipped first so the classification is real. Full suite 2012/2012, stress 5/5, live cut-gate on real Haiku (transient-recovers + deterministic-fast-fails), two-pass review. 161.12 (retry-rate logging) deferred as a fast-follow._ RESEARCH-FIRST. **The problem (the user's framing, confirmed in data):** the SessionStart now→today roll (`compress-session`, Task 84/§8.5) spawns `claude --print --model claude-haiku-4-5` to compress the `now.md` session buffer, under a **50s inner timeout** (`compress-session.mjs:334`, sits under the 60s SessionEnd hook ceiling). When the compression exceeds 50s it errors `haiku_timeout`, `now.md` is left UNTOUCHED (fail-safe — no corruption, no `today-*.md` written), and the roll is retried **only at the next SessionStart** (`detectStaleness`→`stale-now`; the cooldown marker is only set on SUCCESS, so a failed run doesn't block the retry — but it also never drains the buffer). **The compounding spiral (the load-bearing insight — the user 2026-06-18):** a failed roll → `now.md` keeps growing → the next compression has a BIGGER input → takes LONGER → more likely to hit 50s again → grows further. It correlates: bigger buffer ⇒ slower Haiku ⇒ more timeouts ⇒ unbounded growth. **This re-introduces the exact Task-105/D-75 unbounded-`now.md`-growth problem**, just gated behind a timeout instead of a missing SessionEnd hook. **The DATA (the kit's OWN dogfood `context/sessions/*.compress.log` — NOT synthetic):** real compressions span **21s–50s+**; **5 historical `haiku_timeout` failures**; and the kit's own `now.md` has reached **166 KB / 334 KB / 405 KB / 470 KB** inputs — all of which timed out at 50s. At cut-gate-16, a fresh ~10 KB buffer took **71s then 89s** on two consecutive isolated runs of the EXACT compressor invocation (`--print --model claude-haiku-4-5 --tools "" --max-turns 1 --mcp-config {"mcpServers":{}} --strict-mcp-config --output-format text`) — the OUTPUT was a correct 4-section summary; it was just SLOW. So the compression LOGIC is fine; the `claude --print` latency vs the 50s budget is the failure. **Investigation already done (cut-gate-16, 2026-06-18):** isolated the spawn (plain `claude --print "say OK"` returns in <30s — so not a dead CLI / not nested-claude / not env-broken); ran the exact sandboxed invocation with the Haiku model + real input → 71-89s consistently; confirmed `now.md` preserved on timeout; traced the retry path (SessionStart-only, cooldown-on-success-only). **▶ RESEARCH-FIRST (the user's explicit directive — "real deep research, not just skim over"):** before designing a fix, CLONE + read how other memory/agent projects handle session-buffer compression under latency + growth. Candidate questions: do they compress incrementally (chunk-at-a-time) instead of whole-buffer? compress at session-END too (not only SessionStart-lazy)? cap the buffer + compress-the-overflow rather than the whole thing? use a faster path / smaller model / a deterministic pre-trim before the LLM? a streaming/partial compaction? shrink-and-retry on timeout (OpenHands-style — already noted for Task 84)? Sweep the real repos (squad, basic-memory, mem0, MemoryOS, Letta, claude-mem, OpenHands, + the rolling-window precedents). **Candidate fixes to weigh (post-research, NOT pre-decided):** (a) compress at SessionEND in addition to SessionStart (the user's hunch — drain the buffer while it's small, so SessionStart rarely has a huge backlog); (b) a hard `now.md` size cap that triggers mid-session compaction before it gets huge; (c) chunked/incremental compression so input size is bounded regardless of session length; (d) raise/adapt the timeout (weak — doesn't fix the spiral, just delays it); (e) a deterministic pre-trim (keep last N turns verbatim, summarize the rest) to bound LLM input. **BROADER THAN THE ROLL (cut-gate-16 §7 F-4, 2026-06-18):** the timeout is NOT only the now→today roll — it's the **whole Haiku-compression family**. `cmk daily-distill` ALSO timed out `haiku_timeout` at 50000ms in the sweep (it spawns the same `claude --print` Haiku path). `weekly-curate` skipped cleanly only because it had `no-old-files` (no Haiku call). So the fix must address the shared compressor timeout/latency for compress-session AND daily-distill AND weekly-curate — all the lifecycle compression verbs route through `HaikuViaAnthropicApi.compress` under the same 50s budget. **Done when:** research note written (the borrowed mechanism + why), a design decision in design §8.5/§8.2, the fix implemented + a cut-gate stage that feeds a LARGE buffer and asserts the roll completes (or degrades safely without unbounded growth), and the kit's own 400KB+ `now.md` backlog drains. **Verify the fix covers daily-distill + weekly-curate too, not just the session-end roll.**
  - **Done-when (explicit acceptance criteria):**
    - [x] 161.1 RESEARCH note written — 19-system fresh-clone survey of buffer-compaction-under-latency+growth ([2026-06-18-session-buffer-compaction-under-latency-growth.md](../docs/research/2026-06-18-session-buffer-compaction-under-latency-growth.md)); finding: 17/19 bound the input, the 2 that don't are the kit's own precedents (claude-remember + pre-fix claude-mem). _Done 2026-06-18._
    - [x] 161.2 DESIGN decision recorded — bound-the-input (not raise-the-timeout); design **§8.2.5** + DECISION-LOG **D-173**. _Done 2026-06-18 (REFINED by a product-design review: core = A+C at a shared seam; B dropped; D deferred — see §8.2.5 / D-173)._
    **Phase 1 — RESEARCH + DIAGNOSIS (done)**
    - [x] 161.1 RESEARCH note — 19-system fresh-clone survey (done 2026-06-18, 161.1 above).
    - [x] 161.6 MEASURE latency-vs-size — DONE 2026-06-19 (D-174). **RESULT: the failure is ENVIRONMENTAL/TRANSIENT, NOT input-size-driven.** Fresh harness 2–200 KB = flat 12–18s; the kit's own compress.log: largest SUCCESS (470 KB, 21s) BIGGER than the largest timeout (334 KB); a 9 KB input timed out. **This INVERTED the original size-bound design (D-173 set aside).**
    - [x] 161.r REPRODUCTION attempt — DONE 2026-06-19. Could NOT reproduce a failure: ~40 real Haiku calls (in-process AND through the real `cmk-compress-session` bin against real `now.md` on disk, up to 470 KB, concurrent w/ persona) all succeeded. **Conclusion: the failure is tied to the real SessionEnd SHUTDOWN environment** (MCP servers releasing native DLLs, parent teardown, disk/CPU contention at exit) — not harness-reproducible by nature. Confirms: instrument, don't simulate.
    - [x] 161.6a OBSERVABILITY FIX — DONE 2026-06-19, test-first (commit b4accc5). `HaikuFailedError` carries structured `exitCode`+`stderr`; all three callers write `exit_code`+`error_detail` into compress.log. So the next real `compress_failed` is diagnosable (pre-fix the WHY was discarded — the undiagnosable 329-byte failure). Live-verified.

    **Phase 2 — THE FIX: bounded retry on a transient failure (the established plan, grounded in code + research + D-174)**
    The failure is transient/environmental → the field mechanism is **retry** (research §"mechanism 5": OpenHands shrink-and-retry; for US "shrink" is moot since size isn't the cause, so it's a PLAIN bounded retry). The code already RESTORES the buffer on failure (D-79 `restoreRolling`) and re-rolls next SessionStart — so a delayed retry already exists; this task makes it FASTER + covers the cron paths, **within the verified composition budgets.**
    - [x] 161.8 IMPLEMENT the bounded retry helper — DONE 2026-06-19, test-first. `compress-retry.mjs`: `compressWithRetry(backend, opts, {maxAttempts, baseBackoffMs, isRetryable})` + `isRetryableCompressError(err)` (timeout=retry; transient `haiku_failed` via stderr=retry; ENOENT/auth/deterministic=no). Exponential backoff, reraise after exhaustion. 9 unit tests (Door 1 + Door 3: asserts the SECOND spawn happens with the same opts). Grounded in the 9-system retry survey.
    - [x] 161.9 WIRE the CEILING-FREE paths — DONE 2026-06-19, test-first. `dailyDistill` + `weeklyCurate` + the **lazy** `compressSession` (via `runLazyCompress`) call with `maxAttempts: 2`. Retry-and-recover tests added (daily-distill + compress-session: timeout-once→retry→recent.md/today written, 2 spawns).
    - [x] 161.10 SessionEnd-hook path — DONE 2026-06-19 (D-175): NO in-hook retry. `compressSession` gained a `maxAttempts = 1` DEFAULT (single attempt — the hook contract under the 60s ceiling + concurrent persona); it keeps restore-on-failure (D-79) and delegates the retry to the lazy path (which passes `maxAttempts: 2`). Two contract tests pin it: default→1 spawn+restore; maxAttempts:2→retries+recovers.
    - [x] 161.x VALIDATOR FIX (composition surfaced by the wiring) — DONE 2026-06-19. The 3 verbs moved from `backend.compress({...})` to `compressWithRetry(backend, {...})`, so `validate-prompt-assertions` (Door 3.5) stopped discovering them as LLM-spawn sites (its test caught it). Extended the discovery regex to recognize the `compressWithRetry(backend, {` shape too; 5 sites discovered + pinned again. Full suite 2012/2012.
    - [x] 161.11 CUT-GATE + LIVE-test — DONE 2026-06-19, on REAL Haiku. **(a)** transient-recovery: a flaky backend timed out on attempt 1 then delegated to REAL `HaikuViaAnthropicApi` on attempt 2 → genuine 408b compression in 17.5s, `isRetryable(timeout)=true`. **(b)** deterministic-fast-fail: a missing-binary spawn failed in 150ms over 1 attempt (NO retry, no wasted backoff). **Platform finding:** on Windows a missing binary surfaces as `exitCode:1` + stderr "is not recognized as an internal or external command" (NOT raw ENOENT) — and `isRetryableCompressError` correctly returns false via the **conservative default** (unknown non-zero exit → not retryable). That default is load-bearing: it's what makes an unrecognized failure fail-safe instead of looping. _Stress gate (5×) is the last step before merge._

    **Self-review findings (2026-06-19, before the skill-review pass)**
    - _Composition VERIFIED: ceiling-free retry worst case = 50s + 600ms backoff + 50s ≈ 100.6s. Safe for daily-distill/weekly-curate (cron, no ceiling) AND the lazy compressSession (DETACHED SessionStart child — the hook spawns-and-unrefs, so no 30s SessionStart ceiling applies to the child). The 120s cooldown + claim-rename mutex (D-79) prevent a fast-reopen overlap._
    - [x] 161.12 (FOLLOW-UP, the Door-4 gap from self-review) — DONE 2026-06-19. `compressWithRetry` gained an `onRetry({attempt, error})` callback (best-effort, can't break the retry); the three ceiling-free callers (daily-distill, weekly-curate, lazy compress-session) count retries and record `retries: N` on their compress.log entry — on BOTH success (recovered after a transient retry) and failure (exhausted retries = the strongest degrading-environment signal). `retries` only appears when > 0 (clean entries otherwise). So a frequent-retry RATE (the D-174 degrading-environment signal) is now visible. Tests: onRetry fires once/retry with {attempt,error}, not on first-try success / non-retryable failure (unit); the real log entry carries `retries:1` after a recovered timeout (integration).

    **Decision trail (what was tried and set aside — preserve per the decision-trail rule)**
    - _**D-173 (A/B/C/D input-bounding) SET ASIDE 2026-06-19 by D-174** — the size-driven premise was falsified by measurement. The 19-system survey + four-family taxonomy remain valid prior art; they just don't apply to OUR (environmental) failure. **A (input cap) may return as a trivial guard ONLY IF** a future huge-buffer case is ever measured — not now._
    - _**The mid-session 161.3/161.4/161.5 (boundCompressionInput seam) is SET ASIDE with D-173** — it was the size-bound implementation; superseded by the retry plan above._
  - _Phase status (2026-06-19): research ✅ + diagnosis ✅ + observability fix ✅ (commit b4accc5) + the retry design FULLY RESEARCHED (9-system code read, D-175) + RE-PLANNED. The size-bound design (D-173) was inverted by measurement (D-174); the fix is now a bounded transient-only retry (161.8–161.11), grounded in the full code read + the 9-system retry research + the verified composition budgets. The SessionEnd-hook decision (161.10) is SETTLED (delegate to the lazy path, no in-hook retry — D-175). Implementation (161.8–161.11) is the next step, test-first._

- [x] 162. **No user-facing UPDATE path (v0.3.4, D-172).** _shipped 2026-06-19 (D-176). (2) re-run `cmk install` **per project** — to refresh the version-stamped scaffold (the CLAUDE.md managed block, hooks, skills, `.gitattributes`/`.gitignore` all carry `:start v${version}` markers that `install` refreshes idempotently — verified in install.mjs `buildGitattributesBlock`/`buildGitignoreBlock`/etc.); then **restart Claude Code** so the new hooks + MCP server load. **Updating the npm package ALONE does NOT update a project** — the scaffolded block/hooks stay at the old version until `cmk install` re-runs. **This bit US twice THIS session (the dogfood proof, NOT hypothetical):** the global `cmk` was a stale 0.3.3 → had to `npm install -g <tarball>` to get the new code (and a stale TARBALL nearly shipped the wrong code — checked tarball contents, not just "install succeeded"); + a `cmk doctor` HC that detects version drift (global binary version vs the project's CLAUDE.md `:start vX` marker → "run `cmk install` to refresh") and optionally an outdated-vs-npm check (`npm view @lh8ppl/claude-memory-kit version` — network, opt-in). **▶ BOTH INSTALL PATHS need an update story — the npm/CLI path AND the PLUGIN path (the user 2026-06-18 caught that 162 v1 only covered npm).** The kit ships TWO supported install routes (README "pick ONE route"; Linters leave HTML comments alone, so blank-around-headings never touches the pair — but the writers must keep them adjacent. (b) **NEVER reindent column-0 bullets** (2→4 space) — every `^- \(` anchored matcher breaks (provenance.BULLET_RE + 6 readers). The MD007 hit on the 2-space *provenance-comment* indent is NOT a real list item — answer it with a scoped markdownlint nuance or leave it, do NOT reindent. - [ ] 166. **kiro-cli V3 (2.9+) hook support — the delete-guardrail + any new triggers via the V3 mechanism (D-198 follow-up).** kiro-cli V3 redesigned hooks as a BREAKING CHANGE (proven live 2026-06-24, KIRO_VERSION=2.9.0): embedded agent-config hooks moved to **standalone `.kiro/hooks/*.json` files with PascalCase triggers**, and tool-blocking moved from `preToolUse` to a new **`permissions.yaml`** capability model (kiro.dev/docs/cli/v3). Our V2-style embedded `agentSpawn`/`stop` STILL fire on 2.9.0 (capture/inject work — D-198 proven), but V2 `preToolUse` does NOT — so the **delete-guardrail doesn't fire on kiro-cli V3** (it falls back to kiro-cli's own shell-approval prompt). 2.9.0 also renamed the shell tool `execute_bash`→`execute_command` (already added to `guard-memory.mjs` SHELL_TOOLS). **Done when:** the kit emits the V3 guardrail (research the `.kiro/hooks/*.json` PascalCase schema + `permissions.yaml`; decide V3-only vs both-V2+V3 by detecting the installed kiro-cli version), live-verified blocking a memory delete on a real 2.9+ session; capture/inject confirmed still working on both V2 + V3. · Estimate: M (research + a new emit path + version-detection) · Depends: none · _v0.4.x or v0.5 — NOT a v0.4.0 blocker (capture/inject, the core value, work on V3; the guardrail has Kiro's native fallback). Relates D-198._

- [x] 167. **Stale-injection bug — the lazy now.md→today roll (Task 105) doesn't recover a SEVERELY-bloated `now.md`, so the injected snapshot froze at a 5-day-old day-file (surfaced by the v0.4.0 dogfood, 2026-06-25; D-205/D-206). The 105 LINEAGE robustness fix (do 105 with it — the user's call).** **Task 105 IS shipped + works as designed** (lazy-roll on SessionStart; PR #127 + race-fix #128) — but it was built/tested against a ~10 KB `now.md`. **The dogfood exposed the gap:** across the v0.4.0 gate sessions (06-20→06-25, many VS Code restarts), `now.md` grew to **410 KB** and the latest `today-*.md` froze at **06-20** — so `inject-context`'s `latestDaySession()` kept surfacing a 5-day-old snapshot whose "Active Threads" still said *"v0.4.0 Kiro adapter: RESEARCH-FIRST, pending"* (when v0.4.0 had SHIPPED). The user: *"why is it stale? this is the whole point of this kit."* **⚠️ SCOPE / SEVERITY (the user's catch 2026-06-25: "the cron is not registered by default, right?" — CORRECT, and it narrows this):** `cmk install` does NOT register crons; `cmk register-crons` is OPTIONAL (npm README: *"otherwise self-heals lazily"*). So the **DEFAULT user (no cron) is NOT affected** — no sentinel → `cron-active` never fires → the lazy roll works + the "self-heals lazily" promise holds. **This bug bites ONLY a user who ran `cmk register-crons` AND whose cron doesn't actually fire** (machine asleep at 23:00, registration that never triggers, etc.). The nasty part — and why it's still a real bug: **opting into scheduled compression makes things WORSE than not opting in** — `register-crons` writes a sentinel that DISABLES the working lazy fallback, then defers to a cron that may never run. A user who tried to be MORE careful gets a SILENTLY broken self-heal. Severity = medium (not "every user's memory rots"), but it's a trap on the exact careful-user path. **Root cause (PROVEN from `lazy-compress.log` + live state — NOT the timeout I first guessed; the log corrected me):** the lazy roll **never ran once from 06-20→06-25** — SKIPPED every SessionStart, never even attempted. Two compounding gates, NEITHER size-related: **(1) `cron-active` short-circuit (the PRIMARY bug).** `detectStaleness` ([lazy-compress.mjs](../packages/cli/src/lazy-compress.mjs) L216-219) does *"Cron sentinel short-circuits everything"* — if `context/.locks/cron-registered` exists it returns `cron-active` and **no-ops BEFORE the `stale-now` bloat check** (precedence `cron > … > now`; L229's own comment admits *"cron-active above still wins"*). **The trap:** `cmk register-crons` wrote the sentinel → the lazy roll forever defers to "the cron" → **but the host cron NEVER ACTUALLY RAN** (live-confirmed: `Get-ScheduledTask cmk-daily-distill` = State "Ready" but `LastRunTime` BLANK — registered, never fired; machine asleep at the 23:00 trigger). So the sentinel **disabled the only working compression path while pointing at a dead primary.** **(2) `cooldown` (06-23 onward).** After the cron-active stretch the shared 120 s cooldown (L339-359) kept skipping the roll — frequent journal-syncs touch the same cooldown marker, holding it perpetually fresh, so the roll never got a window. Net: `now.md` grew 10 KB→410 KB because **the roll was gated out of existence, not because it failed.** (Manual `cmk-compress-session` drained 410 KB→1386 b in 26 s — the roll WORKS; it was never allowed to run.) **THIS is why "105 wasn't a real fix, just postponed the problem" (the user — correct, now proven):** 105's lazy roll turns ITSELF OFF the instant a cron sentinel exists, with ZERO verification the cron is alive — the fallback defers to a primary that's dead. Green in the test (no sentinel, clean cooldown), broken in the real dogfood (sentinel present, cooldown busy). **Done when (the fix — TDD, the 105 lineage):** ☐ reproduce with a failing test: sentinel present + cron-never-ran (stale `today-*.md`) + bloated `now.md` → assert the roll STILL fires (cron-active must NOT short-circuit a bloated/stale state); ☐ **cron-liveness gate** — `cron-active` may short-circuit ONLY if the cron actually ran recently (test `today-*.md`/`recent.md` freshness or a cron heartbeat, NOT the sentinel's mere existence); a registered-but-dead cron must fall through to the lazy roll; ☐ **size-triggered roll** — `detectStaleness` adds a `now-too-big` verdict that OUTRANKS `cron-active` (a bloated `now.md` ALWAYS rolls, sentinel or not); ☐ **cooldown carve-out** — the roll-when-bloated path bypasses the 120 s cooldown (or journal-sync stops touching the compress cooldown marker); ☐ chunked/bounded compression so a huge `now.md` can't time out one pass + a **synchronous catch-up** past a hard ceiling; ☐ **observability** already logs skips (that's HOW this was diagnosed — keep it) + add a WARN when skipping a bloated `now.md`; ☐ a `cmk doctor` HC that flags (a) a bloated/non-draining `now.md`, (b) a stale `today-*.md`, AND (c) a **registered cron that never ran** (`LastRunTime` blank / sentinel-without-recent-distill) with the repair command; ☐ confirm `inject-context` never serves a day-file older than the actual latest session. **Compose with:** Task 105 (the lazy-roll it extends), Task 106 (rename-race — a sync catch-up must keep atomicity), Task 35 (the cron path the dead-cron gate touches), §6 rolling-window, the cooldown. · Estimate: M-L (a real diagnose→TDD→fix on the memory-roll core, 3 sub-bugs) · Depends: none · _**This is the v0.4.1 release (re-laned 2026-06-25, the user's call: "next version = this fix"). Cursor (was v0.4.1) postponed; Task 151 persona = the version after this.** The now.md-roll lineage: 105 → 106 → 167. Provenance: the v0.4.0 dogfood — a new session read a SHIPPED epic as still-pending because the injected snapshot froze; the user "we need a task for this and lane it for the next version, and do 105 with it" + "105 wasn't a real fix, just postpone the problem" (proven correct by the log). Relates D-205 (symptom) / D-206 (root cause), Task 105/106/35, `lazy-compress.mjs` `detectStaleness`, `inject-context.mjs` `latestDaySession`, `compress-session.mjs`._
  - **🔑 AUTOMATIC-PATH CRITERION (binding, D-169 — the user 2026-06-25: "is the fix automatic? user doesn't need to do anything?").** The fix self-heals with **NO user command**. **The self-heal is the DETACHED SessionStart roll** (`cmk-inject-context` fires on every SessionStart with zero user action and spawns `cmk-compress-lazy`, which drains a stale-now `now.md`) — made RELIABLE by 167.A (a dead cron can no longer suppress it). The drain is DETACHED (a real Haiku roll is 18–37 s, > the 30 s hook ceiling — see Q4), so the bloated `now.md` heals on the NEXT session start, and with 167.A it NEVER compounds again (every session start re-fires the roll). **167.C's `cmk doctor` HC-10 is a DIAGNOSTIC heads-up only** — never the repair path; the fix never depends on the user running `cmk doctor`. **Done-when (the automatic-path check, via `npm run live-verify:now-roll`):** ☑ a session with a bloated `now.md` + a dead-cron heartbeat heals by FIRING ONLY the SessionStart hook (NO `cmk compress`/`roll` run by hand — that would mask the automatic path, the DJ5/D-169 lesson); the detached child drains `now.md` + writes a fresh `today-*.md`. _(The live scenario waits for the detached child to finish before asserting — the heal is automatic, just not synchronous.)_
  - **📚 RESEARCH-BACKED APPROACH (the prior-art sweep 2026-06-25 — [research note](../docs/research/2026-06-25-cron-liveness-lazy-compaction-prior-art.md)).** Internal + external deep-research CONVERGED on one invariant (logrotate / anacron / Postgres-autovacuum / SQLite-WAL / claude-mem / Letta / mem0 all do this): **gate on "a run SUCCEEDED recently" — NEVER on "a scheduler is registered." Make lazy-on-access PRIMARY; cron is an optimization/backstop.** Our bug is the named anti-pattern *"monitoring detects presence, not absence — registration proves the job COULD run, not that it DID."* Internal finding: WE invented this bug — claude-remember (105's basis) has no sentinel gate; and the liveness pattern already exists in our `lock-discipline.mjs` (`process.kill(pid,0)`), just never applied to crons. **The audit also found 3 SIBLING bugs in the same surface (167.D/E/F below).**
  - **🧭 DESIGN RESOLVED (grilling 2026-06-25 — the marker-vs-derive pass + the EverOS/OpenWolf peer-CODE sweep + a 7-question design grilling; memory P-VaK5DNNa/P-DZDQSDQG/P-YZQD9K4U/P-9V3K7KEA/P-UPJDK2UN/P-6PGKSVT3/P-DDRMSBPC).** This is ALSO architecture-review candidate #1 (the missing deep module). **Build a `compaction-state.mjs` deep module** that owns the whole verdict:
    - **(Q1) Absorb the verdict** — the module owns `isCompactionNeeded` (replaces `detectStaleness`); callers ask ONE question. `detectStaleness` + the `cron-registered` sentinel + `cronSentinelPath` retire.
    - **(Q2) Marker-vs-derive = HYBRID** (the GNU make "Empty Target Files" rule: derive when the work's product carries the signal; stamp only "a run happened"). **DERIVE** `now`/`daily`/`weekly` from existing artifacts (`now.md` content, `recent.md` mtime, `today-*.md` dates — NO new marker, ADR-0002, keeps the current `detectStaleness` derive logic which was never broken). **STAMP** cron-liveness with ONE anacron-style `cron-heartbeat` the cron bins touch on each fire (records "a run happened"), gated on **AGE not existence** (`now − heartbeat.mtime < ~2× cron interval`). _(Validated by OpenWolf's `last_heartbeat`-by-age + EverOS's in-process APScheduler — both schedule reliably only because they have an always-on process the kit lacks → the kit MUST derive + stamp-per-fire.)_
    - **(Q3) Interface = TWO methods.** `isCompactionNeeded({projectRoot, now, ...ttls})` returns a RICH object `{verdict, cronStale, heartbeatAge}` (the lazy roll reads `.verdict`; the dev/doctor surface reads `.cronStale`/`.heartbeatAge`) + `recordCronHeartbeat({projectRoot, now})` (the ONLY writer, cron bins call on each fire). **No standalone `isCronAlive`** — cron-liveness is computed ONCE inside `isCompactionNeeded` and exposed via the return, so there's exactly one source of truth and nothing drifts (a 3rd predicate = a 2nd place the rule is read = the exact "two sources disagree" bug class 167 fixes).
    - **(Q4) "We're in the memory business" — correctness > startup speed (P-9V3K7KEA, binding PRINCIPLE; MECHANISM revised by the live test 2026-06-26).** ~~When `now.md` has un-rolled prior-session content AND the cron looks dead → drain SYNCHRONOUSLY before injecting so THIS session reads clean~~ **SUPERSEDED — the live test (real `claude --print`) proved a synchronous SessionStart drain is INFEASIBLE:** a real now→today Haiku roll takes **18–37 s**, but the SessionStart hook ceiling is **30 s**, so the sync drain reliably TIMED OUT and fell back to the detached path anyway (live `lazy-compress.log`: `sync-drain timed-out` then the detached `compress-session success`). **The research confirms the correction:** claude-mem/mem0/Letta compact synchronously at session **END** (the Stop hook, no user waiting), NOT session start — the kit already has that (the SessionEnd `compress-session` hook). **So the now→today roll stays on the DETACHED SessionStart path + the SessionEnd hook; the real fix is 167.A (the cron-liveness gate), which stops a dead cron from suppressing that detached roll.** The principle (correctness > speed) HOLDS — it's just achieved by the cron-fix + the detached floor (now.md heals next session and, with 167.A, NEVER compounds again), not by a blocking start. The `runSyncDrainIfNeeded` code + inject-bin wiring built on 2026-06-26 were REVERTED. _(Decision-trail: Q4's synchronous-at-start mechanism is struck above, not erased; the live-test reason + the research-backed replacement are recorded. The lazy-framing rule applied to our own grilled decision — the live test is the primary source that overturned it.)_
    - **(Q5) Cooldown.** Touch the marker on SUCCESS only (never in a catch block — a failed Haiku call must be free to retry). The stale-content SYNC-DRAIN **bypasses the cooldown** (the cooldown is a COST guard; correctness > cost — it still gates the routine OPPORTUNISTIC compress where nothing's stale).
    - **(Q6) Testing — agent-run, the user does NOTHING.** Unit tests in `npm test` (free, automatic) + a LIVE agent-loop scenario added to the EXISTING [`scripts/live-verify.mjs`](../scripts/live-verify.mjs) harness: trap state (bloated `now.md` + dead-cron heartbeat) → fire ONLY a real SessionStart → assert healed (drained + fresh `today-*.md` + clean inject) + a multi-session variant proving it heals in ONE session. **Forbidden in the live test: any `cmk compress`/`roll`/drain call** (that masks the automatic path — the DJ5/D-169 lesson; the original bug shipped green because every test ran the command first). The live test is on-demand (slow, not in `npm test`) but is REQUIRED for "task done" per the binding live-test rule. **NB (P-SW5R69QS): the user is on a Claude SUBSCRIPTION — no per-token $ cost; the only gate on the live loop is wall-clock/rate-limits, not money.**
    - **(Q7) Doctor check — KEPT as a dev/diagnostic nice-to-have (the user's call), NOT a required part of the heal.** The automatic heal fixes the real problem; HC-10 only TELLS you a cron is dead. It's worth building as a DEV aid (it helps US during kit development, like the log that diagnosed this bug) but is NOT the fix and the kit must never require it (only power users run `cmk doctor`).
    - The fix order: (c) lazy-primary + (b) heartbeat-liveness primary, (a) OS catch-up flag backstop.
  - [x] 167.A **The cron-liveness gate via an anacron-style HEARTBEAT (PRIMARY bug — `cron-active` short-circuits a dead cron).** `detectStaleness` short-circuits to `cron-active` on the mere EXISTENCE of `context/.locks/cron-registered` ([lazy-compress.mjs](../packages/cli/src/lazy-compress.mjs) L216-219), ABOVE the `stale-now` bloat check — so a registered-but-never-fired cron (live-proven: `LastRunTime` blank) disables the lazy roll forever. **Fix (the HYBRID — Q2, NOT a per-level last-success marker; that would 2nd-source the artifacts, ADR-0002):** the cron bins write ONE `cron-heartbeat` stamp on each fire (`recordCronHeartbeat`); `isCompactionNeeded` gates `cron-active` on the heartbeat being FRESH by AGE (`now − heartbeat.mtime < ~2× cron interval`), NOT the sentinel's existence. A dead/stale cron → heartbeat ages out → falls through to the derive logic + the lazy roll. The `now`/`daily`/`weekly` verdicts stay DERIVED from artifacts (`now.md`/`recent.md`/`today-*.md` — unchanged, never broken). Retire the `cron-registered` sentinel + `cronSentinelPath`. **TDD:** RED = {heartbeat stale/absent, non-empty now.md} → assert verdict is `stale-now` (rolls), not `cron-active` (skips); GREEN-path = {fresh heartbeat} → `cron-active` (skips, cron owns it). · _the single highest-leverage fix — this one gate is why now.md hit 410 KB. Part of the `compaction-state.mjs` deep module (Q1/Q3)._
  - [x] 167.D **Make lazy-on-access the PRIMARY path (research rec (c)).** Today the cron is treated as the owner and the lazy roll as a deferring fallback; every event-driven peer (claude-mem's Stop hook, Letta, mem0) does the opposite — the session lifecycle IS the trigger, so it can't be missed. **Fix:** the SessionStart lazy roll (already automatic, zero user action) is the guaranteed path; the cron is a latency optimization for the "idle for days, never opened" case, not something the lazy path ever DEFERS to. Composes with 167.A (the last-success gate makes both paths idempotent — both can fire, the second no-ops; add a lockfile for the concurrent edge). · _Depends: 167.A._
  - [x] 167.E **Set the OS scheduler's catch-up flag (research rec (a), the backstop).** The audit found `register-crons` sets NO catch-up flag on ANY platform: Windows `StartWhenAvailable` defaults FALSE (missed runs silently dropped), Unix uses vanilla cron (no catch-up; anacron/systemd-`Persistent` would), macOS launchd has no powered-off catch-up. So the asleep-laptop missed run is the DEFAULT, not an edge. **Fix:** emit `StartWhenAvailable=true` in the Windows schtasks XML; prefer systemd-`Persistent`/anacron where available on Unix; document the launchd limit. **Caveat (binding):** all catch-up mechanisms COALESCE multiple missed periods into ONE run — don't assume one-catch-up-per-missed-night. Best-effort only; the guarantee lives in 167.A/D. · _Depends: none (touches `register-crons.mjs` only); platform-commands discipline applies._
  - [x] 167.B **Bloat-resilience — defense-in-depth behind 167.A.** _Mostly SUBSUMED by 167.A + 167.F._ The original plan had (a) a `now-too-big` verdict outranking cron-active, (b) a cooldown carve-out, (c) a synchronous catch-up past a hard ceiling. **Outcome after the live test:** **(a)** turned out UNNECESSARY — 167.A already makes `stale-now` (any un-rolled content) win over a dead/stale cron, so a bloated now.md ALWAYS rolls; a separate byte-threshold verdict would be redundant (stale-now ⊇ now-too-big). **(b)** is delivered by **167.F** (the cooldown only blocks on a *successful* prior spend; a failed call no longer holds it, and the detached roll fires on the next SessionStart). **(c)** the synchronous catch-up was BUILT then REVERTED (see Q4 — infeasible under the 30 s hook ceiling; the detached roll + 167.A is the answer). So 167.B ships as "covered by A + F," no separate code. · _Depends: 167.A._
  - [x] 167.C **Observability (REQUIRED) + a `cmk doctor` HC-10 (DEV/diagnostic nice-to-have — the user's call Q7, NOT the repair path).** The self-heal (167.A/B/Q4) is the fix; this is the audit trail + an optional check. **(a) REQUIRED — the WARN log** (free, automatic, zero user surface): a WARN-level entry in `lazy-compress.log` when skipping/healing a stale-or-bloated `now.md`. This is the audit trail — exactly the log that let us diagnose THIS bug; it costs nothing and isn't redundant with the heal. **(b) NICE-TO-HAVE — `cmk doctor` HC-10** (build it as a DEV aid: it helps US during kit development surface a dead cron, and a curious power-user too): reads the SAME `isCompactionNeeded` rich return (`.cronStale`/`.heartbeatAge` — no separate liveness check, Q3) and flags a stale `today-*.md` / a dead cron / a non-draining `now.md`. Framing is informational — *"memory still self-heals automatically each session; your scheduled cleanup looks dead"* — NEVER "run X to fix" (the heal is automatic; the kit must not require a command; only power users run `cmk doctor`). **TDD:** the WARN log fires on the stale-skip path; HC-10 seeds each symptom → FAILs with the informational hint; clean state → PASS/SKIP. · _Depends: 167.A/B (reads the same verdict). Update HEALTH-CHECKS.md + design §14 + the doctor count tests for HC-10._
  - [x] 167.F **Cooldown conflates "spent budget" with "succeeded" (SIBLING bug found by the code audit).** `touchCooldownMarker` fires on BOTH success AND failure — in `compress-session.mjs` (L431 + the catch), `daily-distill.mjs` (L220/222), `weekly-curate.mjs` (L411/413), AND `auto-extract.mjs` (L868 success + L872 catch). So a FAILED Haiku call holds the 120 s cooldown fresh and blocks the next NEEDED compress; two failures back-to-back = 240 s lockout. - [ ] 174. **[D-253a trigger: the next daily-distill/cron-surface touch; OR a commits-but-no-log day observed in dogfood]** **Git-history backfill — reconstruct a working-day's session log when commits exist but no `sessions/` entry was written (idea borrowed from `awrshift/claude-memory-kit`, 2026-06-28; D-215).** **The gap:** the kit compresses `sessions/now.md` → a daily `today-{date}.md` per session (lazy roll + `daily-distill` cron). But if the Stop hook misfires, the session crashes, or the user works a whole day in another tool and only commits, **that day has commits in git but NO session log** — a silent hole in the memory timeline. The `awrshift` kit's `/close-day` detects "working-day-with-commits-but-no-log", queries git for those dates, and reconstructs the entries. We have no equivalent — `daily-distill` only compresses what's already in `now.md`; it never goes back and fills a missed day from git. **Done when:** ☐ a `cmk backfill` path (CLI verb + an automatic sweep on the `daily-distill` cron — per D-169, the automatic path is the real deliverable, the verb is the manual override) detects gaps: a date with `git log` commits but no `context/sessions/today-{date}.md` (bounded to a sensible window, e.g. last N days, not all history); ☐ for each gap it reconstructs a session entry from that day's commit messages + diffs (Haiku summarize, same compress path as the roll — ceiling-free timeout per D-179); ☐ writes the reconstructed `today-{date}.md` **marked as backfilled-from-git** (provenance: not a real captured session, so it's honest about its source); ☐ **automatic-path criterion (binding, D-169):** the backfill happens with NO user command — the `daily-distill` cron (or a SessionStart catch-up) notices the gap and fills it; `cmk backfill` is only the explicit override; ☐ idempotent (re-running never double-writes a day already backfilled or already real); ☐ never overwrites a REAL session log with a reconstruction (real > backfilled, always); ☐ a `cmk doctor` HC heads-up only (flag N recent commit-days with no log + the repair) — never the repair path. **Compose with:** `daily-distill.mjs` (the cron that gains the sweep), `compress-session.mjs` (the Haiku reconstruction), §6 rolling-window (the `today-{date}.md` shape it writes), Task 167's `compaction-state` module (don't fight the roll's verdict), the git-history read (git is already a dependency — `register-crons`/doctor shell out). · Estimate: M (a real diagnose→TDD→fix on the session-timeline; git read + reconstruction + the automatic sweep) · Depends: none (independent of 167, but should READ 167's compaction-state to avoid racing the roll) · _v0.4.x lane (within-paradigm; closes a real timeline-hole the `awrshift` kit surfaced). Provenance: the user found `awrshift/claude-memory-kit` (same repo name, different product — Python, manual `/close-day`); their git-backfill is a genuine capability we lack. D-215. Relates §6 rolling-window, Task 167 (the now.md-roll lineage), Task 35 (cron), D-169 (the automatic-path criterion — the cron sweep, not the manual verb, is the deliverable)._
