- [ ] 176. **Graph-recall research + ADR — should the kit add a relational/graph query mode alongside keyword + semantic recall? (research-then-decide, NOT commit-to-build; surfaced surveying `iwe-org/iwe`, 2026-06-28; D-216.)** **The gap this asks about:** the kit answers EVERY recall query with flat similarity — FTS5 keyword + sqlite-vec semantic (Task 65). Neither answers a RELATIONAL query: "what decisions touched the auth module?", "what facts are connected to this one?", "show the chain from this decision to the code that implemented it." `iwe` (a Rust markdown knowledge-graph/LSP, 1.2k★) makes graph traversal a first-class query mode — `$includes`/`$includedBy`/`$references`/`$referencedBy` over a header-hierarchy + link-edge graph, bounded-depth BFS, MongoDB-style frontmatter filters. It has NO auto-capture (the human authors every note), so it's a different PRODUCT — but its **graph-as-a-recall-mode** is a real idea we lack. **This is a KNOWN-but-undecided fork:** graphiti/Zep graph-memory is already in our research base (the 2026-06-06 recall deep-dive + Task 66 borrowed their bi-temporal `valid_at`/`invalid_at` model) — but we only ever mined those systems for TEMPORAL + PROMOTION lessons, NEVER asked "do we want a graph QUERY layer at all." `iwe` is the 2nd independent signal that relational recall is a distinct, valuable mode. **🟢 KEY UPDATE (2026-06-28, the user's catch — D-219): we are NOT at zero edges; we already WRITE a graph's edges, we just never TRAVERSE them.** Two edge types ship today: (a) **`links` → `related:` frontmatter / `[[cross-links]]`** — a fact can name other facts it relates to (`cmk remember --links a,b` / `mk_remember links:[...]` → `remember-core.mjs:72`, `mcp-server.mjs:642`, `write-fact.mjs:116`); (b) **`superseded_by`** — a real fact→fact foreign key in the index (`index-db.mjs:72` `REFERENCES observations(id)`). So the edges are recorded but DEAD — nothing walks them (no "show facts connected to X", no BFS, no chain query). **This NARROWS the task from "derive edges from scratch" to "ACTIVATE the edges we already have into a queryable graph layer"** — a much cheaper starting point than iwe's hand-authored-graph or a from-scratch derivation. The research question becomes: (1) activate the existing `links`/`superseded_by` edges into traversal (cheap), THEN (2) optionally DERIVE more edges (fact↔fact semantic, decision↔file refs) if traversal proves valuable. **Done when (research + decision, no production code until decided):** ☐ define the candidate query shapes a graph layer would answer that keyword+semantic CAN'T (relational/connection/chain queries — be concrete, with real examples from THIS repo's `context/` + DECISIONS.md); ☐ **survey how the graph-memory systems actually implement it — THOROUGHLY (the user 2026-06-28: "there are a lot of projects we researched that do the graph thing, we should do a more thorough research").** Our research base already names **7+ distinct graph systems** (verified: mem0 132×, graphiti 88×, zep 59×, **memos 41×**, **cognee 30×**, memoryos 19×, neo4j 10×, langgraph) across ~20 notes — Task 176 must CLONE + read the ACTUAL CODE of each relevant one (NOT the note-summaries — the Task 149 discipline), covering: **graphiti/Zep** (entity-edge triples + bi-temporal), **`iwe`** (link-edge BFS over markdown), **mem0** (its graph store — `mem0/memory/graph_memory.py`), **cognee** (the 30-mention system we've cited but never deep-read — ECL pipeline + graph DB), **MemOS/memos** (the 41-mention system), **memoryos**. For each: node/edge model, how edges are CREATED (LLM-extracted entities? hand-authored links? structural?), the query surface (Cypher? BFS? hybrid?), and crucially whether edges are DERIVED or hand-authored. **Output a dedicated graph-memory research note** (like the 2026-06-06 recall deep-dive) that feeds this ADR — the thorough cross-project read happens WHEN this task is worked, the scope is locked HERE so it isn't thin. **➕ ADD `juanceresa/sift-kg` to the read-list (deep-read 2026-06-29; D-225) — the cleanest EDGE-DERIVATION reference (MIT, 653★, real code in `src/sift_kg/`).** It answers the "how do you derive edges from unstructured text" question concretely: a SINGLE combined LLM prompt per chunk (`extract/prompts.py::build_combined_prompt` — "STEP 1 extract entities using ONLY these types, STEP 2 find relations using ONLY these relation types + **direction constraints** `source_type → target_type`"), with THREE schema modes — the smart one is **schema-free DISCOVER-THEN-FREEZE** (`domains/discovery.py`: the LLM samples the corpus, DESIGNS an entity/relation schema, saves it to `discovered_domain.yaml`, then extracts consistently against that frozen schema — avoids the "every run invents different relation types" drift, the exact hazard an auto-derived graph faces). Its other gem = a **3-layer entity-resolution ladder** (`graph/prededup.py` deterministic Unicode/title-strip/SemHash-fuzzy → LLM-proposed-merge-with-confidence → human-approve), with proposal explicitly separated from decision — CONVERGENCE-CONFIRMATION of our own conflict-queue posture (propose-don't-silently-merge), and a clean reference for the dedup ladder (cheap→LLM→decide). **The catch:** sift-kg builds from hand-fed DOCUMENT corpora (not auto-captured conversation), recall is purely STRUCTURAL (traversal + browser UI, no vector hybrid), and its merge step is human-in-the-loop (against our D-169 — we'd keep auto-with-revert). So it's the EDGE-CONSTRUCTION reference, NOT the graph-recall-query reference. _The schema-free-discover-then-freeze + the dedup-ladder are the two patterns to revisit at build time; D-225._ **➕ ADD Memora (Microsoft, ICML 2026) to the read-list — the strongest ONTOLOGY-FREE implicit-graph reference (read 2026-07-03, paper + code; [research note](../docs/research/2026-07-03-memora-harmonic-memory-review.md); clone at `C:/Projects/Memora`).** Its **cue anchors** (1–3 per memory, 2–4 words, `[Main Entity]+[Key Aspect]`; the CODE's taxonomy includes RELATIONAL causal/intentional cues — `core/cue_index_generator.py`) are LLM-derived per memory at capture, embedded, many-to-many, **auto-pruned when orphaned** — shared cues form the graph with NO schema and NO explicit edge construction (vs graphiti/Zep's typed edges, vs sift-kg's discovered schema). Retrieval traverses via a **frontier** (linked memories) + a "relaxed frontier" through *similar* cues (θ=0.85, top-4 — `core/memory_expander.py`), and their ablation shows the multi-hop gains live ENTIRELY in this traversal (the policy retriever's advantage disappears without cues). **The formal case:** their mixed-key theorem (App. D.5 — jointly enforcing "abstraction scope ∩ cue selection" is provably inexpressible for flat top-k AND fixed-attachment KG) is the theory for why cues beat both our flat hybrid and a rigid graph. For the kit: a `cues:` frontmatter list (markdown-native, committed) embedded beside the title is the candidate shape — this is the concrete mechanism 176's "activate the edges we already have" step 2 (DERIVE more edges) should evaluate FIRST.
  - **➕ ADD `synpulse8-opensource/pulse8-ai-cortex-knowledge-vault` to the read-list (deep-read 2026-06-29; D-227) — the closest GIT-NATIVE MARKDOWN typed-graph reference (Apache-2.0, real Python, MCP-first).** This is the nearest architectural sibling to our graph-recall idea: a markdown knowledge OS with a **typed knowledge graph (NetworkX) + AUTOMATIC EDGE MAINTENANCE on file changes** — wikilinks + tags + custom edges kept in sync as the markdown changes, queried via a `vault_context` tool that builds a RANKED SUBGRAPH, plus QMD hybrid (BM25+vector+rerank). **Why it's the priority read for THIS task:** it does the exact thing our KEY UPDATE above describes — DERIVE/maintain edges from the markdown you already write, auto, rebuildable — over `[[wikilink]]` + tags (the edges we already record but don't traverse). So it's the reference for BOTH halves: activating our existing `links` edges (its wikilink-graph) AND the `vault_context` ranked-subgraph IS the "relational query keyword+semantic can't do." Apache-2.0 + real code = readable. The catch: it's a different PRODUCT (drop-files-in knowledge vault, semi-manual ingest) not auto-captured conversation memory — but the edge-maintenance + ranked-subgraph mechanisms are exactly on-target. _Add to the clone+read set alongside cognee/sift-kg; D-227._
  - **📚 THE "NEXT-GEN RAG" TAXONOMY + RAPTOR (MachineLearningMastery, 2026-06-29; D-226).** The "beyond vector search" survey names 5 strategies, and 4 ARE our research tasks — useful confirmation the kit's research lanes track the field: **GraphRAG** (= this task, graph traversal + "community summaries at levels of abstraction" via the **Leiden clustering algorithm** → multi-hop reasoning vs isolated-chunk similarity), **Agentic RAG** (= Task 149 WHEN-to-recall), **HyDE** (= the query-expansion note on Task 178), **ColBERT** (late-interaction/MaxSim — incremental, noted not pursued). **The ONE genuinely-new idea = RAPTOR (Hierarchical Tree-Structured Retrieval):** recursively cluster chunks → summarize each cluster → cluster the SUMMARIES → summarize again → … building a tree of increasing abstraction, then retrieve across levels. For us this is adjacent to BOTH a graph layer (176) AND the re-curation pass (Task 95) — a memory hierarchy where high-level summaries sit above atomic facts, recall pulls the right ALTITUDE. Worth evaluating at 176/95 build time: does a RAPTOR-style summary-tree over our facts beat flat semantic recall for "big picture" queries? **Cognee** (the graph framework we've cited 30× but never deep-read — already on this task's read-list) is independently flagged by the 6-frameworks article as "the lesser-known one worth studying" + the one closest to graph-native reasoning — reinforces it's the priority clone for 176's deep-read. _Relates D-226, Task 95 (RAPTOR ≈ a summary-hierarchy over the re-curated facts), the Leiden/GraphRAG community-summary mechanism, Cognee (the read-list priority)._ ☐ assess the FIT against our markdown-as-truth + rebuildable-SQLite model — could edges be DERIVED (fact↔fact links, decision↔file refs, `[[wikilink]]`-style) from the markdown we already write, rebuildable like the FTS5/vec index, NOT a hand-authored graph (the `iwe` model presupposes human-authored links we DON'T have — auto-capture means our users never build a note web by hand, so any graph must be AUTO-DERIVED or it's dead weight); ☐ a cost/benefit call vs the alternatives (does semantic recall already cover most relational intent? is the win worth a 3rd index + the derive-edges complexity?); ☐ output a **graph-recall ADR**: ADOPT (with the derive-edges design + a version lane) / DEFER (with the trigger that would revive it) / REJECT (with why semantic+keyword suffices). **Compose with:** Task 149 (the recall-trigger study — 149 asks WHEN to recall, this asks WHAT recall MODES; complementary, run them together in the v0.4 recall lane), Task 65 (the semantic layer a graph mode would sit beside), Task 66 (temporal-validity, already borrowed from the same graph systems), §9.3.1 the backend seam, the markdown-as-truth + rebuildable-index invariant (the hard constraint: edges must be derivable, not hand-authored). · Estimate: M (research + ADR; no production code in this task — an ADOPT verdict spawns a SEPARATE build task with its own lane) · Depends: none (research-only; reads Task 65's vec layer + Task 149's repo clones) · _v0.4 recall lane (research input, like Task 149 — pairs with it). Provenance: the user surveying `iwe-org/iwe` ("maybe it's a good fit to add graph recall") + confirming no existing task asks the graph-query-mode question (the temporal/promotion borrows from graphiti/Zep did NOT cover it). D-216. Relates Task 149 (WHEN-to-recall sibling), Task 65 (semantic), Task 66 (bi-temporal borrow), the 2026-06-06 graphiti/mem0/memoryos deep-dive, the markdown-native + derive-don't-hand-author constraint._

- [ ] 177. **Correction-trained behavior-doc research + ADR — can accumulated corrections TRAIN a durable instruction/behavior doc (not just store facts)? (research-then-decide; surfaced surveying `rohitg00/pro-workflow`, 2026-06-28; D-217.)** **The idea:** `pro-workflow` (a direct-competitor CC memory kit, npm, FTS5+SQLite) has a buried gem its README never mentions — a **DSPy-style offline skill optimizer** (`src/optimizer/`): it treats `SKILL.md` as trainable text-space state, uses past corrections as **training trajectories**, holds out 20% as a **validation set**, and runs Reflect→Aggregate→Clip→Apply→Evaluate (LLM-graded against the holdout, accept only if the score improves, budget-capped, periodic "slow" consolidation rewrite). The OUTPUT is an auto-improved instruction document. **Why it's interesting for US:** the kit currently remembers *facts* (and promotes durable ones to the persona — Task 151); it does NOT *train the behavior doc* from corrections. This is a sharper, mechanized version of what **Task 55** (behavioral pattern detection — "learn how I work") and **Task 151** (recurrence-scored promotion) gesture at: a correction isn't just a fact to store, it's a signal that could UPDATE a durable rule, **validated against held-out corrections** so the update is measured, not vibed. **Done when (research + decision, NO production code until decided):** ☐ characterize precisely what a "trainable doc" would be in OUR model — the persona scratchpads? a CLAUDE-rules-style behavior file? the skill docs? (be concrete: what doc, whose corrections, what's the validation signal); ☐ read the real `pro-workflow/src/optimizer/` loop + the DSPy/ReflACT prior art it's based on (CLONE + read, the Task 149 discipline); ☐ assess FIT against our markdown-as-truth + post-hoc-reversible (`cmk forget`) model — does an LLM-graded accept/reject gate cohere with the kit's "no human-in-the-loop ritual" (D-169) and "auto-judge, post-hoc revert" (D-154) postures, or does the validation-set gate re-introduce a heavyweight offline pass we don't want?; ☐ the hard honesty check — is this REAL leverage or a sophisticated solution to a problem semantic recall + recurrence-promotion already cover? (the adoption-evidence rule: concrete counterfactual, not "it felt powerful"); ☐ output an ADR: ADOPT (with the trainable-doc design + a version lane + how it composes with 55/151) / DEFER (with the revive trigger) / REJECT (with why fact-storage + recurrence-promotion suffices). **Compose with:** Task 55 (behavioral pattern detection — the closest sibling; this might BE its mechanism), Task 151 (recurrence-scored promotion — a correction-trained rule is a promotion target), Task 97 (dynamic trust — the validation score is a trust signal), D-169 (no manual ritual — the gate on whether an offline training pass fits), D-154 (auto-judge + post-hoc revert — the posture the gate must cohere with), the adoption-evidence discipline. · Estimate: M (research + ADR; an ADOPT verdict spawns a separate build task) · Depends: none (research-only; reads Task 55/151's design + the pro-workflow optimizer) · _v0.4 curation lane (research input, pairs with Task 55/151). Provenance: surveying `pro-workflow` — its skill-optimizer is the one mechanism we genuinely lack (we're ahead on the core memory loop: it LOGS learnings to stderr, never injects them into context — the README's "auto-loaded" is terminal-only; ours injects the frozen snapshot). The optimizer trains the BEHAVIOR doc, a bet we don't make. The user: "add research task." D-217. Relates Task 55 (behavioral patterns), Task 151 (promotion), Task 97 (dynamic trust), the read-past-the-README discipline, the adoption-evidence rule._
  - **🔑 KEY UNBLOCK — the "outcome signal WITHOUT a user ritual" gap (the open hard part of this task AND Task 97) has a working answer: memclaw's 6 PASSIVE signals (deep-read 2026-06-29; D-223).** Both 177 (train-the-doc) and 97 (dynamic trust) kept hitting the same wall: an LLM-graded / outcome-scored update needs a SUCCESS/FAILURE signal, but asking the user for it violates D-169 (no ritual) — and pro-workflow's DSPy optimizer + caura's `report_outcome` both ASSUME an explicit signal we don't want. **caura-memclaw's Forge cracks it: infer outcome PASSIVELY from signals the kit ALREADY produces** (`session_trace.py`): (1) **contradiction-detected** soon after a recall → that memory was wrong; (2) **fact superseded** (`superseded_by`) → the old one failed; (3) **repeat-recall** of the same query → the first answer didn't land; (4) **terminal-memory classification** — an LLM labels the last memory of a session "shipped/fixed" vs "blocked/abandoned"; (5) **cross-session reuse** — a fact recalled across many sessions with healthy outcomes is load-bearing; (6) optional **git-commit/CI** tied to the session. **We already PRODUCE signals 1, 2, and 5** (contradiction-queue, supersede links, the index's access tracking) — so a passive outcome estimate is reachable WITHOUT a prompt. This is the D-169-compatible "did the correction/rule actually help?" measure that makes a validated training loop (177) or an evolving-trust score (97) buildable instead of stuck. **Revisit at build time** — design the passive-signal estimator as the validation signal for 177's accept/reject gate AND 97's confidence delta; it's the same primitive both need. _Relates Task 97 (the SAME unblock — passive signal = the confidence delta), Task 180 (Forge, where this lives), D-223, D-169 (why passive-not-prompted matters)._

- [ ] 178. **[D-253a trigger: run WITH 149+176 at the next recall-surface minor — the recall-research trio]** **Hybrid-search tuning research — evaluate Reciprocal Rank Fusion (+ other fusion/ranking methods) against the kit's hybrid recall, on the Task 99 benchmark (research-then-decide; surfaced surveying `rohitg00/pro-workflow`, 2026-06-28; D-217/D-219).** **The idea:** our hybrid recall (Task 65, shipped v0.3.0) merges FTS5 keyword + sqlite-vec semantic with our own fusion. `pro-workflow` uses **Reciprocal Rank Fusion** (`reciprocalRankFusion()`, k=60 — `1/(k+rank)` summed across the BM25 + vector result lists) which MAY rank better than our current merge. Filed as a task (not just a logged note) so it doesn't get lost — the user 2026-06-28: *"we should make it a task so it won't get lost."* **Done when (research + measure, no production change until numbers justify it):** ☐ read the real `pro-workflow/src/search/fts.ts` `reciprocalRankFusion` + survey other fusion methods (RRF, weighted-sum, learned re-rank, the cross-encoder rerank MemPalace/Graphiti use) — CLONE + read, the Task 149 discipline; ☐ characterize how OUR hybrid fuses today (read `search.mjs` / `semantic-backend.mjs` — quote the actual merge) and where RRF would differ; ☐ **measure RRF vs current on the Task 99 LongMemEval-style benchmark** (R@k / paraphrase set — the SAME harness that decided Task 65, so the comparison is apples-to-apples; numbers decide, not vibes — D-109 bake-off discipline); ☐ output: ADOPT RRF (with the one-line swap + the benchmark delta) / KEEP-CURRENT (with the numbers showing ours wins or ties) / DEFER. **Compose with:** Task 65 (the shipped hybrid this tunes), Task 99 (the benchmark harness — the decision gate), §9.3.1 the backend seam. **➕ ADD a second experiment to the same bench run (Memora, 2026-07-03; [research note](../docs/research/2026-07-03-memora-harmonic-memory-review.md)): title(abstraction)-only vs content embedding.** Memora embeds ONLY the ~6–8-word abstraction (never the value) and credits this for avoiding embedding fuzziness; their biggest ablation jump (0.653→0.795) is this layer. For us: embed fact TITLE (+ optional cues) instead of / alongside content, measure R@k + the paraphrase set on the Task-99 harness. **Calibrated expectation (App. E case-study read):** our rich facts already avoid the Mem0 fragmentation extreme their ablation punishes, and our content-embedding W2 paraphrase recall is 1.000 — expect smaller gains; the numbers decide (D-109), same harness, same run as the RRF experiment. · Estimate: S–M (research + a benchmark run; the change itself, IF adopted, is small) · Depends: none (Task 65 + 99 shipped) · _v0.4 recall lane (research input; pairs with 149/176). An ADOPT verdict is a small swap — could ride a recall-tuning patch. Provenance: `pro-workflow`'s RRF (D-217) + the user's "make it a task so it won't get lost." D-219. Relates Task 65 (hybrid), Task 99 (benchmark gate), Task 149/176 (recall-lane siblings), the numbers-decide bake-off discipline._
  - **🔬 REVISIT-WHEN-BUILDING — a THIRD fusion method to benchmark (captain-claw deep-read 2026-06-28; D-221).** Beyond RRF (pro-workflow) and ours, `kstevica/captain-claw` (MIT) fuses by **weighted average — `score = 0.65·vector + 0.35·keyword`** (`semantic_memory.py::_merge_hybrid`, treating the embedding as 65% reliable) **PLUS an exponential temporal decay** (`score *= exp(-ln2/21d · age)` — 21-day half-life, so a 21-day-old hit is worth half). So when 178 benchmarks fusion methods on the Task 99 harness, the candidate set is **3+: weighted-average (captain-claw) vs RRF (pro-workflow) vs our current vs a cross-encoder rerank**. The temporal-decay-on-the-score idea is also worth a separate test — it's recency-bias baked into ranking, which composes with (or competes with) Task 66's validity windows. _Relates D-221, Task 66 (temporal — the decay-on-score vs validity-window overlap)._
  - **📚 SEARCH-SCIENCE PRIOR — the fusion comparison has a known WHY, not just "try all and see" (Elastic hybrid-search explainer, 2026-06-29; D-225).** Elastic (who popularized RRF in their engine) frames the two fusion FAMILIES + the science: **RRF** (rank-based, `score = Σ 1/(k + rank_i)` across retrievers; `k` adjusts how much low-ranked docs count) vs **linear/weighted combination** (raw scores merged — what captain-claw does). **The KEY prior for our benchmark:** BM25 scores are UNBOUNDED while cosine is a FIXED range — so a naive weighted-sum (captain-claw's `0.65·vector + 0.35·keyword`) **biases toward whichever retriever emits bigger absolute numbers, independent of actual relevance**, UNLESS the scores are min-max normalized first. RRF sidesteps the scale-mismatch entirely by converting to ranks. **So 178's benchmark carries a HYPOTHESIS, not a blind sweep: RRF should beat naive weighted-average unless captain-claw's scores happen to be normalized — verify on the Task 99 harness.** Elastic's when-to-use rule: START with RRF (plug-and-play, no labeled data, only tune `k`); graduate to linear/weighted ONLY when you need to weight signals AND have data to tune on (= our current hybrid IS a weighted form, so the live question is "does switching to RRF improve recall on our corpus?"). **Gap (so we don't over-rely on Elastic):** it covers only RRF + linear — NO cross-encoder rerank (the 3rd stage MemPalace/Graphiti use, already in our candidate set above). So Elastic = the fusion-stage science; rerank stays separate. _Relates D-225, the score-scale-mismatch why (sharpens the captain-claw weighted-avg note above from "a 3rd option" to "the one RRF was designed to beat"), Task 99 (the benchmark that settles it)._
  - **🟢 PREMISE CORRECTION (2026-06-29, surfaced by this article batch — D-226): we ALREADY use RRF, so 178 is "TUNE + add adjacent techniques", not "adopt RRF".** Code-checked `semantic-backend.mjs:314` — our hybrid ALREADY fuses via **RRF** (the D-72 recipe shipped in Task 65: sqlite-vec + FTS5 `bm25()` via RRF k=60), PLUS a post-fusion rerank (keyword-overlap 0.30 + temporal 0.40, `rerankResults`). So pro-workflow's RRF is NOT a new thing to adopt — we have it. **178's real question narrows to:** (a) is our `k` tuned (60 is the standard default — probably fine); (b) do the ADJACENT techniques below (post-retrieval-filter, HyDE/query-expansion) add measurable lift on Task 99; (c) is captain-claw's weighted-average worth comparing AT ALL given RRF's score-scale advantage (Elastic's prior says probably not). This is a SMALLER task than first framed — mostly "do the recall-quality add-ons help?", not "swap the fusion." **Also worth a metadata-filter check:** our KEYWORD path already filters-before-rank (the `WHERE … AND tier/trust` is in the SQL before `ORDER BY rank LIMIT` — `search.mjs:322`), matching the "filter before scoring" best practice; VERIFY the sqlite-vec KNN path does the same (vec KNN can scan-then-filter, wasting the scan on rows a tier/trust filter will drop) — if it post-filters, pushing the predicate into the vec query is a cheap efficiency win.
  - **📚 IMPLEMENTATION SPECIFICS + 2 ADJACENT TECHNIQUES (MachineLearningMastery RAG articles, 2026-06-29; D-226).** Concrete details for when 178 builds the benchmark: (a) **`k = 60` is the standard RRF constant** ("standard academic convention" — our earlier note said "tune k" without the default; 60 is the start point). (b) **Retrieve ALL docs from BOTH engines before applying RRF, NOT top-k from each** — otherwise "truncation bias favors whichever ranker runs first" (`top_k=len(documents)` then fuse). (c) **POST-RETRIEVAL FILTERING — a technique our pipeline lacks:** after fusion, SCORE the retrieved candidates against the IMMEDIATE task/query and DROP low scorers BEFORE injecting ("significantly improves output quality"). We currently retrieve-and-inject; a re-score-against-the-live-query gate is cheap and adjacent to a rerank stage. (d) **QUERY EXPANSION / HyDE** — generate a hypothetical answer, embed THAT, search with it; bridges the gap between how the user ASKS and how the fact was STORED. Directly relevant to our paraphrase-recall (Task 65/99 already measures a paraphrase set — HyDE is a candidate lever to raise it). The "Lost in the Middle" finding (attention prioritizes the START + END of context, neglects the middle) is the ranking-order reason post-fusion ordering matters. _Relates D-226, Task 99 (paraphrase benchmark — where HyDE + post-filter would show), Task 149 (post-retrieval-filter ≈ a recall-quality gate), the captain-claw/Elastic fusion notes above._

- [~] 179. **RESOLVED at the Task-185 sweep — the research it asked for HAPPENED and produced ADR-0017 (Accepted 2026-07-02, D-252): the kit's ONE loop is the learn-loop in [SYSTEM-MAP §6](../docs/SYSTEM-MAP.md), built as Tasks 190–194 (Phase 1–2).** 179's umbrella question ("should the kit have ONE recurring loop that makes memory better, and how do 95/55/177 relate?") is answered: YES, and the relations are drawn in the map — 95 (re-curation) consumes the loop's utility data (sequenced after 66 + Phase 1), 55's error→fix shape ships via 194's anti-pattern conversion + 191's judgment files, 177 stays its own GO/NO-GO (see its refreshed trigger). No separate "memory-loop" task needed — the umbrella closed into the ADR. _(D-253; original entry preserved below per the decision-trail rule.)_ **Memory-improvement loop — the umbrella research/ADR: should the kit have ONE recurring background loop that makes memory BETTER (re-curate + surface insight + curate the skill library + improve the behavior doc), and how do the existing pieces (95/55/177) relate to it? (research-then-decide; the user's idea 2026-06-28, grounded in Hermes + letta + Dreams; D-219.)** **The user's thought:** *"a 'memory-loop' feature to make skills/make the memory files better, maybe insight — I think we saw some projects that do something like that."* Correct — and the cross-project read (2026-06-28) shows the field does memory-improvement in distinct flavors. For the KIT, three apply (a fourth — skill-library curation — does NOT, see the honest findings below), which is exactly why we need ONE framing decision rather than disconnected tasks:
  - **(A) Re-curate FACTS** — merge dups, resolve contradictions, drop stale. Prior art: **mem0** (`DEFAULT_UPDATE_MEMORY_PROMPT` ADD/UPDATE/DELETE/NONE per fact), **letta** (`rethink_memory` whole-block rewrite, sleeptime agent), **Anthropic Dreams**. ↔ already **Task 95** (needs-design, after 66).
  - **(B) Generate INSIGHT** — spot cross-session patterns, surface NEW derived knowledge that was never explicitly stored. Prior art: **Anthropic Dreams** (the real version), letta sleeptime (partial). ↔ gestured at in Task 95 ("surface new cross-session insights") + **Task 55** (behavioral patterns) but never a first-class deliverable.
  - **(C) Train the BEHAVIOR/PERSONA from corrections** — corrections → improved instruction doc / persona, validated. Prior art: **pro-workflow optimizer** (DSPy-style), Hermes `darwinian-evolver` (user-triggered genetic search — NOT an auto loop). ↔ already **Task 177** (train-the-doc) + **Task 151** (persona promotion). For US the "doc" is the PERSONA (HABITS / working-style), NOT a skill — we have only 2 fixed scaffolded skills (memory-write/search), nothing to curate.
  - **🔑 TWO HONEST FINDINGS (so we don't mis-borrow):** (1) Hermes's "insights" are PURE STATISTICS (token/session/cost counts, no LLM, no pattern discovery) — NOT flavor B; and its curator never feeds back into the agent's prompt (no closed learning loop). Hermes's real loop is **SKILL-LIBRARY curation** (archive stale + merge overlapping skills into umbrellas) — **which does NOT apply to the kit: we have no user-accumulated skill library to curate** (our 2 skills are fixed infrastructure). So the "memory learns and improves itself" framing is **Anthropic Dreams + letta sleeptime**, not Hermes; and the skill-curation angle is dropped from this loop (the user's catch 2026-06-28: *"what skill are we improving? we only have memory-write/search"* — correct). (2) The DISTINCT idea "synthesize a NEW skill FROM the user's memory/persona" is NOT part of this loop either — it's exploratory and filed separately as **Task 180** (memory→skill synthesis), not folded here.
  - **🔬 REVISIT-WHEN-BUILDING — captain-claw is the READABLE reference for the insight/"dream" loop (deep-read 2026-06-28; D-221).** `kstevica/captain-claw` (MIT, in-repo, 5,337 LOC memory layer) implements EXACTLY this loop's insight half — and unlike Anthropic Dreams (closed product) we can read it. Its `nervous_system.py` is a literal "dream" pass: every 12 messages (300s cooldown, + optional idle-dreaming), an LLM reads ACROSS all memory layers + recent messages + open contradictions and synthesizes ≤3 **intuitions** (typed: `connection`/`pattern`/`hypothesis`/`association`/`unresolved`), FTS5-deduped at insert, injected back into context ranked by `confidence × importance` + recency. **Steal-list when 179 is built:** (a) the `dreaming_system_prompt.md` shape (find non-obvious connections + recurring patterns + hypotheses across layers — a ready template for our insight pass); (b) the **maturation pipeline** (`raw`→`maturing`→`mature` over N dream cycles before an intuition surfaces in context — a built-in "don't inject half-baked insights" gate); (c) `source_ids`/`source_layers` provenance on each intuition (cite what it was derived from — fits our citation discipline). **The HONEST weakness to AVOID copying:** maturation is pure TIME-gating, not evidence — a wrong intuition "matures" if it survives N cycles uncontradicted (the kit should gate on evidence, not cycles). **Revisit at build time** to see how the dream-pass symbiotes with OUR markdown-as-truth + rebuildable-index model (their intuitions live in SQLite; ours would need to be markdown facts the index rebuilds from, OR a derived index-only layer). _Relates Task 97 (their confidence/decay = the trust reference), Task 66 (their `unresolved` tension-holding = a 66 revisit note), D-221._
  - **Done when (research + ADR, NO production code until decided):** ☐ decide: is this ONE unified background "memory-dreams" loop, or do A/B/C stay separate features? (the architecture fork); ☐ if unified, define the single recurring pass (input → re-curate facts + surface insight + improve persona → reviewable output); ☐ resolve the two forks Task 95 already names (review-gate vs auto-apply-revertible per D-169; raw-transcript privacy — gitignored, sanitized output only); ☐ output an ADR mapping 95/55/177/151 onto the chosen architecture, each with a lane. **Compose with:** Task 95 (re-curate facts, flavor A — likely the engine the loop runs), Task 55 (patterns/insight, flavor B), Task 177 (train-the-persona-doc, flavor C), Task 151 (persona promotion — the loop's persona output), Task 66 (the validity engine 95 consumes), Task 180 (the adjacent memory→skill-synthesis idea, kept separate), D-169 (no-ritual — the loop must be automatic), D-154 (auto-judge + post-hoc revert). · Estimate: M (research + ADR; the umbrella that sequences 95/55/177/151) · Depends: none (research-only; reads letta sleeptime / mem0 / Anthropic Dreams + our 95/55/177 designs) · _v0.4 curation lane (the umbrella over 95/55/177 — run it FIRST in the lane so it frames the others). - [ ] 180. **Memory → skill SYNTHESIS — generate a bespoke skill FROM the user's accumulated memory/persona, + a possible improve-loop (EXPLORATORY — research whether it's even worth it; the user's idea 2026-06-28, flagged "maybe going too far"; D-219).** **The idea (the user, verbatim):** *"we can create a skill based on how the user works and his instructions and memories, and create a skill based on it, and then a loop that improves that skill… I don't know if we are ready for this, maybe I'm going too far… maybe this is a different task at all."* So: take the captured persona (HABITS / working-style / LESSONS) + project conventions + decisions, and SYNTHESIZE a custom Claude Code skill (e.g. a generated `the-way-I-build-backends` skill) that encodes the user's way of working — then optionally a loop that refines that generated skill as memory grows. **Why it's DISTINCT from everything else (so it's not muddled again):** the kit's persona work (Task 151) INJECTS facts into context (a snapshot); this would EMIT an ARTIFACT — a `.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` the agent loads on-demand. Different output, different surface. It is NOT Task 179's loop (that improves MEMORY + persona-facts), NOT Task 177 (that trains an existing behavior doc), NOT Hermes skill-curation (we have no skill library to prune). It's "memory as the INPUT to author a new skill." **⚠️ EXPLORATORY — the honest flags (this task's FIRST job is to decide if it's worth doing AT ALL):** ☐ is there a real user need, or is the injected persona already sufficient (a generated skill may just duplicate what the snapshot already carries)? ☐ does a generated skill compose with Claude Code's skill model (auto-invoke `description`, `allowed-tools`) without becoming noise/another thing to maintain? ☐ does it violate D-169 (a skill the user must manage) or the kit's "memory just works, you don't curate it" thesis? ☐ the improve-loop adds the pro-workflow/DSPy validation question (Task 177's territory) — does it collapse INTO 177, or is generating-from-scratch genuinely different from training-an-existing-doc? ☐ prior art to read at task-time: pro-workflow's optimizer (trainable SKILL.md), the gstack/gskill skill-layer notes (2026-05-30), Anthropic's skills doc, any project that GENERATES skills from usage. **Done when:** a short research note + a GO/NO-GO call (is this worth a build task, or does the persona/177 already cover the need?) — NOT a commitment to build.   - **🔬 PRIMARY-SOURCE REFERENCE — caura-memclaw's "Forge / Skill Factory" is a WORKING memory→skill-synthesis pipeline (deep-read 2026-06-29; D-223). UPGRADES this task from "maybe too far / no prior art" to "exploratory but with a proven reference design."** memclaw (Apache-2.0) BUILT exactly this (it was vaporware at our 2026-06-12 README review; now production code: `core_api/services/forge/forge_service.py` + `distill_prompt.py` + `fingerprint.py` + a spec/impl-plan). The real pipeline, adapted to OUR single-user + markdown model: **(1) build session traces** + infer outcome from **6 PASSIVE signals — NO user ritual** (contradiction-detected, fact-superseded, repeat-recall=first-answer-failed, terminal-memory-classification "shipped/fixed" vs "blocked/abandoned", cross-agent reuse, optional git-commit/CI hooks tied to session) — this is the D-169-compatible answer to "where's the success signal?"; **(2) cluster** repeated workflows (memclaw uses entity-Jaccard ≥40%; for us = recurrence across SESSIONS/PROJECTS, since we're single-user not a fleet); **(3) gate on volume + diversity** (≥N recurrences before synthesizing — don't make a skill from one-off noise; their "≥3 distinct agents" → our "≥N distinct sessions/projects"); **(4) distill via LLM** (`distill_prompt.py` is a ready template) into a candidate `SKILL.md` with PROVENANCE (`cites:[mem-ids]`, `evidence:"across 4 sessions…"`, `cluster_fingerprint`); **(5) fingerprint** (`fp:v1:sha256(goal+domain+top-entities+step-skeleton)`) + a **rejected-fingerprints cooloff table** (don't re-propose a skill the user already rejected — for us a local `.json` + 30d TTL); **(6) NEVER auto-promote** — candidates stay `candidate` until evidence gates pass (recurrence + convergence + freshness) = EARN-IT, not auto-apply (composes with 151's recurrence-scoring + D-154 post-hoc-revert). **The honest catch:** memclaw is Postgres + multi-tenant + FLEET (its diversity gate is "across agents" — meaningless for one user); we adapt the SHAPE (passive-signal outcomes, fingerprint-dedup, earn-it gates, recurrence-across-sessions), NOT the server machinery. **This makes 180's GO/NO-GO sharper:** the question is no longer "is memory→skill even possible?" (memclaw proved it) but "does a single user generate enough recurrence to clear the earn-it gate, or does the injected persona already cover it?" _Relates Task 97/177 (the passive-outcome-signal gem cracks their open "signal without ritual" gap too), Task 95 (the fingerprint-dedup-rejected pattern), Task 151 (earn-it = recurrence-scoring), D-223._

- [x] 181. **RESOLVED at the Task-185 sweep — the research happened via the 2026-07-01 arc and each option got its verdict (D-253):** **(a) behavioral-adherence counting → REJECTED** (behavioral inference stays out; the comparative-judgment study's self-judge-circularity finding reinforces the risk); **(b) stability-promotion → ADOPTED-as-shape** — it ships as the judgment files' confidence gate (`n_episodes` + `direction_consistent` + un-contradicted duration, Task 191), which is exactly "a rule earns its way by NOT breaking"; **(c) correction-as-signal → SHIPS in Task 192** (user-correction is a first-class judge signal); and the friction insight itself is now BINDING design law — recurrence is never read as reinforcement (ADR-0017 Decision #2). _(Original entry preserved below per the decision-trail rule.)_ **Recurrence measures FRICTION, not adherence — a silently-followed rule never promotes (RESEARCH-then-decide; the user's insight found live in the v0.4.3 cut-gate, 2026-07-01; D-246).** **The gap (the user's reasoning, verbatim shape):** *"I told you once, it's in memory, and you keep doing it every time without fail — so why would I repeat myself? The only time I repeat myself is the times you DIDN'T do it although it's in your memory. So a rule that works perfectly generates zero recurrence."* This is a real hole in Task 151's recurrence gate. `recurrence_count` bumps ONLY when the SAME canonical fact is written again (`write-fact.mjs:240`, `existingIdAtPath === id` → `bumpRecurrence`) — it counts **fact re-captures**, NOT **observed adherence in the transcript**. The kit has NO behavioral-pattern detector (verified 2026-07-01: the only bump site is the duplicate-write branch; auto-extract dedups by content-hash, it does not count actions). **Consequence — the paradox:** recurrence effectively measures *"how often did the user have to RE-ASSERT this?"*, which correlates with **friction/failure** (the rule was ignored → the user restated it), NOT with **how well an ingrained habit is followed**. A rule stated once and honored forever stays at `recurrence_count: 1` — the BEST rule scores LOWEST. So the demonstrated-but-undeclared trait the 151 pitch promises to promote ("you keep doing X, I'll graduate it") is exactly the trait recurrence CANNOT see, because a well-followed silent rule is never re-captured. **NOT a v0.4.3 regression** — 151's declared-rule path (`via confidence-high`) fully works and shipped; this is a MISSING capability, not a broken one. The `via recurrence-N` path still fires correctly for the case it handles (a fact genuinely re-surfacing across sessions) — it just doesn't handle the "silently adhered-to" case. **⚠️ RESEARCH-then-decide — the honest options to evaluate (do NOT commit to build):** ☐ **(a) behavioral-adherence counting** — detect repeated adherence in the transcript (I ran test-first AGAIN → +1 toward "user works test-first"); powerful but RISKY (behavioral inference is exactly what the kit deliberately avoided — needs the grilling/research treatment, high false-positive surface). ☐ **(b) stability/longevity promotion** — a fact that stays high-trust + un-contradicted for N sessions promotes on STABILITY, not repetition (a good rule earns its way by NOT breaking, the inverse of the friction signal). ☐ **(c) correction-as-signal** — the user's own idea: *"if I tell you to STOP doing X, that should trigger something"* — a correction/countermand as a demote (or re-evaluate) event; and the existing friction signal (repeated restatement) is real but means "the rule is FAILING," which is arguably a DIFFERENT action (escalate/surface, not silently promote). ☐ which of these (if any) composes with 151's existing `trust_score` (Move 3) + the memclaw 6-passive-signal set (Task 180's `repeat-recall = first-answer-failed` is the SAME friction insight — they overlap)? **Done when:** a short research note + a GO/NO-GO call per option (build / defer / reject), NOT a commitment to build. Likely finding: (b) stability-promotion is the cleanest D-169-compatible fit (no behavioral inference, no ritual); (a) is a separate large design; (c) folds the friction signal into a "surface, don't promote" affordance. · Estimate: S (scoping research note + go/no-go) · Depends: none (reads 151's Move-1/Move-3 design + the memclaw passive-signal set) · _v0.4 curation lane (exploratory research; sibling to 179/180). Provenance: the user's live cut-gate insight 2026-07-01 — "silence = success, so recurrence only fires on FAILURE; the rule I state once and you follow forever never promotes." Relates Task 151 (the recurrence gate this critiques), Task 97 (dynamic-trust — stability-promotion may live here), Task 180 (memclaw's `repeat-recall=failure` is the same friction insight), Task 177 (correction-trained behavior — (c) may fold in), D-169 (the no-ritual gate any fix must pass), D-246._

- [ ] 184. **Cross-project search — `cmk search --all-projects` (promoted from a v0.1.0 deferred one-liner to a real trackable task; the v0.4.3 cold-open made the case, 2026-07-01; D-247).** **The deferral (verbatim, tasks.md v0.1.0 deferred-ideas list):** *"Cross-project search (`cmk search --all-projects`) — v0.2."* It has sat as an un-scoped bullet since v0.1.0 — now a real entry because the Session-3 cold-open showed WHY it matters. **The gap:** `cmk search` is scoped to ONE project's index (`<projectRoot>/context/.index/memory.db`). A query from project B cannot reach a fact captured in project A — even though the user often WANTS that ("how did I solve this in my other project?", "what's my standard X across everything?"). Today the ONLY cross-project channel is (1) the user-tier persona (a curated SUBSET, promoted via `cmk lessons promote`) and (2) injection of that persona at SessionStart. There is no way to SEARCH across all your projects' captured facts. **Why the cold-open makes the case:** in Session 3, the fresh project couldn't SEARCH the user's uv/ruff preferences (they lived in cut-gate19's project tier + the un-indexed persona — Task 182); a true `--all-projects` search would let a new project find a relevant fact from ANY prior project, not just the hand-promoted persona slice. **Design questions to resolve at task-time (this is DESIGN-first):** ☐ how are project index-dbs discovered/registered (a user-tier registry of known project roots? a scan? explicit `cmk project register`)? ☐ merge-search across N sqlite dbs vs. a central user-tier index that mirrors all projects (the latter re-raises the privacy + staleness questions)? ☐ how does it compose with the deferred `cmk persona sync <git-url>` (design §16, 72.2) — is cross-project search a LOCAL-only feature or does it want the synced remote? ☐ ranking across projects (recency? per-project trust? project-relevance?). ☐ privacy: a cross-project result surfaces project A's content in project B's session — is that always wanted, or opt-in per query? **Done when:** a design note (registry vs central-index, the privacy model, the ranking) + a GO/NO-GO; if GO it spawns the build task. - [ ] 186. **Consolidate the 4 doc-validators into ONE manifest-driven `validate-docs.mjs` (structural half of the D-249 "one rule to rule them all"; the user's 2026-07-01 "this is redundant, why don't we have one rule" call).** **Why:** doc-coverage was 4 overlapping `validate-*.mjs` scripts (`validate-doc-completeness` = CLI.md/MCP.md; `validate-doc-registry` = new-file registration; `validate-index-completeness` = 4 catalogs; `validate-references` = link validity) + 2 prose rules + a manual gate — **redundant where they overlapped (README/CHANGELOG governed 3×), gap-ridden where none reached (design.md/glossary/memory-lifecycle-map + ~10 living docs had NO check).** D-249 unified the JUDGMENT layer into one per-change walk over the source-of-truth table (the complete living-docs manifest). THIS task unifies the STRUCTURAL layer: one `validate-docs.mjs` driven by the **same source-of-truth table as data** (parse the manifest → per-doc: exists? links resolve? registered? catalog-listed? verb/tool-covered?). One script, one place to add a doc, no overlap. **Honest scope boundary (do NOT over-promise):** a validator can only check **existence / link / registration / verb-coverage** — it CANNOT check **content-staleness** ("is this §N current for the change" — the design.md-describes-old-behavior class). Staleness stays the per-change walk's judgment (D-249). So 186 removes the *machinery* redundancy + closes the *existence* gaps; it does not replace the walk. **Done when:** the 4 validators are one manifest-driven `validate-docs.mjs` wired into `npm test`, the source-of-truth table (or a derived `docs/manifest.json`) is the single input, and each living doc has a classification (`living` vs frozen `record`) so records are never flagged. · Estimate: M · Depends: none · _Relates D-249 (the unified rule this is the structural half of), the 4 existing `validate-*.mjs` it consolidates, the "Prose rules vs enforcement" + "Single source of truth" kernels. **Trigger (D-248): decided at the v0.4.4 cut — build when next touching the validator suite, OR sooner if doc-drift recurs after D-249's per-change walk interim.** D-249._

- [~] 188. **ABSORBED into Task 191 at the Task-185 sweep (D-253, 2026-07-02)** — the "ask the human, then remember the resolution" affordance IS the expectation-resolution mechanism: Claude's uncertainty pre-registers as an expectation (191), the user's answer/correction resolves it (192's correction signal), and the resolution lands in the judgment evidence log — no separate detection problem, the wiring already carries it. The fold the entry itself predicted ("likely FOLDS into 55 or pairs with 181(c)") landed one task over. _(Original entry preserved below per the decision-trail rule.)_ **Escalate-to-the-user, then CAPTURE the resolution — the "user as last-resort teacher" affordance (NEW near-term idea from the U-Mem harvest; the user's own framing 2026-07-01; D-251).** **The idea:** U-Mem (arXiv:2602.22406, NUS) escalates a knowledge gap through teacher→tools→human, consulting the human ONLY as a last resort. For a single-user IDE kit the full cascade is out of scope (Task 127's future), but the LAST step — *"ask the human, then remember the answer so it's never re-asked"* — is usable NOW and is squarely the kit's thesis (don't re-derive, don't re-ask). **The affordance:** when Claude is genuinely uncertain and the user resolves it (a correction, a decision, an answer to "which way do you want X?"), that resolution is the highest-value durable fact in the session — capture it as memory automatically. **Why it's DISTINCT from what exists:** auto-extract already captures user-STATED facts; this specifically targets the *uncertainty→resolution* turn (Claude asked / was wrong → the user corrected), which U-Mem's evidence (harvest #8) says is the ONLY reliable failure-lesson signal — "you can't self-diagnose without a correct reference," and the user's correction IS that reference. So it composes with Task 55 (behavioral capture) as a WEIGHTING rule: a user-correction turn is a stronger capture trigger than a restatement. **⚠️ RESEARCH-then-decide (do NOT commit to build):** ☐ can auto-extract reliably DETECT the "Claude uncertain → user resolved" turn shape (vs a normal statement)? — the detection is the crux, same risk class as Task 55's behavioral inference; ☐ does it become a SKILL (an explicit "when uncertain, ask + remember" procedure) or just an auto-extract weighting rule? ☐ does surfacing "should I remember this resolution?" violate D-169 (memory just works, no ritual) or is a silent capture cleaner? ☐ overlaps Task 181(c) "correction-as-signal" — is 188 the same idea from the capture side (181c is the trust/demote side)? likely FOLD or pair. **Done when:** a short research note + GO/NO-GO; if GO it spawns a build task (likely folded into Task 55). NOT a build commitment. · Estimate: S (scoping research note + go/no-go) · Depends: none (reads Task 55 design + the U-Mem note) · _v0.4 curation lane (exploratory; sibling to 55/181). **Trigger (D-248): triage at the Task 185 sweep — likely FOLDS into Task 55 (error→fix capture) or pairs with Task 181(c).** Provenance: the user's 2026-07-01 read of the U-Mem cascade ("an idea to add for future use… make the agent work better with the user"). Relates Task 55 (behavioral/error→fix capture — the likely home), Task 181 (correction-as-signal — the trust-side sibling), Task 127 (the FULL cascade — this is its single-user cut), the U-Mem note, D-251._

- [ ] 189. **Recurrence = memory ROI — MEASURE how much the kit's memory is actually helping, per project (NEW out-of-the-box idea from the U-Mem harvest; potential differentiator; 2026-07-01; D-251).** **The finding (U-Mem's strongest empirical result):** Pearson **r = 0.888** between task-similarity (how much a new task resembles past ones) and the performance gain memory provides — *"memory is a bet on repetition."* Memory helps most in high-recurrence domains (same codebase / conventions / problem-shape), near-zero for wildly-different one-off work. **The out-of-the-box idea:** no surveyed memory product MEASURES its own recurrence/ROI. The kit could — using the semantic backend it already ships (Task 65, sqlite-vec + embeddings) — compute a per-project "recurrence score" (how similar is this session's work to the captured history?) and (a) TELL the user how much memory is helping them ("your work is highly recurring — memory is paying off" vs "mostly novel this session — memory has less to offer"), and/or (b) ROUTE capture effort toward high-recurrence domains where it pays. This turns U-Mem's *analysis metric* into a *user-facing product feature* — a "your memory is working" signal that's honest (it can say "not much this session") and unique. **⚠️ RESEARCH-then-decide (do NOT commit to build — this needs its own design):** ☐ is a recurrence score ACTIONABLE for a single user, or just a vanity metric? (the honest risk: knowing "memory helped 12%" may not change anything the user does); ☐ can it be computed cheaply from the existing embedding index (AMCS-style average-max-cosine-similarity between new facts and the corpus) without a new pipeline? ☐ does it surface in `cmk doctor` / a `cmk stats` view, or the snapshot? ☐ does routing capture-by-recurrence conflict with "capture everything, it's cheap" (the kit's current stance)? ☐ is this a differentiator worth a lane, or a research-note curiosity? **Done when:** a research note (is the metric actionable + cheap-to-compute on our stack?) + a GO/NO-GO; if GO it spawns a design task with a version lane. NOT a build commitment. · Estimate: S (scoping research note + go/no-go; a build, if GO, is M) · Depends: Task 65 (the semantic/embedding layer any recurrence score reuses) · _v0.5+ candidate (a "measure-your-own-value" feature, past the core loop). **Trigger (D-248): triage at the Task 185 sweep; if GO, lane after Task 65's semantic layer is a stable base to build the AMCS metric on.** Provenance: the U-Mem harvest (r=0.888 recurrence↔ROI) + the user's "give us ideas out of the box." Relates Task 65 (the embedding index it reuses), U-Mem §4.4 (the AMCS metric + Fig 4), D-251._

- [ ] 190. **RECALL-LOG — record which memory IDs surfaced each turn (the learn-loop's attribution primitive; ADR-0017 Phase 1a; D-252).** The ONE genuinely new primitive in the adopted design ([SYSTEM-MAP §6](../docs/SYSTEM-MAP.md)): without "which memories were injected/searched this turn," NO outcome signal can find its target memory — every downstream organ (191/192/194) depends on it. NOT a committed tier (it's attribution plumbing, not memory). **Done when:** ☐ inject-context appends `{session, ts, source:'inject', ids:[…]}` per injection; ☐ search/mk_search append `{source:'search', query, ids}` per query; ☐ a `readRecallLog(session)` reader for 191/192; ☐ **automatic-path: entries appear with NO manual command** (hooks only); ☐ gitignored + screened (IDs only, no content); ☐ tests (five doors; over-mutation: one query appends one entry). · Estimate: S · Depends: none · _**v0.5 lane (the learn-loop differentiator, Phase 1a — build FIRST).** Relates ADR-0017 (Decision #6), SYSTEM-MAP §6, D-252. - [ ] 191. **Expectation pre-registration + `judgment_*.md` files — the earned-judgment wedge (ADR-0017 Phase 1b; D-252).** The one comparative-judgment kernel that's ready oracle-free ([study](../docs/research/2026-07-01-comparative-judgment-earned-method-preference.md)): before acting on a recalled fact/method, record a one-line EXPECTED outcome; the kit's automatic signals resolve it HIT/MISS next turn; the memory written is the PREDICTION-ERROR — an earned judgment, no oracle, no human grade. **Files:** `context/memory/judgment_<slug>.md` per the study's schema (`type: judgment`, claim vs BASELINE, `status: provisional|corroborated|contested|retracted`, `n_episodes`, `direction_consistent`, `confounds`, `decays_after`, append-only evidence log). **Honesty guards (binding, from the study):** no pre-registered expectation → no better-than claim; vague expectations don't count (must be specific+checkable); met predictions NUDGE, only misses lock; a cycle (A>B,B>C,C>A) → `contested`, surfaced to the user, never auto-picked; judgments NEVER enter ranking. **Done when:** ☐ expectation capture rides the existing Stop-hook/auto-extract path (a `PREDICTION:` candidate pattern — no new spawn); ☐ judgment file writer via `writeFact`-class safe path (Poison_Guard + dedup); ☐ resolution: next-turn signals (192) append HIT/MISS/REVERSAL to the evidence log + bump `n_episodes`; ☐ **automatic-path: a judgment is born + resolved with NO manual `cmk` command**; ☐ `decays_after` honored at inject/search read; ☐ tests incl. the cycle→contested route + over-mutation. · Estimate: M · Depends: 190 · _**v0.5 lane (Phase 1b).** Absorbs Task 188 (escalate-to-user capture — the user-correction resolution IS this mechanism) + Task 181(c) (correction-as-signal). Relates ADR-0017 (Decision #1), the judgment schema, D-252._

- [ ] 193. **FEEDBACK-SCREEN — Poison_Guard for the loop (ADR-0017 Phase 1d; a BUILD PREREQUISITE for 192/194; D-252).** Feedback is a second unscreened input channel: Poison_Guard screens WRITES; nothing screens UTILITY MUTATIONS. - [ ] 198. **Per-session temporal sweep — the contradiction-catch runs at EVERY existing Haiku maintenance site, not weekly-only (D-266; revisits D-259's site choice with new evidence — the user's "weekly is too long" catch, 2026-07-03).** The 66.4 temporal sweep judged stale-State pairs only inside `weekly-curate` — a cadence inherited from the convenient host site, never derived from a freshness requirement. The sweep's own shipped properties make higher cadence ~free: marker-incremental + `no-new-facts` returns BEFORE any LLM call (an idle session costs zero), and Memora's Appendix F shows judged consolidation stays a flat 16.5–22.2% of writes as the store grows — linear, safe ([research note](../docs/research/2026-07-03-memora-harmonic-memory-review.md)). **Build (198.1):** call `temporalSweep` from the SessionEnd handler (`compress-session` — already a Haiku cycle) and the SessionStart lazy path (`lazy-compress` — covers the new-chat-same-window case where SessionEnd never fires, the Task-105 gap); `weekly-curate` keeps it as the backstop. Best-effort (never aborts the host flow — the 66.4 posture), `userDir` via `defaultUserDir()` at the production entry points only (the D-260/D-69 rule), rides the shared cooldown cycle (`cooldownMs:0` within an already-gated cycle, §8.7.2). **Build (198.2) — Memora-style candidates:** augment/replace the FTS OR-query candidate finder with title-embedding similarity when the semantic backend is enabled (their validated θ=0.80 as the starting reference; FTS stays the always-available fallback) — sidesteps the FTS5 version-token shredding D-259 had to work around, and better pairs matter more at higher cadence. **Done when:** ☐ 198.1 the sweep fires from SessionEnd + lazy with NO manual command (the D-169 automatic-path criterion — a stale pair created mid-session is closed by the NEXT session boundary, live-tested); ☐ idle sessions provably spawn no judge call (no-new-facts short-circuit pinned); ☐ 198.2 embedding candidates behind the semantic-enabled check, FTS fallback intact, Door-3.5 prompt pins unchanged; ☐ composition: the host handlers' ceilings/cooldowns verified (the D-92/F-2 timeout-family rule); ☐ five doors + over-mutation; ☐ curate.log/compress-log NDJSON carries the per-site temporal outcome (Door 4). · Estimate: S–M · Depends: Task 66 [x] · _**v0.4.5 rider** (non-headline, rides the Cursor lane per the laned-rider convention; small, within-paradigm). Relates D-266 (the cadence re-decision), D-259 (design unchanged — judge/close semantics untouched; only sites + candidates evolve), D-166 (the acceptance window), Memora App. F (the linear-scaling evidence), Task 105 (the lazy-path coverage)._

- [ ] 199. **Write-time temporal DETECTION + in-conversation propose-and-approve resolution (design-first; the Memora-inspired durable design — D-266).** Task 198 shrinks the misleading window to a session boundary; this closes it to ZERO by catching the contradiction at the moment it is born — WITHOUT any hot-path LLM call. **The shape:** at `writeFact` time (auto-extract + `cmk remember`/`mk_remember`), a DETERMINISTIC local check (title-embedding or FTS similarity against existing live State facts — no Haiku, no latency beyond a local index query) detects a probable same-subject predecessor; instead of judging silently, the kit SURFACES it in-conversation via the result envelope (the D-215 mention posture — silent when nothing matches): *"this looks like it updates P-XYZ ('deploys to Vercel', May) — mark it superseded?"* **Claude — already in the conversation with full context — is the judge**, and the user's yes is the gate (the ADR-0018 propose-and-approve shape; strictly better than Memora's silent write-time merge, which discards the moment of change — our close keeps the trail via the 66.2 window-close). Resolution runs the existing `resolveTemporalSupersede` (event-time decides direction, LLM/user never overrides it). **Design must settle before code:** (a) which surfaces carry the mention (mk_remember envelope ✓; the CLI print for `cmk remember`; auto-extract has no conversation — its detections queue for the 198 sweep instead); (b) threshold + at-most-one-mention-per-turn noise budget (the D-169 no-ritual line — never a review queue the user must drain); (c) composition with dedup/near-dup (a detection ≠ a duplicate — dedup fires first, this fires on same-SUBJECT-different-state); (d) whether a declined proposal suppresses re-mention (a cooldown marker per pair). **Done when (design):** ☐ a short design section in design.md §16.18 extending the shipped engine, the four forks above settled; ☐ then the build as its own PR with the automatic-path criterion (the mention appears with NO manual command). · Estimate: M (design S + build S–M) · Depends: Task 198 (the sweep remains the fallback for non-conversational writes) · _**Trigger (D-248): fires when Task 198 ships AND a live session/cut-gate still surfaces a stale-State answer within the per-session window** (evidence the session-boundary cadence is insufficient), OR when the v0.5 learn-loop work touches the write path anyway (ride the surface). Relates D-266, ADR-0018 (propose-and-approve), D-215/D-169 (the mention posture), Memora §3.5/Fig-6 (the write-time precedent — adopted as DETECTION, not silent merge), 66.2 `resolveTemporalSupersede` (the resolution primitive)._

- [x] 163. **Ceiling-free compress callers used the hook-sized 50s timeout → needless `haiku_timeout`, stale `recent.md` (D-179).** _fixed 2026-06-20, branch `fix-ceiling-free-compress-timeout`._ Surfaced live (post-update `cmk doctor` HC-2: `recent.md` 4d stale; the user's "if it's not automatic, it's a bug"). **Real-data diagnosis** (not guessed): the daily-distill input is 4.7 KB yet timed out at 50s; measuring the REAL input showed `claude --print` taking 18–27s fast / **78s in a slow window** — environmental slowness (confirms D-174), and SUSTAINED, so the v0.3.4 retry (50+50, same slow window) didn't help. **Root cause:** `daily-distill`, `weekly-curate`'s curate call, and the lazy `compressSession` used `timeoutMs: 50_000` (sized for the 60s SessionEnd HOOK ceiling) despite being CEILING-FREE (cron/detached-lazy, no outer ceiling) — the D-92/F-2 rule applied to weekly-curate's PERSONA call (120s) but missed on these three. **Fix (TWO levers):** **(1) timeout** — the three → 120s; `compressSession` gains a `timeoutMs` param (default 50s = hook contract; lazy passes 120s). **(2) backoff** — the kit's retry backoff was **600ms** (the field waits 5–120 SECONDS); since D-174 slowness is a WINDOW, 600ms retries inside the same slow window → a `CEILING_FREE_BACKOFF_MS = 5_000` on the ceiling-free retrying paths so the retry lands AFTER the window; `compressSession` gains a `baseBackoffMs` param. Both extracted to named constants (`CEILING_FREE_TIMEOUT_MS` / `CEILING_FREE_BACKOFF_MS`) so the family can't drift. **The escalating-timeout idea (the user's suggestion) was REJECTED after checking 19 systems — none escalate the timeout; all use fixed-timeout + growing-backoff.** **Composition verified** (lazy child `detached`+unref'd → ~245s worst case in background after the 30s hook returns; cron standalone; SessionEnd keeps 50s + no retry). **Live-proven:** patched daily-distill ran the real input in 77.9s (died at 50s, succeeds at 120s) → `recent.md` refreshed. Full suite 2030/2030, two-pass-reviewed (skill-review added the constant-extraction + the 120s value assertions). _Secondary finding (filed, not fixed): the lazy cascade can starve daily/recent on a busy cron-less repo (`now.md` refills → verdict stays `stale-now`); designed mitigation = `cmk register-crons` (HC-5 was SKIP). Relates D-179, D-174/D-175 (retry handles a blip, the right budget handles a sustained slow window), D-92/F-2 (the rule completed across the compress family), Task 105/D-75 (the cascade-starvation secondary)._

- [ ] 149. **Recall-trigger architecture study — CLONE the real repos, don't trust the note summaries (D-153 follow-up; v0.4 recall-lane input).** The v0.3.1 cut-gate exposed that our recall is **judgment-pulled** (a `memory-search` skill the model must DECIDE to fire) — and it failed on structure/location questions until the D-153 trigger-description fix. The fix worked, but it raises the architecture question: is judgment-pulled the right model, or should recall move toward **always-search-then-answer** or **wider-inject** like other memory products? **The user's directive (2026-06-14): the research notes are second-hand SUMMARIES, not the actual implementation — CLONE the real repos and read how they actually decide WHEN to recall.** Sweep ALL researched projects (not a cherry-picked subset — the earlier mistake): graphiti, mem0, memoryos, memsearch, mempalace, claude-mem, claude-remember, basic-memory, hermes, gbrain, memory-os, simon-scrapes, openclaw, + the design-stack (cursor/kiro/chatgpt/antigravity). For each: does it have a "when to recall" decision at all, or does it always-search / inject-everything (sidestepping our problem)? Output: a recall-architecture ADR — keep judgment-pulled (+ the D-153 trigger fixes), move to always-search, or hybrid. Retrieval IS the kit's core thesis (the user: "if the search isn't working, what's the point?") — so this is a real v0.4 recall-lane decision, not cosmetic. **➕ ADD Memora to the sweep (read 2026-07-03; [research note](../docs/research/2026-07-03-memora-harmonic-memory-review.md); clone `C:/Projects/Memora`):** its **policy-guided retriever** (REFINE/EXPAND/STOP over a working-set+frontier MDP, prompted-LLM or GRPO-distilled) is the field's strongest validation that AGENTIC recall beats one-shot top-k (LoCoMo 0.863 vs 0.849 semantic; the gap is multi-hop) — i.e. our judgment-pulled `memory-search` skill ladder is the RIGHT architecture class, shipped before they named it. Two specifics for the ADR: (a) their latency honesty (3.4 steps ≈ 4.6s vs 0.23s one-shot) quantifies the agentic-recall cost we should budget; (b) their **episodic grouping at retrieval** (retrieved facts grouped by shared source episode to restore narrative coherence) is a presentation-layer idea our ladder lacks — facts return flat today; grouping by `source_file`/session could be the cheap coherence win. _Relates Task 75 (the recall ladder), D-153 (the trigger fix that surfaced it), the full-research-base + primary-source rules, the 2026-06-06 recall briefs (graphiti/mem0/memoryos + memsearch/mempalace)._
  - **📚 EXTERNAL VALIDATION — "memory as a TOOL" is a named, recognized pattern (MachineLearningMastery, 2026-06-29; D-226).** Two of the surveyed articles name the EXACT fork this task studies: **"give the agent retrieval as a TOOL it chooses to call"** (agent-controlled, targeted) **vs auto-retrieval before every turn** (pipeline, untargeted) — and frame agent-controlled as the BETTER targeting ("memory as tool" / "Agentic RAG"). This is independent confirmation that our **judgment-pulled `memory-search` skill is a recognized design, NOT a workaround** — the v0.3.1 cut-gate made it feel like a gap (the model didn't always fire it), but the field calls agent-controlled-retrieval the more targeted pattern. So 149's ADR isn't "fix a broken thing" — it's "judgment-pulled (validated pattern, + the D-153 trigger fixes) vs always-search, on the merits." **Also from the articles — a technique to fold into whichever way 149 lands: POST-RETRIEVAL FILTERING** (score candidates against the immediate task, drop low scorers before injecting — see Task 178's note) is the recall-quality gate that makes EITHER model better. _Relates D-226, Task 178 (post-retrieval-filter), the judgment-pulled-vs-always-search decision this task owns._
  - Estimate: M (research + ADR, no code until decided) · Depends: v0.3.1 cut · _v0.4 recall-lane._

## Road to 1.0 — video parity (the "worth giving to a friend" bar)

_Per D-24/D-25/D-26 (DECISION-LOG 2026-06-01). The bar for handing it to a friend = everything the Simon Scrapes video described ([source](../docs/sources/simon-scrapes-master-claude-memory.md)). Cadence: **one wow → live test → publish a version → next**; never shelve until "finished." 1.0 is a **feel** call (the user), not a date._

**Video-layer parity scorecard** (the concrete done-bar):

| Video layer | Status | Gap → task |
| --- | --- | --- |
| L1 — in-repo location (`context/`, travels with git) | ✅ built | — |
| L2 — granular per-fact archive + INDEX | ✅ built | — |
| L3 — bounded scratchpads (hot state, caps) | ✅ built | — |
| L4 — memory-aware hooks (Stop capture / SessionStart inject / auto-extract) | ✅ built | — |
| L5 — **memsearch / semantic Recall** | ⚠️ **keyword FTS5 only** | **Task 65 (the one true parity gap)** |
| L6 — cron self-curation (distill / curate) | ✅ built | — |
| Frozen-snapshot inject | ✅ built | — |
| _Beyond video — cross-project persona FILLS_ (our wedge, D-27) | ⚠️ F2-broken | **Task 64** |
| _Beyond video — temporal currency_ (facts stay true as they age) | ⚠️ not built | **Task 66** |

**Release sequence (each = build → fresh live test → publish):**

- **0.2.0** — Task 63 (F1 ✅) + Task 64 (F2) → **wow #1 cross-project cold-open**. Gated above.
- **0.3.0** — Task 65 (L5b semantic recall) → **wow #2 recall-with-reasoning** = **video parity reached**.
- **0.4.0+** — Task 66 (temporal validity) → **wow #3 currency / contradiction-catch** = past-the-video differentiator.

- [x] 66. _shipped 2026-07-02, PR #249 (v0.4.4 headline) — all four sub-tasks + the D-258/D-259 measured designs; two cut-gate live items flagged inline (66.3 auto-expiry no-invented-dates, 66.4 real-corpus weekly-curate run)._ **Temporal validity — facts stay TRUE as they age (§16.18 implementation).** Today the kit knows a fact's *age* but not its *currency*: "we use Postgres" (March) and "moved to SQLite" (May) can both sit in the archive; keyword recall may surface the stale one. Designed in [design §16.18](../specs/design.md) (from the Chandra "Beyond the Log" research note); not implemented. = **wow #3 (currency / contradiction-catch)**, beyond video parity. Post-0.3.0. **Reference model to study first (D-70, 2026-06-05):** MemPalace shipped a **SQLite entity-relationship graph with explicit validity windows** ([research note](../docs/research/2026-06-05-mempalace-review.md)) — a working precedent for our `started_at`/`ended_at`/`status` design; read theirs before building ours. **Concrete schema (D-72 source dive — [note](../docs/research/2026-06-06-recall-deep-dive-memsearch-mempalace.md)):** triple `subject→predicate→object` + `valid_from` + `valid_to` (NULL = current) + `confidence` (0–1) + `source` link back to the verbatim memory; `invalidate()` sets `valid_to`, `query_entity(as_of=date)` for point-in-time, `timeline(entity)`. Same bi-temporal pattern as Zep/Graphiti. **For us: take the model + `as_of`/`invalidate` semantics but keep it markdown-native** (validity fields in fact-file frontmatter, committed), not a separate SQLite triple store. **Graphiti/Zep is BI-temporal (D-73 dive):** two axes — `valid_at`/`invalid_at` (world truth) + `created_at`/`expired_at` (system knowledge). **We need only the TRUTH axis in frontmatter** — the system/ingestion axis we **already get for free from git history + `.locks/audit.log`**, so the bi-temporal "as-of" query falls out of (frontmatter validity) × (git/audit) with *less* to build than a triple store. Single-axis-in-frontmatter + git = our bi-temporal. **Bug 2 is a concrete acceptance case (D-166):** the SessionStart snapshot showed "v0.3.2 deferred" after v0.3.2 shipped — a Current-State fact contradicted by a later one but never superseded. 66 (validity windows: close the old `State`, open the new) + 95 (contradiction-resolve, latest-value) must make the snapshot surface the CURRENT version/lane, not the stale one. Add a test: capture "vN deferred", then "vN shipped" → recall/inject returns "shipped". Fact P-UCG4RKNL.

  - **💡 REVISIT-WHEN-BUILDING — the "tension-holding" idea (captain-claw's genuinely-novel gem; deep-read 2026-06-28; D-221).** Every system we've read (mem0, graphiti, ours) is ADDITIVE — a contradiction triggers immediate resolution (close the old window, latest-wins). `kstevica/captain-claw` (MIT) does the OPPOSITE with its `unresolved` intuition type: when its "dream" finds a genuine contradiction, it **deliberately does NOT resolve it** — it creates a first-class `unresolved` object, "holds the tension" across dream cycles (decaying at HALF speed — tensions are valuable), and only later, when new info resolves it, transforms it to a `connection` + records the lifespan + a confidence boost (`resolve_tension()`). **Why note it here (the symbiosis question to answer at build time):** 66.4 RESOLVES contradictions (the kit's default — latest-wins, close the window); captain-claw's idea is that SOME contradictions are worth HOLDING as an open question rather than auto-resolving. **The tension with OUR architecture (the honest catch — why this is a note, not a task):** a deliberately-unresolved contradiction sitting in memory cuts against the kit's "files are clean, committed truth" model + the D-169 "memory just works" thesis — an `unresolved` marker is a loose end a user might not want in their git-committed `context/`. **So: revisit when 66.4 (or 95/179) is built** — decide whether "hold the tension" fits (maybe as a `status: open-question` fact the digest surfaces, NOT a silent loose end) or whether latest-wins-resolution is right for a memory kit (vs an exploratory agent). The user 2026-06-28: *"attach it as a note so when we get there we know to revisit and see how this idea symbiotes with our kit's code + architecture."* _Relates Task 66.4 (resolve vs hold), Task 95/179 (the dream/re-curation passes that would surface tensions), D-221, D-169 (the clean-files thesis the idea must reconcile with)._
  - **🔬 PRIMARY-SOURCE GEM (graphiti deep-read, 2026-06-28; D-218).** graphiti's [`graphiti_core/utils/maintenance/edge_operations.py`](https://github.com/getzep/graphiti) `resolve_edge_contradictions()` is the textbook implementation of 66.2/66.4: on a contradicting fact it sets `invalid_at = new.valid_at` (CLOSE the old window at the moment the new one opens) + `expired_at = now()` — and **NEVER deletes** the old edge, so point-in-time `as_of` queries fall out for free. Two specifics worth stealing: (a) ONE LLM pass (`resolve_extracted_edge` → `EdgeDuplicate` with BOTH `duplicate_facts` AND `contradicted_facts`) classifies dedup + contradiction together — cheaper than two passes (we run zero today; `detectConflicts` is lexical Jaccard only); (b) validity is anchored to the **episode's `reference_time`** (LLM-extracted from the text), NOT the wall clock — so "back in 2024 we chose X" gets the right `valid_at`. mem0 is the WEAKER alternative (`_delete_memory` HARD-deletes from the live store + a side history table) — graphiti's invalidate-in-place matches our shipped DECISIONS.md annotate-never-remove posture, so it's the right template. **Detection is the unbuilt crux:** graphiti uses an LLM to decide what contradicts; our markdown-native model needs a `state_key`-match heuristic (66.2) OR a Haiku pass — so 66.1 (shape field, no-LLM) + 66.3 (expiry sweep) ship FIRST/low-risk; 66.2 + 66.4 gate on the detection design.
  - **💡 REVISIT-WHEN-BUILDING — U-Mem's advantage-based trust update (2026-07-01, [U-Mem note](../docs/research/2026-07-01-umem-autonomous-memory.md), D-251).** When 66 composes with the `trust_score` engine (151.T) to move a fact's confidence on a contradiction/supersession event, U-Mem (arXiv:2602.22406, NUS) offers a refinement to our ABSOLUTE update rule (`updateTrustScore`: fixed `+0.1`/`−0.15`). U-Mem argues absolute rewards are NOISY — they confound intrinsic task difficulty with a memory's actual efficacy (an easy task succeeds with junk memory → false-positive utility; a hard task fails with good memory → false-negative). Their fix: **advantage** = `S(with the memory) − S(without it)` — the marginal contribution, difficulty cancelled. **Why a note, not an adopted change:** computing "with vs without" needs a measurable per-outcome signal we don't have in a single-user IDE kit (no ground-truth reward per turn); our passive signals (contradiction/restatement) are already outcome-flavored proxies. So: at 66/151.T build time, evaluate whether ANY cheap advantage-proxy exists (e.g. "was the fact contradicted SHORTLY after being surfaced?" as a weak marginal signal) before assuming absolute deltas are the only option. Compose with harvest #9 (marginal-contribution self-pruning) — same underlying idea. _Relates 151.T (`trust-score.mjs` update rule), design §20.2, D-251, U-Mem SA-CTS advantage update._
  - **➡️ FOLDS IN TASK 59 (decision-contradiction reconciliation; D-218).** Task 59 ("contradiction reconciliation via temporal validity windows" — close old window / open new / link `superseded_by` / flag the reversal in the digest) is the **decision-flavored SLICE of 66's general mechanism** — the SAME graphiti `resolve_edge_contradictions` arithmetic pointed at `type:decision` facts instead of `State` facts. D-166 already settled "66 before 95"; keeping 59 separate would re-derive the window code. 59's only distinct deliverable — "flag the reversal in the decisions digest + cite the raw transcript" — lands in 66.4's contradiction-catch surface + the existing `decisions-journal.mjs`. _(Task 59's standalone entry retired into this fold 2026-06-28; if a "Claude reconciles its OWN positions" user-facing demo is ever greenlit as a Phase-3 theme, 59 re-spins as the demo surface OF 66's engine — but the engine is built once, here.)_
  - _Requirements: temporal currency (US, to add); design §16.18; research [`2026-05-24-beyond-the-log-time-aware-memory.md`](../docs/research/2026-05-24-beyond-the-log-time-aware-memory.md)._
